Conditions of Dabit (Accuracy) and Adala (Uprightness) in Narrators
Defines accuracy in hearing and retaining, and uprightness in religion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the conditions of dabit (accuracy) and adala (uprightness) for a narrator in Hanafi usul, and explain why understanding the meaning is required for hadith but not for Quran.

Core Idea
A narrator must understand the meaning of the hadith, not just memorize words, because mere sound is not proof—unlike the Quran, which is divinely preserved.

In Hanafi usul al-hadith, the reliability of a narrator depends on two key conditions: accuracy (dabit) and uprightness (adala). The text defines dabit not merely as hearing words but as understanding their intended meaning and preserving them with utmost effort. Adala is defined as steadfastness in religion, which admits of degrees. This lesson unpacks these conditions and explains why the Quran is exempt from the requirement of understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for narrator acceptance
The passage lists two conditions: dabit (accuracy) and adala (uprightness). Note that these are conditions for the narrator's reliability in transmitting hadith.
Other schools may have additional conditions.
2
Define dabit in detail
Dabit includes: (1) hearing the speech completely from beginning to end with full words and sentences, (2) understanding its intended meaning (linguistic or legal), (3) memorizing it with maximum effort, and (4) retaining it until transmission. The narrator must not be overconfident in memory but should think 'If I leave it, I will forget it.'
The text warns against arriving late to a session; such incomplete hearing is not proof.
3
Differentiate hadith from Quran regarding understanding
For the Quran, transmission of exact wording is sufficient even without understanding meaning, because the Quran is divinely preserved (Quran 15:9) and was transmitted by upright Imams after perfect dabit. For hadith, understanding is required because human preservation is fallible.
This distinction is based on the Quranic verse and the rationale of divine protection.
4
Define adala and note its gradation
Adala (uprightness) is defined as steadfastness in religion. It has varying degrees, from minimum (avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins) to higher degrees of piety.
Hanafis consider adala as a condition but it can be established by external signs.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Consider a narrator who hears half a hadith, memorizes it exactly, but does not understand its meaning. He is not dabit because he missed the beginning and lacks understanding. His narration is not accepted as proof, only as blessing.
For the Quran, such a narrator could transmit the wording if the chain is sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالضَّبْطُ هُوَ سَمَاعُ الْكَلَامِ كَمَا يَحِقُّ سِمَاعَة أَي سمَاعًا مِثْلَ سَمَاع شيءٍ يَحِقُ سَمَاعَةَ يَعْنِي مِنْ أَوْلِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ بِتَمَامِ الْكَلِمَاتِ وَالهة التركيبية وإنما قَالَ ذَالِكَ لأَنه كَثِيرًا مَا يَجِلَى السَّامِعُ فِي سَمَاع مَجْلِسِ الْوَعْظِ بَعْدَ أَنْ مَضَى شيْءٌ مِنَ أَوْلِهِ وَفَاتَهُ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمُهُ الْمُعِلْمُ لِلإِزدحام حَتَّى يُرَدِّدُ الْكَلَامُ الْمَاضِي. بَعْدَ حُضُورِهِ فَمِثْلُ هَذَا السَّمَاءِ لا يَكُونُ حُجَّةٌ فِى بَابِ الْحَدِيثِ بَلْ يَكُونُ تَبَرُّكا كَمَا يُوتى الصبْيَانُ فِي مَجْلَسَ الْوَعْظِ تَبَرُّكَّا لَهُمْ ثُمَّ فَهِمَة بِمَعْنَاهُ الَّذِي أُرِيدَ بِهِ لُغَوِيًا كَانَ أوْ شَرْعِيًا لآآنْ يَقْتَصِرَ عَلَى حِفْظِ الأَلْفاظِ فَقَط لَأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِسمَاعِ مُطلق بَلْ سَمَاعُ صَوْتِ ثُمَّ حَفِظَهُ بِبَذَلِ الْمَجْهُودِ لَهُ الضمِيرُ فِي حِفْظِهِ وَلَهُ رَاجِع الى الْمَسْمُوعِ وَالْمَجْهُودِ مَصْدَرٌ يَمَعْنَى الْجَهْدِ وَهُوَ الطَّاقَةُ أَي ثُمَّ حَفِظ ذلِكَ الْمَسْمُوعَ بَقْدِرِ الطَّاقَةِ البَشَرِيَّةِ لَهُ ثُمَّ الثَّبَات عَلَيْهِ بِمُحَافَظَةٍ حُدُودِهِ وَهِيَ الْعَمَلُ يُمُوْجَبَهِ بِبَدَنِهِ وَمُرَاقَبَتُهُ بَمُذَا كَرَتِهِ أَى مَعَ مُنَا كِرِيهِ حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مُسْتَقِرًا على إساءَة الظَّنْ بَنَفْسِهِ بِاَنْ لاَ يُعتَمِد عَلى نَفْسه بالقُوَّةِ الْحَافِظَةِ بَلْ يَقُولُ إِنِّي إذَا تَرَكْتُه نَسِيْتُه وهَذَا كُلُّهُ إِلَى حِيْنِ آدَائِهِ أَى إِلى حِيْنِ أَنْ يُؤَدِّيَهُ وَيُبَلِّغَهُ إِلَى شخص آخَرَ كَذَلِكَ وَاحِدًا كَانَ أَوْ جَمَاعَةٌ فَحِينَئِذٍ تَفْرَغَ ذِمَّتُهُ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَتَسْتَغلُ بِهِ ذِمَّةٌ إِنْسَانِ آخَرَ يُؤَدِّيَة إِلى أَحَدٍ وَهَكَذَا الَى يَوْمَ التَّنَادِ أَوْ إِلى تُؤلّف كتب الأحَادِيثِ وَهَذَا بِخِلافِ الْقُرْآنِ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُسْتَرَطُ لِنَقْلِهِ فَيْمُهُ لأَنَّهُ مَا ثَبَتَ فِي الأصل الأ بأيْمَةِ الْهُدَى وَخَيْر الْوُرَى وَهُمْ نَقَلُوْهُ بَعْدَ الضَّبْطِ النَّامِ وَنَظْمُتُهُ فِي نفسية مُعْجِرٌ يَتَعَلَّقُ بهِ الأَحْكَامُ فَلَمْ يُعْتَبَرُ مَعْنَاهُ وَلآنه محفوظ عن التغيير ومصون عَنِ التَّبْدِيلِ قَالَ الله تَعَالَى إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّالَهُ لَحَفِظُونَ فَيَصحُ نُقِلَ نَظْمُهُ مِمَّنْ لَيْسَتْ لَهُ مَعْرِفَةٌ بِمَعْنَاهُ وَالْعَدَالَة وَهُوَ الاِسْتِقَامَةُ فِي الدِّينِ وَهُوَ يَتَفَاوَتْ إِلى دَرَجَاتِ متفاوتة بالفَرَاطِ وَالتَّعَصب. والضبط هو سماع الكلام الخ : ضبط کے معنی ہیں کلام کہ کما حقہ سننا یعنی کلام کو شروع سے آخر تک تمام کلمات اور بیت ترکیبیہ کے ساتھ اس طرح سنتا جیسا کہ نئے کافی ہے۔ یہ ماتن نے اس وجہ سے کہا ہے کہ اکثر ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ سننے والا مجلس وعظ میں دیر سے پہونچا۔ جب کہ وعظ کا اول حصہ گذر چکا ہوتا ہے اور وہ اس سے محروم رہ جاتا ہے اور استاد کو بھی ہجوم کی وجہ سے اس کا علم نہیں ہوتا تاکہ وہ گذشتہ کلام کو دوبارہ دہرائے۔ ایسا سننا حدیث کے باب میں حجت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ محض تبرک ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ بچوں کو مجلس وعظ میں تبرک کے لئے لایا جاتا ہے۔
And accuracy (dabit) is hearing the speech as it deserves to be heard, i.e., a hearing like the hearing of something that deserves to be heard, meaning from its beginning to its end with complete words and compositional sentences. He said that only because often the listener comes to a preaching session after something of its beginning has passed and missed it, and the teacher does not know it due to crowding so that he might repeat the past speech after his arrival. So such hearing is not a proof in the chapter of hadith, but it is for blessing, just as children are brought to a preaching session for blessing for them. Then he understands its intended meaning, whether linguistic or legal, not confining to just memorizing the words, because it is not absolute hearing but hearing of a sound. Then he preserves it by expending effort. The pronoun in 'preserving it' refers to the heard thing, and 'effort' is a verbal noun meaning ability, i.e., he preserves that heard thing to the extent of human ability. Then he remains steadfast upon it by safeguarding its limits, which is acting according to it with his body and monitoring it with his memory, i.e., with his discretion while being settled in thinking ill of himself, not relying on his memory strength, but saying: If I leave it, I will forget it. All this is until the time of his performance, i.e., until the time he performs it and conveys it to another person, whether one or a group. Then his responsibility becomes free before Allah, and the responsibility of another person becomes occupied with it, and he performs it to someone, and so on until the Day of Summons or until the compilation of hadith books. And this is different from the Quran, because for its transmission understanding its meaning was not required, because it was established originally only by the Imams of guidance and the best of mankind, and they transmitted it after perfect accuracy, and its composition in itself is a miracle to which rulings are attached, so its meaning is not considered; and because it is preserved from change and protected from alteration. Allah said: 'Indeed We sent down the Reminder and indeed We will be its guardians.' So it is valid to transmit its wording from one who has no knowledge of its meaning. And uprightness (adala) is steadfastness in religion, and it varies into varying degrees by excess and prejudice. The Urdu commentary says: Accuracy is hearing the speech as it deserves to be heard, i.e., from beginning to end with all words and compositional sentences, hearing in a way that suffices. The author said this because often it happens that a listener arrives late to a preaching session, missing the first part, and the teacher is unaware due to crowding so he cannot repeat the past speech. Such hearing is not a proof in hadith but is merely for blessing, just as children are brought to a preaching session for blessing.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage explains the second and third conditions for a narrator: accuracy (dabit) and uprightness (adala). Accuracy is defined as hearing the speech completely from beginning to end, in its proper form, with full words and sentences. The author warns against the common practice of arriving late to a session and catching only part of the speech; such incomplete hearing is not considered valid for hadith transmission but only for blessing. Furthermore, accuracy requires understanding the intended meaning (linguistic or legal) of the speech, not merely memorizing the words, because mere sound memorization without understanding is not sufficient for reliable narration. The narrator must then exert maximum effort to preserve the heard material in memory and maintain it until he transmits it to another, all the while distrusting his own memory to ensure he does not forget. This applies whether the transmission is to a single person or many. The passage then distinguishes hadith from the Quran: for the Quran, transmission of the exact wording is sufficient even without understanding the meaning, because the Quran is divinely preserved and mutawatir in transmission from the righteous Imams; the Quran itself is a miracle, and its wording is safeguarded by Allah (إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّالَهُ لَحَفِظُونَ). Finally, uprightness (adala) is defined as steadfastness in religion, which admits of degrees and can vary. This lesson establishes the Hanafi requirement that a narrator must be dabit (accurate in hearing, understanding, and memorizing) and adil (upright in religious observance).

Key Terms
الضبط (al-ḍabṭ): Accuracy in hearing, understanding meaning, memorizing with effort, and retaining until transmission; it is a condition for the narrator.
العدالة (al-ʿadāla): Uprightness in religion, steadfastness in religious observance; it admits of varying degrees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is required for accuracy (dabit) beyond just hearing the words?
A) Only memorizing the exact words
B) Understanding the intended meaning
C) Writing down the hadith immediately
D) Having many teachers

Key Takeaway
Accuracy in hadith narration requires complete hearing, understanding, and diligent preservation; uprightness is steadfastness in religion.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Condition of Dabt in Hadith Transmission
Defining dabt and its conditions for hadith transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of dabt, identify its four components, and explain why understanding is required for hadith but not for Quran.

Core Idea
Dabt requires complete hearing, understanding, memorization, and steadfastness — mere listening is insufficient.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi condition of dabt (precision) for reliable hadith transmission. You will learn that a transmitter must do more than just hear the words — they must fully comprehend and retain the entire speech. The lesson also contrasts this with the Quran, whose divine preservation makes understanding unnecessary for valid transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its legal role
Recognize that dabt is a condition required in the transmitter (rawi) for hadith to be accepted. It is not a mere virtue but a legal prerequisite for the validity of transmission.
Dabt is part of the broader conditions of 'adalah and dabt for riwayah.
2
Break down the definition into its components
Examine the author's definition: dabt is hearing the entire speech from beginning to end, understanding its intended meaning (linguistic or legal), memorizing it with full effort, and then remaining steadfast until transmission — this includes regular review and self-doubt about memory.
The four components: complete hearing, understanding, memorization, steadfastness.
3
Apply the example of the latecomer to a sermon
The text provides a concrete negative example: a person who arrives after the sermon began misses the first part; his later hearing is not dabt but merely tabarruk (seeking blessing). This shows that incomplete hearing invalidates dabt.
This example clarifies that hearing a part is not sufficient; the whole must be caught.
4
Distinguish hadith transmission from Quran transmission
The text explains that for the Quran, understanding is not required because its preservation is guaranteed by Allah (Q. 15:9) and its words are miraculous. Hence even someone who does not understand the meaning can validly transmit the Quran.
This contrast highlights the unique status of the Quran as a revealed miracle.
5
Note the scriptural proof
The author cites Quran 15:9, 'Indeed, it is We who sent down the Quran, and indeed, We will be its guardian,' to support that the Quran is protected from alteration, so understanding is not needed for its transmission.
This dalil is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala in Hanafi usul.

ہوں۔ ایسا نہیں ہے کہ صرف الفاظ کے حفظ کرنے پر اکتفاء کیا جائے۔ کیونکہ ایسا سننا صرف سماع صوت شمار ہوتا ہے۔ سماع مطلق (یعنی کاج کامل ) نہیں ہے۔ ثُم حفظة الخ : پھرتے ہوئے کلام کو انسانی طاقت کے مطابق ذہن میں محفوظ کر لیتا لفظ حفظة اودر کے دونوں کی خبر کا مر جمع مسموع ہے ام الجهود مصدر ہے جہد کے معنی میں ہے جس کے معنی طاقت "" لا کے ہیں یعنی پھر اس سننے والے نے کلام مسموع کو بشری طاقت کے مطابق یاد کر لیا ہو۔ كُمُ الثَّبَات عَلَيْهِ : پھر اس پر اس کی حدود کی محافظت کے ساتھ ساتھ قائم رہنا۔ یعنی اس کلام کے نقاشے پر ہندن سے عمل بھی کرنا۔ وَ مُرَاقَبَتُهُ بِمُذَا كَرَتِهِ : اور اس کی دیکھ بھال کرتے رہنا۔ اسے بار بار زبانی یاد کر کے یعنی اس کلام کو ذہن نشین ہوتے ہو ئے اس کو بار بار تکرار کرتے رہنا۔ على اساءة الظن بنفسه . اپنے نفس پر بد گمان ره کر یعنی اپنے نفس کی قوت حافظہ پر اعتماد نہ کرے بلکہ خیال رکھے کہ اگر میں اسے ترک کر دوں گا تو بھول جاؤں گا۔ وَهَذَا كُلَّه إِلى جِيْنِ آدَاء ؟ - یہ سب کچھ اس کی ادا کے وقت تک یہ تمام باتیں جن کا اوپر ذکر کیا گیا یہ ہے اس وقت تک ضروری ہے کہ سامع اس حدیث کو دوسرے شخص تک بحفاظت ہو نچارے جن کو پہونچائے۔ وہ فرد واحد ہو یا جماعت ہو اس وقت اللہ کے نزدیک اس کی ذمہ داری ختم ہو گئی، اور اس حدیث کے ساتھ دوسرے شخص کی ذمہ داری عائد ہو گئی۔ کہ وہ دوسرے شخص تک اس کو پہونچادے۔ اور یہ سلسلہ قیامت تک یا یہاں تک کے کتب حدیث کی تدوین و ترتیب ہو جائے مگر قرآن مجید کی حفظ وامانت اس کے بر خلاف ہے کیونکہ قرآن مجید کو دوسرے بیک نقل کرنے کے لئے اس کے معنی کا سمجھنا ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کی ایک وجہ تو یہ ہے کہ نقل قرآن اصل میں (ابتداء) جو کچھ بھی ثابت ہے۔ وہ خیر الوری صلی اللہ علیہ و سلم اور ائمہ ہدی رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے ثابت ہے ان حضرات نے کامل ضبط کے بعد سے نقل فرمایا ہے اس کے علاوہ خود قرآن مجید کا نظم (لفظ) خود معجز ہیں جن سے احکام وابستہ ہیں لہذا اس بارے میں اس کے معنی کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ منجانب اللہ قرآن مجید محفوظ اور ہر قسم کے تغیر و تبدل حفاظت کا وعدہ ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے۔ اِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَفِظُونَ الذا قرآن مجید کی نقل ایسے شخص سے درست ہے جو اس کے معنی کو نہیں سمجھتا ہو۔ نقل وَالْعَدَالَةُ وَ فِی الاستقامة فِي الدِّينِ : اور عدالت کے معنی ہیں دین مستقیم (اٹل ) رہنے کا۔ اور یہ
And dabt is hearing the speech as it deserves to be heard, i.e., hearing like the hearing of a thing that deserves to be heard, meaning from its beginning to its end with complete words and compositional structure. And he said that only because often the listener comes to a sermon after some of its beginning has passed and he missed it, and the teacher does not know him due to crowding so that he might repeat the past speech after his arrival. So such hearing is not a proof in the chapter of hadith, rather it is a blessing, just as children are brought to the sermon for blessing. Then understanding its intended meaning, whether linguistic or legal, so that he does not confine himself to merely memorizing the words, because that is not absolute hearing but just hearing sound. Then he memorizes it with exertion; the pronoun 'hi' in 'hifzihi' refers to what is heard, and 'majhud' is a verbal noun meaning energy, i.e., then he memorizes that heard thing within human capacity. Then he remains steadfast upon it by preserving its limits, which is acting upon it with his body and guarding it by repetition, i.e., while doubting himself, not relying on his memory power but saying: If I leave it I will forget it. And all this until the time of his performance, i.e., until he performs it and conveys it to another person, whether one or many. Then his responsibility before Allah is discharged, and the responsibility of another person becomes binding to convey it to someone else, and so on until the Day of Gathering or until the compilation of hadith books. And this is contrary to the Quran, because for its transmission understanding was not required, because it was established originally only by the Imams of guidance and the best of mankind, and they transmitted it after complete dabt, and its composition itself is a miracle upon which rulings depend, so its meaning was not considered; and because it is preserved from change and protected from alteration. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, it is We who sent down the Qur'an, and indeed, We will be its guardian.' So its transmission is valid from one who has no knowledge of its meaning. And 'adalah is steadfastness in religion, and it varies in degrees with excess and prejudice.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Noor al-Anwar defines the condition of dabt (precision) for a hadith transmitter. The author explains that dabt is not merely hearing, but hearing the entire speech from beginning to end with all its words and structure. He gives an example: a person who arrives late to a sermon and misses the first part cannot be considered a reliable transmitter of what he heard, because his hearing is incomplete; it is only a blessing (tabarruk), similar to children brought for blessing. Then he adds that one must understand the intended meaning (linguistic or legal) of what is heard; mere memorization of words without understanding is just hearing sounds, not proper hearing. After that, one must memorize with full effort, maintain the knowledge by repeatedly reviewing and acting upon it, and remain distrustful of one's own memory until the time of transmission. This ensures the responsibility of accurate transmission is fulfilled. The text then distinguishes hadith transmission from Quran transmission: for the Quran, understanding the meaning is not required because the Quran was transmitted by the best of mankind with complete dabt, its words are miraculous, and Allah has guaranteed its preservation. Therefore, even someone who does not understand the meaning can validly transmit the Quran. The passage ends by introducing 'adalah (uprightness) as another condition, which varies in degrees.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): Hearing the speech completely from beginning to end with understanding, memorization, and steadfastness until transmission
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): Steadfastness in religion, which varies in degrees
سماع (samāʿ): Hearing with attention and comprehension, not mere audial reception

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which component of dabt is fulfilled by understanding the intended meaning of the speech?
A) Complete hearing from beginning to end
B) Steadfastness until transmission
C) Understanding the meaning
D) Memorization with full effort

Key Takeaway
Dabt requires complete hearing, understanding, memorization, and steadfastness; for the Quran, divine preservation makes understanding unnecessary.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Conditions of 'Adalah in Hadith Narration
Defining 'adalah and outlining transmission requirements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'adalah operationally, identify what breaks it, and distinguish the transmission requirements for hadith versus Quran.

Core Idea
'Adalah requires dominance of piety over desire; a major sin or persistence on minor sins destroys it.

This lesson delves into the essential quality of 'adalah (integrity) required for a hadith narrator. The passage begins by outlining the responsibilities of a narrator: understanding, memorizing, acting upon, and reviewing the narration. It then provides a detailed definition of 'adalah, the conditions that uphold it, and the sins that nullify it. Understanding these principles is foundational for the science of hadith criticism (al-jarḥ wa al-ta'dīl).

Guided Path
1
Trace the stages of hadith transmission
Identify from the passage the required stages: understanding the meaning, memorizing according to human capacity, being steadfast upon it (acting), reviewing it by discussion, and maintaining this until narration.
The passage emphasizes that merely hearing sounds is insufficient; understanding is essential.
2
Note the exception for Quran transmission
Contrast the hadith process with the Quran: understanding the meaning is not required for Quran transmission due to divine preservation (Quran 15:9). The verse is cited as proof.
This exception is based on the miraculous nature of Quranic wording and Allah's promise of preservation.
3
Define 'adalah operationally
The passage defines 'adalah as steadfastness in religion, but the operational definition is the preponderance of the inclination of religion and reason over desire and lust.
This is a contextual degree; complete avoidance of all sin is only for prophets.
4
Identify what vitiates 'adalah
Committing a major sin (kabīrah) or persisting in a minor sin (al-iṣrār ʿalā al-ṣaghīrah) nullifies 'adalah. Occasional minor sins without persistence do not break it.
Persistence on minor sins is treated like a major sin in effect.
5
Analyze the lists of major sins and the relativistic view
The passage provides several lists of major sins from different Companions and concludes with a relativistic definition: every sin is major compared to what is below and minor compared to what is above. It also contrasts the standard with testimony in non-hudud cases.
For hadith narration, a higher standard is applied than for ordinary testimony.

ثُمَّ هِمَ مَعْنَاهُ الخ . پھر اس کے مرادی معنی کو سمجھنا لغوی ہوں خواہ شرکی ہوں۔ ایسا نہیں ہے کہ صرف الفاظ کے حفظ کرنے پر اکتفاء کیا جائے۔ کیونکہ ایسا سننا صرف سماع صوت شمار ہوتا ہے۔ سماع مطلق (یعنی کاج کامل ) نہیں ہے۔ ثُم حفظة الخ : پھرتے ہوئے کلام کو انسانی طاقت کے مطابق ذہن میں محفوظ کر لیتا لفظ حفظة اودر کے دونوں کی خبر کا مر جمع مسموع ہے ام الجهود مصدر ہے جہد کے معنی میں ہے جس کے معنی طاقت لا کے ہیں یعنی پھر اس سننے والے نے کلام مسموع کو بشری طاقت کے مطابق یاد کر لیا ہو۔ ثُمَّ الثَّبَات عَلَيْهِ : پھر اس پر اس کی حدود کی محافظت کے ساتھ ساتھ قائم رہنا۔ یعنی اس کلام کے نقاشے پر ہندن سے عمل بھی کرنا۔ وَ مُرَاقَبَتُهُ بِمُذَاكَرَتِهِ : اور اس کی دیکھ بھال کرتے رہنا۔ اسے بار بار زبانی یاد کر کے یعنی اس کلام کو ذہن نشین ہوتے ہوئے اس کو بار بار تکرار کرتے رہنا۔ على اساءة الظن بنفسه . اپنے نفس پر بد گمان ره کر یعنی اپنے نفس کی قوت حافظہ پر اعتماد نہ کرے بلکہ خیال رکھے کہ اگر میں اسے ترک کر دوں گا تو بھول جاؤں گا۔ وَهَذَا كُلَّه إِلى جِينِ أَدَاء ؟ - یہ سب کچھ اس کی ادا کے وقت تک یہ تمام باتیں جن کا اوپر ذکر کیا گیا یہ ہے اس وقت تک ضروری ہے کہ سامع اس حدیث کو دوسرے شخص تک بحفاظت ہو نچارے جن کو پہونچائے۔ وہ فرد واحد ہو یا جماعت ہو اس وقت اللہ کے نزدیک اس کی ذمہ داری ختم ہو گئی، اور اس حدیث کے ساتھ دوسرے شخص کی ذمہ داری عائد ہو گئی۔ کہ وہ دوسرے شخص تک اس کو پہونچادے۔ اور یہ سلسلہ قیامت تک یا یہاں تک کے کتب حدیث کی تدوین و ترتیب ہو جائے مگر قرآن مجید کی حفظ وامانت اس کے بر خلاف ہے کیونکہ قرآن مجید کو دوسرے بیک نقل کرنے کے لئے اس کے معنی کا سمجھنا ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کی ایک وجہ تو یہ ہے کہ نقل قرآن اصل میں (ابتداء) جو کچھ بھی ثابت ہے۔ وہ خیر الوری صلی اللہ علیہ و سلم اور ائمہ ہدی رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے ثابت ہے ان حضرات نے کامل ضبط کے بعد سے نقل فرمایا ہے اس کے علاوہ خود قرآن مجید کا نظم (لفظ) خود معجز ہیں جن سے احکام وابستہ ہیں لہذا اس بارے میں اس کے معنی کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ منجانب اللہ قرآن مجید محفوظ اور ہر قسم کے تغیر و تبدل حفاظت کا وعدہ ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے۔ اِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لَحَفِظُونَ الذا قرآن مجید کی نقل ایسے شخص سے درست ہے جو اس کے معنی کو نہیں سمجھتا ہو۔
نقل
وَالْعَدَالَةُ وَ فِی الاستقامة فِي الدِّينِ : اور عدالت کے معنی ہیں دین مستقیم (اٹل ) رہنے کا۔ اور یہ معنی افراط و تعصب کے لحاظ سے مختلف درجات میں تقسیم ہیں۔ والمُعْتَبَرُ ههنا كَمَا لَها وَهُوَ رُجْحَانُ جِهَةِ الدِّيْنِ وَالْعَقْلِ عَلَى طَرِيقِ الْهَوَى والشهوةِ حَتَّى إِذَا ارْتَكَبَ كَبِيرَةً أَوْ أَصَرُ عَلَى صَغِيْرَةٍ سَقَطَتْ عَدَالَتُهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُصِرُ عَلى صَغِيْرَةٍ بَلْ يَلِمُ بِمَا أَحْيَانًا لَمْ تَسْقُطْ عَدَالَتَهُ لأَنَّ الْاِحْتِرَانَ عَنْ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ خَوَاصُ الأَنْبِيَاءِ والتَّعَدِّرُ فِي حَقٍّ عَامَّةِ الْبَشَرِ وَالإِصْرَارُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْكَبِيرَةِ فَيَجِبُ الاِحْتِرَار عَنْهُ وَفِي الْكَبَائِرِ اِخْتِلافٌ فَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّهَا سَبْعٌ الإشرَاكِ بِاللهِ وَقَتْلُ النَّفْسُ الْمُوْمِنَةَ وَقَدْفُ مُحْنَةِ وَالْفِرَارُ مِنَ الزُّحْفِ وَأَكُلُ مَالِ اليْتِيمِ وَعُقُوقَ الْوَالِدَيْنِ الْمُسْلِمِيْنِ والإِلْحَادُ فِي الْحَرَمِ وَرَوَى أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ مَعَ ذَلِكَ أَكُلُ الرِّبَا وَعَلَى أَضَافَ إِلَى ذَالِكَ السَّرَقَةَ وَشَرْبِ الْحَمَرِ وَزَادَ بَعْضُهُمُ الزَّنَا واللواطةَ وَالسِّحْرَ وَشَهَادَةَ الزُّهْرِ وَالْيَمِيْنَ الْكَاذِبَةِ وَقَطَعَ الطَّرِيقِ وَلِغَيْبَةٍ وَالْقِمَارِ وَقَيْلَ هُمَا أَمْرَانِ إِضافِيَانِ فَكُلُّ ذَنَبِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا تَحْتَهُ كَبِيْرُ وَبِاعْتِبَارِ مَا فَوْقَهُ صَغِيْرٌ دُونَ قُصُوْرِهَا وَهُوَ مَاثَبَتَ بِظَاهِرِ الإِسلام وَاعْتَدَالِ العَقْلِ فَإِنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنْ كُلِّ مَنْ هُوَ مُسلِمٌ مُعْتَدِلُ العَقْل لا يَكْذِبُ وَيَمْتَنِعُ عَنْ خِلافِ الشَّرْعِ ولَكِنْ هَذَا لَا يَكْفِي لروَايَةِ الْحَدِيثِ لَاَنْ هَذَا الظَّاهِرَ يُعَارِضُهُ ظَاهِرٌ آخَرُ وَهُوَ هَوَى النَّفْس فَكَانَ عَدْلاً مِنْ وَجْهِ دُونَ وَجْهِ إِنْمَا يَكْفِى هَذَا فِي الشَّاهِدِ فِى غَيْرِ الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ مَالَمْ يَطْعُنِ الْخَصْمُ فَإِذَا كَانَ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ أَوْ طَعَنَ الْخَصْمُ فِيْهِ لَا يَكْفِي هَيْنَا أَيْضًا وَالإسلامُ وَهُوَ التَّصْدِيقُ وَالإِقْرَارُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى كَمَا هُوَ وَاقِعٌ فَالتُصَدِيقُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ نِسْبَةِ الصِّدْقِ إِلَى الْمُكْبِرِ اِخْتِيَارًا الآن الإِنْعَانَ قَدْ يَقَعُ فِي قَلْبِ الْكَافِرِ بالضرُورَةِ وَلا يُسمى ذلِكَ إِيْمَانًا قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَ هُمْ وَحُصُولُ هَذَا الْمَعْنِى لِلْكُفَّارِ مَمْنُوعٌ وَلَوْ سُلمَ فَكَفْرُهُمْ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَمَارَاتِ الإِفْكَارِ وَالأَقْرَارِ شَرْطُ لإجْرَاءِ الأحكام أَوْ رُكْنُ مِثْلَ التَّصْدِيقِ والمُعْتَبَرُ فَهُنَا كَمَا لَها :- لیکن یہاں روایات حدیث کے باب میں کمال استقامت ترجمہ و تشریح عدالت کا ملہ معتبر ہے اور عدالت کا ملہ یہ ہے کہ جہت دین و عقل و خواہش و شہوت کی راہ و رسم پر غالب ہو چنانچہ جب کوئی کسی کبیرہ گناہ کا مرتکب ہو یا کسی صغیرہ گناہ کے ارتکاب پر مصر ہو تو اس کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے گناہ کبیرہ سے مکمل اجتناب اور صغیرہ گناہ کے اصرار سے بچاؤ اور دین پر قائم
Then understanding its meaning, whether lexical or technical. It is not that one is satisfied with merely memorizing words, because such listening is only hearing the sound; it is not absolute listening. Then memorizing it according to human capacity. Then being steadfast upon it, i.e., acting upon it. And reviewing it by discussing it. With thinking ill of oneself. And all this until the time of performance. This is necessary until the listener transmits the hadith safely to another person. Then the responsibility is transferred. This chain continues until the end of time or until compilation of hadith books. But the preservation of the Quran is different because understanding meaning is not necessary for transmission. Allah said: 'Indeed, We sent down the Reminder and indeed We will be its guardians.' So transmission of Quran from one who does not understand is valid. And 'adalatu is steadfastness in religion. Its degrees vary. What is considered here is the preponderance of religion and reason over desire and lust. So if one commits a major sin or persists in a minor sin, his 'adalah falls. If he does not persist but occasionally commits a minor sin, his 'adalah does not fall because complete avoidance is a characteristic of prophets, and it is difficult for common people. But persistence on minor sin is like a major sin. There is difference of opinion on major sins: Ibn Umar said they are seven: shirk, killing a believer, slandering chaste women, fleeing from battle, consuming orphan's property, disobeying Muslim parents, and heresy in the sanctuary. Abu Hurairah added usury. Others added theft, drinking alcohol, and some added fornication, sodomy, sorcery, false testimony, false oath, banditry, backbiting, and gambling. Some said they are relative: every sin is major compared to what is below and minor compared to what is above. What is established by apparent Islam and sound mind is that every Muslim of sound mind does not lie and avoids violating the law, but this is not sufficient for hadith narration because this appearance is counterbalanced by another appearance: the desire of the soul. So one is 'adl from one aspect but not from another. This suffices in testimony except in hudud and qisas unless the opponent challenges. But in hudud and qisas or if challenged, it does not suffice. Islam is affirmation and acknowledgment of Allah as He is. Affirmation is attributing truth to the Creator willingly, because compulsion may occur in the heart of the disbeliever but is not called faith. Allah said: 'They recognize it as they recognize their sons.' But this meaning is denied for disbelievers, and even if conceded, their disbelief is due to signs of rejection and acknowledgment is a condition for applying rulings, or a pillar like affirmation. What is considered here is perfection of 'adalah: that the aspect of religion and reason prevail over the path of desire and lust.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a definition and expansion of the concept of 'adalah (integrity) as a condition for hadith narration. The author first outlines the process of hadith transmission: the narrator must understand the meaning, memorize it, act upon it, review it, and maintain it until narration. Then he distinguishes Quran transmission, where understanding is not required due to divine protection. The core definition of 'adalah is given as 'steadfastness in religion', but the operational definition is 'preponderance of religion and reason over desire and lust'. The passage then discusses what vitiates 'adalah: committing a major sin or persisting in a minor sin. Occasional minor sins do not nullify it. A list of major sins from various narrations is provided, concluding with the relativistic view. Finally, the passage contrasts the apparent integrity due to Islam and reason with the hidden influence of desire, stating that for hadith narration, the standard is higher than for testimony in routine cases. The author emphasizes that 'adalah here means the habitual dominance of piety.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-'adalah): الاستقامة في الدين بغلبة جهة الدين والعقل على الهوى والشهوة
الكبيرة (al-kabirah): الذنب الذي يوجب الحد في الدنيا أو الوعيد في الآخرة، أو هو ما دون الكبائر
الإصرار على الصغيرة (al-israr 'ala al-saghirah): المداومة على فعل الصغيرة بدون توبة، وهو بمنزلة الكبيرة في إسقاط العدالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a narrator's 'adalah if he commits a minor sin but does not persist in it?
A) His 'adalah falls immediately.
B) His 'adalah does not fall because occasional minor sins are excusable for non-prophets.
C) He must repent for his 'adalah to be restored.
D) His narration becomes invalid only if the sin is a major sin.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's 'adalah is defined by the dominance of piety over desire; it is broken by major sins or persistence on minor sins, but occasional minor sins are excusable.

Conditions for Acceptance of Hadith Narration
Listing four shurut and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a narrator's acceptance in Hanafi usul and apply them to classify narrators as acceptable or unacceptable.

Core Idea
Four conditions — Islam, 'adala, sanity, and precision — determine whether a narrator's report is accepted.

In Hanafi usul, not every report is accepted. The reliability of the narrator is judged by four fixed conditions. This passage lists them and clarifies some exceptions, such as women and slaves, whose narration is accepted despite limitations in testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Conditions
From the passage, extract the four conditions: Islam, 'adala (justice), kamil al-'aql (complete intellect/sanity), and dabit (precision/memory).
These are listed implicitly via their opposites: kafir (no Islam), fasiq (no 'adala), child/insane (no sanity), severely heedless (no dabt).
2
Match Rejected Narrators to Missing Condition
For each rejected type (kafir, fasiq, child, insane, heedless), identify which condition is absent.
The passage explicitly links: kafir → Islam, fasiq → 'adala, child/insane → intellect, heedless → dabt.
3
Identify Exceptions
Note that the blind, the one punished for false accusation (mahdud fi al-qadhf), women, and slaves are accepted as narrators even if their testimony is not accepted in transactions.
Their narration is accepted because they can meet the four conditions; the limitation is in shahada, not riwaya.
4
Understand the Riwaya vs Shahada Distinction
Recognize the Hanafi usul principle that narration (riwaya) has less stringent conditions than testimony (shahada). This explains the exceptions.
For example, a woman can be a precise and just narrator even if her testimony is restricted in certain cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِهَذَا لَا يُقْبَلُ خَبَرُ الْكَافِرِ وَالْفَاسِقِ والصَّبِيُّ وَالْمعْتُوهِ وَالَّذِئ إشتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُهُ تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرُوطِ الأَبَعَةِ عَلَى غَيْرِ تَرْتِيْبٍ اللَّفْ فَالْكَافِرُ رَاجِعْ إِلَى الإِسْلامِ وَالْفَاسِقُ إِلَى الْعَدَالَةِ و يصبِى وَالْمَعْتُوْهُ إِلَى كَمَال الْعَقْلِ وَالَّذِي اسْتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُه إلى الضبْطِ وَأَمَّا الأَعْمَى وَالْمُحْدُودُ فِي الْقَدْفِ وَالْمَرْأةُ وَالْعَبْد فَتَقْبَلُ رِوَايَتُهُمْ فِي الْحَدِيثِ لِوُجُودِ الشَّرَائِطِ وَإِنْ لَمْ تقبل شَهَادَتْهُمْ فِي الْمَعَامَلات هَكَذَا قِيلَ .
And for this reason, the report of the disbeliever, the fasiq, the child, the insane, and the one whose heedlessness is severe is not accepted. This is a branching from the four conditions without order. The disbeliever relates to Islam, the fasiq to 'adalat, the child and the insane to completeness of intellect, and the one whose heedlessness is severe to precision (dabit). As for the blind, the one who has been punished for slander, the woman, and the slave: their narration in hadith is accepted because the conditions exist, even if their testimony is not accepted in transactions. Thus it is said.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage lists the four conditions for a narrator of hadith: Islam, justice ('adala), sanity (kamil al-'aql), and precision (dabit). It explains that the narration of a kafir is rejected due to lack of Islam; of a fasiq due to lack of 'adala; of a child or mad person due to lack of sanity; and of a heedless person due to lack of precision. Then it notes exceptions: the blind, a person punished for false accusation (qadhf), women, and slaves can narrate hadith because they can still fulfill the conditions despite limitations in testimony. This reflects the Hanafi usul distinction between riwaya (narration) and shahada (testimony).

Key Terms
ضبط (ḍabṭ): Precision in memory and accuracy in narration; the condition of being free from gross heedlessness.
محدود في القذف (maḥdūd fī al-qadhf): One who has been punished for false accusation of adultery; such a person's testimony is rejected but narration is accepted if he repents and becomes 'adil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi conditions, whose narration is NOT accepted?
A) A woman
B) A slave
C) A fasiq
D) A blind person

Key Takeaway
Four conditions (Islam, 'adala, sanity, dabt) govern narrator acceptance, with exceptions where narration is accepted despite limitations in testimony.

Summary Faith vs Detailed Description in Accepting Islam
Commentary on sufficiency of summary faith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that summary faith (iman ijmal) is sufficient for accepting Islam and evaluate the opposing view requiring detailed description.

Core Idea
Summary faith suffices; requiring detail causes hardship.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar addresses a dispute among early Hanafi scholars: must a person describe Islamic beliefs in detail to be considered Muslim, or is a general affirmation enough? The author defends the majority view using prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is about the requirement of tafsir (detailed description) vs ijmal (summary) in accepting Islam.
2
State the Hanafi position
Summary faith is sufficient; one needs only to affirm that everything from the Prophet is true and that Allah is eternal with attributes.
3
Examine the proof
The Prophet accepted the testimony of a Bedouin and a slave girl without demanding details.
These hadiths are primary evidence.
4
Present the opposing view
Some mashayikh require detailed description, leading to severe consequences like separation of spouses.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The opposing view causes great hardship and contradicts the easy nature of Islam; thus the majority view is preferred.
The principle of avoiding haraj is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باسمَائِهِ وَصفَاتِهِ بَدَل مِنْ قَوْلِهِ بِاللَّهِ وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُتَعَلِّقًا بِالْوَاقِعِ الْمُقَدِّرِ خَيْرًا لَهُوَ وَالإِسْمَاءُ فِى الْمُسْتَقَّاتُ مِنَ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ وَالْعَلِيمِ وَالْقَدِيرِ وَالصَّفَاتُ هِيَ مَبَادِئَ الْمُسْتَقَّاتِ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ وَالْقُدْرَةِ وَقُبُوْلُ أَحْكَامِهِ وَشَرَائِعِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَرْفُوعًا مَعْطَوْفًا عَلى الإِقْرَارِ وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَجْورًا مَعْطَوْفًا عَلى قَوْلِهِ بِأَسْمَائِهِ وَصِفَاتِهِ وَالشَّرْطُ فِيْهِ الْبَيَانُ إِجْمَالاً كَمَا ذَكَرْنَا أَي الشَّرْطُ فِي الإِسْلَامِ بَيَانُ الشَّرَائِعِ إِجْمَالاً بِأَنْ يَقُولَ كُلُّ مَا جَاءَ بِهِ مُحَمَّدٌ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَهُوَ حَقٌّ وَإِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى مَعَ جَمِيعِ صِفَاتِهِ قَدِيمٌ ثَابِتٌ حَقٌّ وَقَدْ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَكْتَفِي بِالإِيْمَانِ الإِجْمَالِي حَيْثُ قَالَ لِلْأَعْرَابِي شَهِدَ بِهِلاَلِ رَمَضَانَ أَتَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلا اللهُ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُوْلُ اللهِ قَالَ نَعَمْ فَقَبِلَ شَهَادَتَهُ وَحَكَمَ بِالصَّوْمِ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لِجَارِيَةٍ أَيْنَ اللهُ قَالَتْ فِي السَّمَاءِ قَالَ مَنْ أَنَا فَقَالَتْ أَنْتَ رَسُولُ اللهِ فَقَالَ أَعْتِقُوهَا فَإِنَّهَا مُؤْمِنَةٌ وَقَالَ بَعْضُ المَشَائِخِ لابُدَّ مِنَ الْوَصْفِ عَلَى التَّفْصِيْلِ حَتَّى إِذَا بَلَغَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ فَاسْتَوْصَفَتِ الإِسْلَامَ فَلَمْ تَصِفْ فَإِنَّهَا تَبِينُ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا وَجُعِلَ ذَلِكَ رِدَّةً مِنْهَا وَفِيْهِ حَرَجٌ عَظِيمٌ لا يَخْفَى وَلِهَذَا لَا يُقْبَلُ خَبَرُ الْكَافِرِ وَالْفَاسِقِ وَالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَعْتُوهِ وَالَّذِي اشْتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُهُ تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرُوطِ الأَرْبَعَةِ عَلَى غَيْرِ تَرْتِيْبٍ فَالْكَافِرُ رَاجِعٌ إِلَى الإِسْلَامِ وَالْفَاسِقُ إِلَى الْعَدَالَةِ وَالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَعْتُوْهُ إِلَى كَمَال الْعَقْلِ وَالَّذِي اشْتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُهُ إِلَى الضَّبْطِ وَأَمَّا الأَعْمَى وَالْمَحْدُودُ فِي الْقَذْفِ وَالْمَرْأَةُ وَالْعَبْدُ فَتُقْبَلُ رِوَايَتُهُمْ فِي الْحَدِيثِ لِوُجُودِ الشَّرَائِطِ وَإِنْ لَمْ تُقْبَلْ شَهَادَتُهُمْ فِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ هَكَذَا قِيلَ.
By His names and attributes is a substitute for His saying 'by Allah', and it is possible that it is connected to the assumed reality, and 'He' is its predicate. And 'names' refer to derived words like al-Rahman, al-Raheem, al-'Aleem, al-Qadeer; and 'attributes' are the sources of these derived words like knowledge and power. And 'acceptance of His rulings and laws' may be nominative (marfu') conjoined to 'al-iqrar', or it may be genitive (majrur) conjoined to 'with His names and attributes'. And the condition in it is a summary explanation (bayan ijmalan) as we mentioned: the condition for Islam is a summary explanation of the laws, by saying: everything that Muhammad (SAW) brought is true, and Allah the Exalted with all His attributes is eternal, established, true. And the Prophet (SAW) was content with summary faith (iman ijmal) when he said to a Bedouin who testified to seeing the crescent of Ramadan: 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said yes, so he accepted his testimony and ruled for fasting. And he (SAW) said to a slave girl: 'Where is Allah?' She said: 'In the heaven.' He said: 'Who am I?' She said: 'You are the Messenger of Allah.' So he said: 'Free her, for she is a believer.' And some mashayikh said: detailed description is required, such that if a woman reaches puberty and requests a description of Islam and does not describe it, then she is separated from her husband and it is considered apostasy from her. But there is great difficulty in this, which is not hidden. Therefore, the report of the disbeliever, the sinner, the child, the insane, and one whose heedlessness is intense is not accepted; this is a subdivision of the four conditions without ordering. Thus the disbeliever refers to Islam, the sinner to justice, the child and insane to complete intellect, and the one whose heedlessness is intense to precision. As for the blind, the one who has been flogged for slander, the woman, and the slave: their narration is accepted in hadith due to the existence of the conditions, even if their testimony is not accepted in transactions. This is what is said.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on a matn discussing the conditions for accepting reports (khabar) in Islam. It begins with grammatical analysis of the matn's phrase 'with His names and attributes', explaining it as a substitute for 'by Allah' and connecting it to the assumed reality. It then moves to the concept of summary faith (iman ijmaly), citing two hadiths: the Bedouin who testified to the crescent and the slave girl who knew Allah in heaven. These show that the Prophet (SAW) accepted summary faith without detailed description. However, some mashayikh require detailed description, leading to a difficult consequence of apostasy if a woman cannot describe Islam. The author dismisses this due to hardship. The passage then lists the four conditions for accepting a report: Islam, justice ('adalah), intellect ('aql), and precision (dabt). It applies these conditions: a disbeliever lacks Islam, a sinner lacks justice, a child/insane lacks intellect, and one with intense heedlessness lacks precision. Notably, it states that the blind, a person flogged for slander (after repentance), women, and slaves can have their narration accepted in hadith because these conditions exist in them, but their testimony is not accepted in transactions. This distinction between rivaya (narration) and shahada (testimony) is an important Hanafi principle.

Key Terms
الإيمان الإجمالي (al-iman al-ijmali): Summary faith, affirming that everything brought by Muhammad is true and that Allah exists with all attributes, without detailed exposition.
شروط قبول الخبر (shurut qabul al-khabar): Conditions for accepting a report: Islam, justice ('adalah), intellect ('aql), and precision (dabt).
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision and thoroughness in transmitting reports, ensuring accuracy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which hadith is cited to support the sufficiency of summary faith?
A) The hadith of the Bedouin testifying to the crescent of Ramadan
B) The hadith of the slave girl (narrated by Muslim)
C) Both A and B
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice establishes that summary faith is sufficient for acceptance of Islam, avoiding hardship.

The Four Conditions for Accepting Reports (Rivaya) and the Distinction from Testimony (Shahada)
Listing and applying conditions for rivaya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for accepting a report in hadith (rivaya) and identify which categories of people are accepted in rivaya but not in shahada according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For rivaya, Islam, justice, intellect, and precision suffice; women and slaves are accepted in rivaya even if not in shahada.

The second part of the passage lists the conditions for accepting a report: Islam, justice, intellect, and precision. It then applies these to categories like the blind, the flogged for slander, women, and slaves, explaining why their narrations are accepted even when their testimonies may not be.

Guided Path
1
List the four conditions
The conditions are Islam, justice ('adalah), intellect ('aql), and precision (dabt).
These are the core requirements for rivaya.
2
Apply each condition to the examples
A disbeliever lacks Islam, a sinner lacks justice, a child and insane lack intellect, and one with intense heedlessness lacks precision.
3
Analyze the exceptions
The blind, the flogged for slander (after repentance), women, and slaves still have their rivaya accepted because these conditions exist in them.
The text explicitly states this.
4
Explain the rivaya/shahada distinction
Rivaya (narration) has lighter requirements than shahada (testimony); for example, women and slaves are accepted in rivaya but their testimony is not accepted in transactions.
This is a key Hanafi principle.

باسمَائِهِ وَصفَاتِهِ بَدَل مِنْ قَوْلِهِ بِاللَّهِ وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُتَعَلِّقًا بِالْوَاقِعِ الْمُقَدِّرِ خَيْرًا لَهُوَ وَالإِسْمَاءُ فِى الْمُسْتَقَّاتُ مِنَ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ وَالْعَلِيمِ وَالْقَدِيرِ وَالصَّفَاتُ هِيَ مَبَادِئَ الْمُسْتَقَّاتِ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ وَالْقُدْرَةِ وَقُبُوْلُ أَحْكَامِهِ وَشَرَائِعِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَرْفُوعًا مَعْطَوْفًا عَلى الإِقْرَارِ وَيَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَجْورًا مَعْطَوْفًا عَلى قَوْلِهِ بِأَسْمَائِهِ وَصِفَاتِهِ وَالشَّرْطُ فِيْهِ الْبَيَانُ إِجْمَالاً كَمَا ذَكَرْنَا أَي الشَّرْطُ فِي الإِسْلَامِ بَيَانُ الشَّرَائِعِ إِجْمَالاً بِأَنْ يَقُولَ كُلُّ مَا جَاءَ بِهِ مُحَمَّدٌ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَهُوَ حَقٌّ وَإِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى مَعَ جَمِيعِ صِفَاتِهِ قَدِيمٌ ثَابِتٌ حَقٌّ وَقَدْ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَكْتَفِي بِالإِيْمَانِ الإِجْمَالِي حَيْثُ قَالَ لِلْأَعْرَابِي شَهِدَ بِهِلاَلِ رَمَضَانَ أَتَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلا اللهُ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُوْلُ اللهِ قَالَ نَعَمْ فَقَبِلَ شَهَادَتَهُ وَحَكَمَ بِالصَّوْمِ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ لِجَارِيَةٍ أَيْنَ اللهُ قَالَتْ فِي السَّمَاءِ قَالَ مَنْ أَنَا فَقَالَتْ أَنْتَ رَسُولُ اللهِ فَقَالَ أَعْتِقُوهَا فَإِنَّهَا مُؤْمِنَةٌ وَقَالَ بَعْضُ المَشَائِخِ لابُدَّ مِنَ الْوَصْفِ عَلَى التَّفْصِيْلِ حَتَّى إِذَا بَلَغَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ فَاسْتَوْصَفَتِ الإِسْلَامَ فَلَمْ تَصِفْ فَإِنَّهَا تَبِينُ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا وَجُعِلَ ذَلِكَ رِدَّةً مِنْهَا وَفِيْهِ حَرَجٌ عَظِيمٌ لا يَخْفَى وَلِهَذَا لَا يُقْبَلُ خَبَرُ الْكَافِرِ وَالْفَاسِقِ وَالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَعْتُوهِ وَالَّذِي اشْتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُهُ تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الشَّرُوطِ الأَرْبَعَةِ عَلَى غَيْرِ تَرْتِيْبٍ فَالْكَافِرُ رَاجِعٌ إِلَى الإِسْلَامِ وَالْفَاسِقُ إِلَى الْعَدَالَةِ وَالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَعْتُوْهُ إِلَى كَمَال الْعَقْلِ وَالَّذِي اشْتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُهُ إِلَى الضَّبْطِ وَأَمَّا الأَعْمَى وَالْمَحْدُودُ فِي الْقَذْفِ وَالْمَرْأَةُ وَالْعَبْدُ فَتُقْبَلُ رِوَايَتُهُمْ فِي الْحَدِيثِ لِوُجُودِ الشَّرَائِطِ وَإِنْ لَمْ تُقْبَلْ شَهَادَتُهُمْ فِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ هَكَذَا قِيلَ.
By His names and attributes is a substitute for His saying 'by Allah', and it is possible that it is connected to the assumed reality, and 'He' is its predicate. And 'names' refer to derived words like al-Rahman, al-Raheem, al-'Aleem, al-Qadeer; and 'attributes' are the sources of these derived words like knowledge and power. And 'acceptance of His rulings and laws' may be nominative (marfu') conjoined to 'al-iqrar', or it may be genitive (majrur) conjoined to 'with His names and attributes'. And the condition in it is a summary explanation (bayan ijmalan) as we mentioned: the condition for Islam is a summary explanation of the laws, by saying: everything that Muhammad (SAW) brought is true, and Allah the Exalted with all His attributes is eternal, established, true. And the Prophet (SAW) was content with summary faith (iman ijmal) when he said to a Bedouin who testified to seeing the crescent of Ramadan: 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said yes, so he accepted his testimony and ruled for fasting. And he (SAW) said to a slave girl: 'Where is Allah?' She said: 'In the heaven.' He said: 'Who am I?' She said: 'You are the Messenger of Allah.' So he said: 'Free her, for she is a believer.' And some mashayikh said: detailed description is required, such that if a woman reaches puberty and requests a description of Islam and does not describe it, then she is separated from her husband and it is considered apostasy from her. But there is great difficulty in this, which is not hidden. Therefore, the report of the disbeliever, the sinner, the child, the insane, and one whose heedlessness is intense is not accepted; this is a subdivision of the four conditions without ordering. Thus the disbeliever refers to Islam, the sinner to justice, the child and insane to complete intellect, and the one whose heedlessness is intense to precision. As for the blind, the one who has been flogged for slander, the woman, and the slave: their narration is accepted in hadith due to the existence of the conditions, even if their testimony is not accepted in transactions. This is what is said.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on a matn discussing the conditions for accepting reports (khabar) in Islam. It begins with grammatical analysis of the matn's phrase 'with His names and attributes', explaining it as a substitute for 'by Allah' and connecting it to the assumed reality. It then moves to the concept of summary faith (iman ijmaly), citing two hadiths: the Bedouin who testified to the crescent and the slave girl who knew Allah in heaven. These show that the Prophet (SAW) accepted summary faith without detailed description. However, some mashayikh require detailed description, leading to a difficult consequence of apostasy if a woman cannot describe Islam. The author dismisses this due to hardship. The passage then lists the four conditions for accepting a report: Islam, justice ('adalah), intellect ('aql), and precision (dabt). It applies these conditions: a disbeliever lacks Islam, a sinner lacks justice, a child/insane lacks intellect, and one with intense heedlessness lacks precision. Notably, it states that the blind, a person flogged for slander (after repentance), women, and slaves can have their narration accepted in hadith because these conditions exist in them, but their testimony is not accepted in transactions. This distinction between rivaya (narration) and shahada (testimony) is an important Hanafi principle.

Key Terms
الإيمان الإجمالي (al-iman al-ijmali): Summary faith, affirming that everything brought by Muhammad is true and that Allah exists with all attributes, without detailed exposition.
شروط قبول الخبر (shurut qabul al-khabar): Conditions for accepting a report: Islam, justice ('adalah), intellect ('aql), and precision (dabt).
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision and thoroughness in transmitting reports, ensuring accuracy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is accepted in hadith narration (rivaya) but not in testimony (shahada) in transactions?
A) A free male
B) A woman
C) A just person
D) A blind person

Key Takeaway
The four conditions for rivaya (Islam, justice, intellect, precision) are sufficient; women and slaves are accepted as narrators even if not as witnesses.

Classification of Discontinuity (Inqita') in Hadith: Mursal
Definition of the second division of discontinuity in hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-inqita' and distinguish between its two types: apparent (mursal) and hidden, with an explanation of why the Hanafi school accepts mursal under conditions.

Core Idea
Discontinuity in hadith is of two types: apparent (mursal) and hidden; the Hanafi school accepts the mursal from a reliable tabi'i.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the authority of a hadith depends on the continuity of its chain. This lesson introduces the concept of discontinuity (inqita') and its first subdivision: the apparent discontinuity known as mursal. Understanding this classification is crucial for evaluating which hadith can serve as evidence (dalil) in deriving rulings. We will focus on the definition and the Hanafi stance on accepting mursal reports.

Guided Path
1
Define inqita'
Discontinuity is the lack of a fully connected chain from the Prophet. The passage defines it as 'lack of completion.'
2
Identify the two types
The passage divides inqita' into apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). We focus on the apparent.
3
Explain apparent discontinuity
Apparent discontinuity is the mursal hadith: the narrator (a tabi'i) omits the sahabi intermediary and narrates directly from the Prophet.
4
Distinguish from hidden
Hidden discontinuity refers to subtle defects like tadlis, which are not discussed in this snippet.
Hanafis accept mursal from trustworthy tabi'in; Shafi'is generally require a sahabi mention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالتَّقْسِيْمُ الثَّانِي فِي الاِنْقِطَاعِ أَى عَدَم إِسْنَادِ الحَدِيْثِ بِنَاءً مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ ظَاهِرٌ وَبَاطِنٌ أَمَّا الظَّاهِرُ فَالْمُرْسَلُ مِنَ الأَخْبَارِ بِأَنْ لَا يَذْكُرَ الرَّاوِي الْوَسَائِطَ الَّتِي بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَلْ
The second division concerns discontinuity (inqita'), i.e., lack of completion of a hadith from the Messenger of Allah, and it is of two types: apparent and hidden. As for the apparent, it is the mursal among reports, where the narrator does not mention the intermediaries between himself and the Messenger of Allah, but (text incomplete).
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of discontinuity (inqita') in hadith transmission. It defines inqita' as a break in the isnad such that the hadith cannot be traced back to the Prophet (SAW). The two types are: 1) Apparent (zahir) discontinuity, which is the mursal hadith – where the narrator omits one or more intermediaries between himself and the Prophet. This is a lower level of acceptance in Hanafi usul compared to muttasil (connected) hadith. 2) Hidden (batin) discontinuity, which is not fully defined in the given snippet but refers to more subtle defects (like tadlis). The Hanafi school has its own criteria for accepting mursal hadith under certain conditions.

Key Terms
الانقطاع (al-inqita'): Discontinuity; a break in the isnad such that the hadith is not directly traceable to the Prophet.
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where a tabi'i (successor) narrates directly from the Prophet without mentioning the sahabi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mursal
B) Munqati'
C) Mu'addal
D) Shadh

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, discontinuity in hadith (inqita') is classified into apparent (mursal) and hidden; the mursal from a reliable tabi'i is accepted as valid evidence.

The Four Conditions for Accepting a Narration in Hanafi Usul
Listing categories of people whose reports are not accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for accepting a khabar and distinguish between the standards for riwaya and shahada in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A narrator's report is rejected if he lacks Islam, justice, sanity, or precision—but narration is easier than testimony.

In this passage from *Ashraf al-Anwar*, the author explains the underlying basis for rejecting reports from certain narrators. By identifying four key conditions—Islam, 'adala, kamaal al-'aql, and dabt—we can categorize which narrators are disqualified. Importantly, the passage also highlights a nuance: in hadith narration (riwaya), some reports are accepted even from those whose testimony in legal matters would be rejected. Let's unpack this rule.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Four Conditions
From the passage, identify the four essential qualities that a narrator must possess: Islam, justice ('adala), perfect intellect (kamaal al-'aql), and precision (dabt). These are implied by the disqualifications mentioned.
The passage lists disqualified narrators; each lacks one condition: disbeliever (Islam), sinner ('adala), feebleminded (intellect), extremely negligent (dabt).
2
Match Each Disqualified Narrator to the Missing Condition
For each rejected narrator (kafir, fasiq, jinn, ma'tuh, extremely negligent), determine which of the four conditions is absent. This shows the direct causal link.
Jinn and ma'tuh both fail 'kamaal al-'aql'; the text groups them together.
3
Analyze the Exception for Riwaya
Note that in hadith narration, reports from ummi, repentant slanderer (after tawba), woman, and slave are accepted. This indicates that for riwaya, only the four conditions are required; additional conditions (like freedom or male gender) are not needed.
The text says 'because the conditions are found in them' meaning they possess Islam, 'adala, intellect, and dabt.
4
Distinguish Riwaya from Shahada
Understand that while these narrators are accepted for hadith, their testimony in legal transactions is not accepted. This proves that the standards for shahada are stricter than for riwaya.
Shahada requires additional conditions like freedom and male gender in certain cases.
5
State the Rule Concisely
Formulate the principle: A khabar is accepted if and only if the narrator has Islam, 'adala, kamaal al-'aql, and dabt. In riwaya, these four suffice; in shahada, more conditions apply.
This rule is foundational in Hanafi usul for evaluating hadith and witness testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا لا يُقْبَل خَبَرُ الكَابر : ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ کافر، فاسق، جنی، معتوہ اور وہ شخص جس کی غفلت شدید ہو جائے ان میں سے کسی کی خبر قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے، بغیر ترتیب نے کورہ کا لحاظ کئے مصنف نے تفصیلات کا بیان شروع فرما دیا ہے یعنی شر انکا اربعہ کی غیر مرتب تفریح ہے۔ چنانچہ کافر اسلام کی طرف رائع ہے۔ اور فاسق عدالت کی طرف راجع ہے، اور صمیمی و معتوہ کمال عقل کی طرف رافع ہے اور وہ شخص جس کی بے عقلی و غفلت شدید ہو ضبط کی طرف رافع ہے اور بہر حال امی اور محمد ود فی القذف (توبہ کر لینے کے بعد) اور عورت، غلام کی خبر تو روایت حدیث کے باب میں قبول کرلی جائے گی۔ کیوں کہ شر انکہ ان میں پائی جاتی ہیں ،اگر چہ معاملات میں ان کی گواہیاں معتبر نہ مانی جائیں گی بعض علماء نے اسی طرح کہا ہے۔
And for this reason, the news of a liar is not accepted. This is the reason why the news of a disbeliever, a sinner, a jinn, a feeble-minded person (ma'tuh), and a person who becomes extremely negligent is not accepted. Without considering order, the author has begun explaining the details, i.e., the disordered elaboration of the four conditions. Thus, the disbeliever is disqualified due to [lack of] Islam, the sinner due to [lack of] justice ('adala), the deaf and feeble-minded due to [lack of] perfect intellect, and the person with severe foolishness and negligence due to [lack of] precision (dabt). Nevertheless, the news of an ummi, a person who repented from slander (after repentance), a woman, and a slave is accepted in the context of hadith narration because the conditions are found in them, even though their testimonies are not considered valid in transactions. Some scholars have said the same.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage states a rule in usul al-fiqh regarding the acceptance of akhbar (reports). It explains that a narrator's news is rejected if they lack one of the four essential conditions: Islam, justice ('adala), sanity (kamaal al-'aql), and precision (dabt). The author lists specific categories: disbeliever (fails Islam), sinner (fails justice), jinn and ma'tuh (fail sanity), and extremely negligent (fails precision). However, the text notes an exception: in hadith narration, reports from ummi, repentant slanderer, woman, and slave are accepted because they possess the required conditions even though their testimonies in legal matters are not. This shows that the standards for riwaya (narration) are less strict than for shahada (testimony).

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or narration from a person, especially regarding hadith or testimony.
عدالت (adala): Justice or moral probity; one of the conditions for accepting a narrator's report.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the report of a disbeliever not accepted according to the passage?
A) Because he lacks 'adala
B) Because he lacks Islam
C) Because he lacks sanity
D) Because he lacks dabt

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a khabar in Hanafi usul depends on four conditions: Islam, 'adala, kamaal al-'aql, and dabt, and the standards for hadith narration are more lenient than for testimony.

Types of Mursal Hadith and Their Acceptance in Hanafi Usul
Classifies four types of mursal and discusses acceptance in Hanafi usul, including dispute with Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of mursal hadith and apply the Hanafi rule of acceptance to each type using the qiyas awlawi argument.

Core Idea
A mursal hadith is accepted if the narrator is trustworthy; Hanafis accept it from Companions, Tabi'un, and later generations based on a fortiori reasoning.

Mursal hadith—where a narrator omits the intermediary and says directly 'The Messenger of Allah said'—is a contested topic between madhabs. The Hanafi school classifies mursal into four types and accepts most of them, using a rational argument (qiyas awlawi) about the narrator's trustworthiness. This lesson unpacks that classification and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the passage, list the four types of mursal based on the status of the narrator: Companion, second/third generation, later generation, and mixed transmission.
These categories determine the ruling.
2
Understand acceptance rules
For each category, note the ruling: Companion mursal is accepted by ijma'; Tabi'i/Tabi' al-Tabi'i mursal is accepted by Hanafis but conditionally by Shafi'is; later generation mursal is accepted by Karkhi but rejected by Ibn Aban; mixed transmission is accepted by majority giving precedence to musnad.
The Hanafi view (عندنا) is the focus.
3
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute
Focus on the second type: the Shafi'i objection is that the narrator's identity is unknown (jahalat al-sifat), so the hadith is not a proof. The Hanafi response uses an a fortiori argument: a trustworthy person would not lie about the Prophet, so his direct statement is even more reliable than a full chain.
This is the core ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the a fortiori argument
Use the dalil_block: 'If a narrator is trusted not to lie about an ordinary person, then a fortiori he would not lie about the Prophet.' Derive the acceptance of mursal from a trustworthy narrator.
This is qiyas awlawi (a fortiori analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَقُولُ قَالَ الرَّسُوْلُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَذَا وَهُوَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ لأَنَّهُ إِمَّا أَنْ يُرْسِلَهُ الصَّحَابِي أَوْ يُرْسِلَهُ الْقَرْنُ الثَّانِي وَالثَّالِثُ أَوْ يُرْسِلُهُ مَنْ دُونَهُمْ أَوْ هُوَ مُرْسَلٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ دَوْنَ وَجْهِ وَهُوَ إِنْ كَانَ مِنَ الصَّحَابَى فَمَقْبُولُ بِالإِجْمَاعِ لَأَنْ غَالِبَ حَالِهِ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ مِنْ صَحَابِى آخَرَ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ هُوَ بَنَفْسه حاضرًا جِيْتَلِدٍ [؟] فَإِنْ أَرْسَلَ الصَّحَابِي يَقُولُ قَالَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَذَا وَإِنْ أَسْنَدَ يَقُولُ سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَذَا وَمِنَ الْقَرْنِ الثَّانِي وَالثَّالِثُ كَذَلِكَ عِنْدَنَا أَى مَقْبُول عِنْدَ الْحَنِيفَةَ بِإِنْ يَقُولَ التَّابَعِي أَوْ تَبْعُ التَّابَعِي قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَذَا وَعِنْدَ الشافعي لا يُقْبَلُ لأَنَّهُ إِذَا جَهِلَتْ صِفَاتُ الرَّاوِئ لَمْ يُكُنِ الْحَدِيثُ حُجَّةٌ فَإِذَا جَهِلَت صفَاتُه وَذَاتُهُ فَبا الطريق الأولى إِلَّا إِذَا تَأْيْدَ بِحُجْةٍ قَطْعِيَةٍ أَوْ قَيَاسِ صَحِيحِ أَوْ تَلَقَّتْهُ الأمةُ بَالْقَبُول أَوْ ثَبَتَ إِتْصَالُهُ بَوَجْهِ آخَرَ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ إِنْ كَلامَنَا فِي إِرْسَتَالِ [إرسال] مَنْ لَوْ أسْنَدَهُ إلى شخص آخَرَ يُقْبَلُ وَلا يُظَنُّ بِهِ الكِذَّبَ فَلَأَنْ لَايُظَنُّ بِهِ الْكِذَبَ عَلَى رَسُوْلِ اللهِ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَوْلى بَلْ هُوَ فَوْقَ السَّنَدِ [المسند] لَأَنَّ الْعَدْلَ إِذَا اتَّضَحَ لَهُ طَرِيقَ الإسْنَادِ يَقُولُ بِلا وَسوَسةٍ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ كَذَا وِإِذَا لَمْ يَتَّضِحُ لَهُ ذَالِكَ يَذْكُرُ أَسْمَاءَ الرَّاوِي لِيُعْلِمَهُ مَا تَحْمِلُ عَنْهُ وَيَفْرُغُ ذِمَّتُهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَإِرْسَالَ مَنْ دُونَ هؤلاء بَأَنْ يَقُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ الْقُرُونِ الثَّانِي وَالثَّالِثِ قَالَ النَّبِيُّ كَذَا مَقْبُول كَذَالِكَ عِنْدَ الْكَرْخِي خِلافًا لاِبْنِ أَبَانَ لأَنَّ الزَّمَانَ بَعْدَ القُرُونِ الظَّلَكَةِ [الظلمة] زَمَانُ فِسَبْقِ [فسق] لَمْ يَشْهَدِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِعَدَ إِلَتِهِمْ [بعدالتهم] فَلَا يُقْبَلُ وَالتَّقْسِيمُ الثَّانِي فِي الانْقِطَاع : اور دوسری تقسیم انقطاع ہے یعنی جناب رسول اللہ نے ترجمہ و تشریح سے لیکر ہم تک حدیث کا متصل نہ ہوتا۔ وهو نوعان ظاهر و باطن : ۔ یہ دو قسم پرمشتمل ہے ظاہر و باطن ، ظاہر مرسل احادیث کو کہتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں راوی ان واسطوں کو ذکر نہ کرے جو اس کے اور جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مابین ہیں، بلکہ کہتا ہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا (جناب رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسا فرمایا ہے ) اس کی چار اقسام ہیں۔ کیوں کہ یا صحابی نے مرسل کیا ہے یا قرن ثانی اور ثالث والے نے مرسل کیا ہے، یا ان کے بعد والوں نے مرسل کیا ہے یا وہ روایت ایک طریق سے مرسل اور دوسرے طریق سے غیر مرسل ہے۔ (یعنی مسند ہے) وَهُوَإنْ كَانَ مِنَ الصحابی ۔ پس اگر مرسل صحابی کی ہو تو بالاتفاق مقبول ہے کیوں کہ غالب احوال یہ ہے کہ حضرت صحابی رضی اللہ عنہ نے خود بطہ جناب رسول اللہ ہے ہے اگر چہ احتمال اس کا بھی ہے کہ ان صحابی نے دوسرے صحابی سے سنا ہو اور خود بنفس تھیں جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی مجلس میں حاضر نہ رہے ہوں۔ اس صورت میں اگر صحابی نے رسل کیا اور کہتا ہے، کہ قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا ( جناب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسے فرمایا) اور اگر مند کیا اور کہتا ہے کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے سنا۔ یا کہتا ہے حدثني رسول الله رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مجھے سے اس طرح بیان فرمایا کہ وَمِنَ القَرْنِ الثاني والثالث:۔ اور قرن ثانی اور ثالث کا مرسل بھی ہمارے نزدیک اس طرح مقبول ہے۔ یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان کا مرسل قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک قبول نہ کیا جائے گا کیونکہ جب راوی کی صفات دار صاف مجہول ہوں تو حدیث محنت نہیں ہوتی تو جب ذات اور صفات دونوں کے دونوں مجہول ہوں تو بدرجہ اولی قیبت نہ ہو گی۔ ہاں البتہ جبکوئی فی تعلیمی اس کی تائید کرے یا قیاس صحیح تائید کرے یالت نے اس کو قبول کر لیا ہو۔ یا اس حدیث کا اتصال دوسری سند سے ثابت ہو تو قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ وَنَحْنُ نَقُول اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ہماری گفتگو اس شخص کے ارسال کرنے میں ہے کہ اگر وہ دوسرے رادی کی طرف سند کر دے تو قبول کی جاتی ہے اور اس سے کذب کا کوئی مہمان نہیں کیا جاتا ہے جب صورت حال یہ ہے تو بطریق اولی اس کے بارے میں رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر جھوٹ بولنے کا مان نہ کیا جائے گا۔ (کیونکہ جب وہ غیر رسول کی طرف جھوٹ کی نسبت کرنے سے ڈرتا ہے۔ تو رسول اللہ کی طرف نسبت کرنے سے بطریق اولی خوف کرے گا بلکہ یہ قسم مسند حدیث سے فوقیت رکھتی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ عادل آدمی کے لئے جب طریق اسناد و اضح ہوتا ہے تو بلا وسوسہ کے قول کو حضور کی جانب منسوب کر دیتا ہے کہ حضور نے یہ فرمایا۔ من قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ كَذا: اور اگر طریق استاد واضح نہیں ہوتا تو راوی کا نام ذکر کر دیتا ہے تاکہ اپنا ذمہ اس راوی پر ڈال سکہ ۔ جس سے اس نے روایت لی ہے اور خود اس کا ذمہ اس سے فارغ ہو جائے۔ وَارْسالُ مَن دُونَ هولاء :۔ اور ان سے نیچے (بعد والے) راویوں کا مرسل مثلا وہ لوگ جو قرن ثانی د ثالث کے بعد کے ہیں۔ کہتے ہیں قَالَ النَّبِيِّ كَذَا مَقْبُول كَذَالِكَ عِنْدَ الْكَرْخِي تو امام کرخی کے نزدیک اس طرح مقبول ہے مگر عیسی ابن ابان اس کے خلاف ہیں کیوں کہ قرون ثلاث کے بعد کا زمان فیش اینجور کا زمانہ ہے۔ جناب نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کی عدالت کی شہادت نہیں دی ہے لہذا ان کی مرسل حدیث قبول نہ کی جائے گی۔ وَالَّذِي أَرْسَلَ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَاسْتَنَدَ مِنْ وَجْهِ مَقْبُول عِنْدَ الْعَامَّةِ كَصَدِيث لا نكاح الا بولِيِّ رَوَاهُ إِسْرَائِيلُ بْنُ يُونُسَ مُسْتَنِدًا وَسُعْبَةَ [شعبة] مُرْسَلاً فَيَغْلِبُ اسْتِنَادُهُ عَلَى إِرْسَالِهِ وَقِيلَ لا يُقْبَلُ لِأَنَّ الِاسْتِنَادَ كَالتَّعْدِيلِ وَالإرْسَالَ كَالْجَرْحِ وَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَ الْجَرْحُ وَالتَّعْدِيلُ يَغْلِبُ الْجَرْحُ وَأَمَّا الْبَاطِنُ فَنَوْعَانِ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ الِاتِّصَالُ فِيهِ
He says: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such.' And it has four divisions, because either the Companion sends it, or the second or third generation sends it, or someone after them sends it, or it is mursal from one path and [musnad] from another. If it is from a Companion, it is accepted by consensus, because most often he heard it himself from him, peace be upon him, even though it is possible that he heard from another Companion and was not himself present at [؟]. So if the Companion sends it, he says: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such.' And if he gives it with a chain, he says: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say such-and-such.' And [mursal] from the second and third generation is similarly accepted in our view, i.e., accepted according to the Hanafis, when the Tabi'i or the follower of the Tabi'i says: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such.' But according to al-Shafi'i, it is not accepted because when the qualities of the narrator are unknown, the hadith is not a proof. So when both his qualities and his identity are unknown, then a fortiori [it is not accepted] unless it is supported by a conclusive proof, or sound analogy, or the ummah received it with acceptance, or its continuity is established through another path. And we say: Our discussion concerns the mursal of one who, if he attributed it to another person, would be accepted, and lying is not suspected of him. So it is even more [obvious] that lying against the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, is not suspected of him. Rather, it is above the musnad, because an upright person, when the path of attribution is clear to him, he says without hesitation: 'He, peace be upon him, said such-and-such.' And when that is not clear to him, he mentions the names of the narrators to inform [the listener] what he heard from him and to discharge his responsibility. And the mursal of those below these [the later generations], i.e., one from after the second and third generations says: 'The Prophet said such-and-such' - it is accepted similarly according to al-Karkhi, contrary to Ibn Aban, because the time after those generations is a time of darkness and transgression; the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not testify to their uprightness, so it is not accepted. And the second division regarding discontinuity: The discontinuity, meaning from the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, from translation and commentary to us, the hadith is not continuous. It is of two types: apparent and hidden. The apparent is called mursal hadiths, i.e., in that case the narrator does not mention the intermediaries between him and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, but says: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such.' It has four divisions. Because either the Companion sent it, or the second or third generation sent it, or those after them sent it, or the narration is mursal in one way and not mursal (i.e., musnad) in another. And if it is from the Companion: So if the mursal is from the Companion, it is accepted unanimously, because the usual case is that the Companion himself heard from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, although it is possible that that Companion heard from another Companion and himself was not present in the assembly of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. In this case, if the Companion sent it and said, 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such,' and if he gave it with an attribution, he says, 'I heard from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him,' or he says, 'The Messenger of Allah narrated to me thus.' And from the second and third generation: The mursal of the second and third generation is also accepted in our view similarly. That is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, their mursal will be accepted. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, it will not be accepted, because when the attributes of the narrator are unknown, the hadith is not a proof. So when both identity and attributes are unknown, a fortiori it will not be accepted. Except when some decisive proof supports it, or sound analogy supports it, or the ummah has accepted it, or the continuity of this hadith is established through another chain, then it will be accepted. And we say: Our discussion concerns the mursal of a person who, if he were to attribute it to another narrator, it would be accepted, and lying is not suspected of him. So when this is the case, a fortiori lying against the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, will not be suspected of him. (Because when he fears attributing a lie to someone else, a fortiori he will fear attributing it to the Messenger of Allah.) Rather, this type has precedence over musnad hadith, because for a just person, when the method of attribution is clear, he ascribes the statement to the Prophet without hesitation, saying: 'He said such-and-such.' And if the method of attribution is not clear, he mentions the name of the narrator so that he can discharge his responsibility onto that narrator from whom he took the narration, and his own responsibility is freed. And 'the mursal of those below these': The mursal of narrators below these (later ones), e.g., those who are after the second and third generations, they say: 'The Prophet said such-and-such' - it is accepted similarly according to Imam al-Karkhi. Imam al-Karkhi accepts it, but 'Isa ibn Aban opposes, because the time after the three generations is a time of transgression and corruption. The Prophet, peace be upon him, did not testify to their uprightness, so their mursal hadith will not be accepted. And the one who is mursal from one path and musnad from another is accepted by the majority, like the hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian' narrated by Isra'il ibn Yunus as musnad and by Shu'bah as mursal, so its musnad version overrides its mursal version. And some say it is not accepted, because attribution (isnad) is like tazkiyah (declaring uprightness) and mursal is like jarh (impugning), and when jarh and tazkiyah conflict, jarh prevails. And as for the hidden [discontinuity], it is of two types: that the continuity is in it...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar is a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, presenting the Hanafi classification of mursal (disconnected) hadith. It begins by stating that mursal is of four types: (1) mursal from a Companion (sahabi), (2) mursal from the second or third generation (tabi'i and tabi' al-tabi'i), (3) mursal from later generations, and (4) a hadith that is mursal through one chain but musnad (connected) through another. The passage then explains each type. The first type—mursal from a Companion—is accepted by scholarly consensus (ijma') because it is the norm that a Companion heard directly from the Prophet, even though it is possible he heard it from another Companion. If he sends it with the direct formula 'said the Messenger of Allah,' it is accepted; if he gives a chain, he uses a hearing formula. The second type—mursal from a tabi'i or tabi' al-tabi'i—is accepted by the Hanafis (specifically Imam Abu Hanifa) but rejected by al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi argument is that if such a narrator is trustworthy enough that his attribution to another person would be accepted, then his direct statement about the Prophet is even more reliable; a just person would not lie about the Prophet more so than about others. Al-Shafi'i's objection is that since the narrator's identity and characteristics are unknown (the intermediary is omitted), the hadith lacks the required verification; however, if supported by a decisive proof, sound analogy, general acceptance, or another chain, it becomes acceptable. The third type—mursal from someone after the first three centuries—is accepted by Imam al-Karkhi but rejected by 'Isa ibn Aban, because those later times are considered corrupt (zaman fasiq), and the Prophet did not testify to their uprightness. The fourth type—a hadith that is mursal in one transmission and musnad in another, like the famous hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian' (narrated by Isra'il as musnad and by Shu'bah as mursal)—the majority (jumhur) accept it, giving precedence to the musnad version. However, a minority argue that the mursal version is like a jarh (impugnment) and the musnad like a ta'dil (declaration of uprightness), and jarh takes precedence over ta'dil. The passage also introduces the concept of discontinuity (inqita') being of two types: apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). The apparent discontinuity is the mursal just discussed; the hidden discontinuity will be explained later.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits the intermediary between himself and the Prophet, saying directly 'The Messenger of Allah said.'
إرسال (irsal): The act of a narrator transmitting a hadith without mentioning the intermediary (i.e., as mursal).
صحابي (sahabi): A person who met the Prophet Muhammad as a believer and died as a Muslim.
قرن ثاني وثالث (qarn thani wa thalith): The second and third generations after the Prophet: the Tabi'un (followers) and Tabi' al-Tabi'in (followers of followers).
كرخي (Karkhi): Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH), a prominent Hanafi jurist, who accepted mursal even from later generations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is a mursal hadith from a trustworthy tabi'i accepted even without a full chain?
A) Because the tabi'i was always present with the Prophet.
B) Because a just person who would not lie about another person is even less likely to lie about the Prophet.
C) Because all mursal hadiths are mutawatir.
D) Because the tabi'i's memory is infallible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts mursal hadith from trustworthy narrators based on an a fortiori argument that a just person would not lie about the Prophet.
