Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Acceptance of Mursal Hadith: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Usul rule on acceptance of mursal hadith with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which Hanafis accept mursal hadith and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principles from the passage.

Core Idea
Hanafis accept mursal from trustworthy narrators of early generations; Shafi'is require a complete chain.

Mursal hadith—where a narrator omits the Companion and directly quotes the Prophet—has been a point of contention between schools. This passage lays out the Hanafi position that such narrations from upright narrators of the early generations are acceptable, while the Shafi'i school insists on a fully connected chain. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to evaluate hadith evidence in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define mursal and its categories
First, understand what mursal means and the different types: from a Companion (accepted by consensus), from the second and third generations (tabi'in and their followers, disputed), and from later generations (dispute among Hanafis themselves).
The text explicitly mentions three tiers: Companions, second/third generations, and later generations.
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa) accepts mursal from trustworthy narrators of the second and third generations. Their reasoning: an upright person would not lie about the Prophet; if unsure, he would name his source. This is an a fortiori argument (qiyas).
The passage states: 'when he fears attributing a lie to a non-Messenger, then by stronger reason he will fear attributing to the Messenger.'
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i rejects such mursal unless supported by another evidence. His reasoning: the narrator's attributes are unknown, so the hadith is unacceptable. Unknown identity and attributes make the narration even more doubtful.
The text quotes the Shafi'i argument: 'when the narrator's attributes are unknown, the hadith is not accepted.'
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that their discussion is about the narrator who does name his source when the chain is unclear, indicating carefulness. They argue that such a narrator is even more reliable than one who always gives an isnad, because he avoids attributing directly to the Prophet without certainty.
The passage says: 'this type is superior to the musnad hadith. Because for an upright person, when the method of chain is clear, he attributes the saying to the Prophet without doubt.'
5
Consider exceptions and intra-Hanafi disagreement
The text notes exceptions: if the mursal is supported by another evidence, analogy, majority acceptance, or another chain, even Shafi'is accept it. Also, among later Hanafis, al-Karkhi accepts mursal from later generations while Isa ibn Aban rejects due to deterioration of moral standards.
Also note the case of conflicting transmissions: when a hadith is mursal from one chain and musnad from another, the majority treats the musnad as overriding, but some apply the rule that jarh (impugnment) prevails over ta'dil (declaration of reliability).

Source Text

الله عليه وسلم نے مجھے سے اس طرح بیان فرمایا[ وَمِنَ القَرْنِ الثاني والثالث:۔ اور قرن ثانی اور ثالث کا مرسل بھی ہمارے نزدیک اس طرح مقبول ہے۔ یعنی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان کا مرسل قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک قبول نہ کیا جائے گا کیونکہ جب راوی کی صفات [غیر] صاف مجہول ہوں تو حدیث [مقبول] نہیں ہوتی تو جب ذات اور صفات دونوں کے دونوں مجہول ہوں تو بدرجہ اولی [مقبول] نہ ہو گی۔ ہاں البتہ جبکوئی [دلیل] اس کی تائید کرے یا قیاس صحیح تائید کرے یا [جمہور] نے اس کو قبول کر لیا ہو۔ یا اس حدیث کا اتصال دوسری سند سے ثابت ہو تو قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ وَنَحْنُ نَقُول اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ہماری گفتگو اس شخص کے ارسال کرنے میں ہے کہ اگر وہ دوسرے [راوی] کی طرف [اسناد] کر دے تو قبول کی جاتی ہے اور اس سے کذب کا کوئی [گمان] نہیں کیا جاتا ہے جب صورت حال یہ ہے تو بطریق اولی اس کے بارے میں رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر جھوٹ بولنے کا [گمان] نہ کیا جائے گا۔ (کیونکہ جب وہ غیر رسول کی طرف جھوٹ کی نسبت کرنے سے ڈرتا ہے۔ تو رسول اللہ کی طرف نسبت کرنے سے بطریق اولی خوف کرے گا بلکہ یہ قسم مسند حدیث سے فوقیت رکھتی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ عادل آدمی کے لئے جب طریق اسناد واضح ہوتا ہے تو بلا وسوسہ کے قول کو حضور کی جانب منسوب کر دیتا ہے کہ حضور نے یہ فرمایا۔ من قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ كَذا: اور اگر طریق اسناد واضح نہیں ہوتا تو راوی کا نام ذکر کر دیتا ہے تاکہ اپنا ذمہ اس راوی پر ڈال سکے ۔ جس سے اس نے روایت لی ہے اور خود اس کا ذمہ اس سے فارغ ہو جائے۔ وَارْسالُ مَن دُونَ هولاء :۔ اور ان سے نیچے (بعد والے) راویوں کا مرسل مثلا وہ لوگ جو قرن ثانی و ثالث کے بعد کے ہیں۔ کہتے ہیں قَالَ النَّبِيِّ كَذَا مَقْبُول كَذَالِكَ عِنْدَ الْكَرْخی تو امام کرخی کے نزدیک اس طرح مقبول ہے مگر عیسی ابن ابان اس کے خلاف ہیں کیوں کہ قرون ثلاث کے بعد کا زمان [فیش و فجور] کا زمانہ ہے۔ جناب نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کی عدالت کی شہادت نہیں دی ہے لہذا ان کی مرسل حدیث قبول نہ کی جائے گی۔ وَالَّذِي أَرْسَلَ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَاسْتَنَدَ مِنْ وَجْهِ مَقْبُول عِنْدَ الْعَامَّةِ كَصَدِيث لا نكاح الا [بولي] رَوَاهُ إِسْرَائِيلُ بْنُ يُونُسَ مُسْتَنِدًا وَشُعْبَةَ مُرْسَلاً فَيَغْلِبُ [الاستناد] على [الارسال] وَقِيلَ لا يُقْبَلُ لأَن الاستنَادَ كَالتُعْدِيلِ وَالإرْسالَ كَالجرح واذا اجتمع الْجَرْحُ وَالتَّعَدِيلِ يَغْلِبُ الْجَرْحُ
If it is from the Companion: So if the mursal is from a Companion, it is accepted by consensus because the dominant situation is that the Companion himself heard from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, although it is possible that the Companion heard from another Companion and was not present in the assembly of the Messenger. In that case, if the Companion [mursal] and says 'The Messenger of Allah said such-and-such' and if [musnad] and says 'I heard from the Messenger of Allah' or 'The Messenger of Allah narrated to me.' And from the second and third generation: The mursal of the second and third generation is also accepted in our view. That is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, their mursal is accepted, but according to Imam al-Shafi'i it is not accepted because when the narrator's attributes are unknown, the hadith is not accepted, so when both his identity and attributes are unknown, it is even more so not accepted. However, if some [evidence] supports it, or a correct analogy supports it, or the [majority] has accepted it, or the continuity of the hadith is established through another chain, then it is accepted. And we say: Our discussion is about the one who [mursal]; if he [chains] to another [narrator], it is accepted and no suspicion of lying is attached. Since the situation is such, then by stronger reason, he will not be suspected of lying about the Messenger of Allah. (Because when he fears attributing a lie to a non-Messenger, then by stronger reason he will fear attributing to the Messenger. Rather, this type is superior to the musnad hadith. Because for an upright person, when the method of chain is clear, he attributes the saying to the Prophet without doubt: 'The Prophet said such.' And if the method of chain is not clear, he mentions the narrator's name to shift responsibility to that narrator from whom he took the narration, and his own responsibility is discharged.) And the mursal of those below these: i.e., the mursal of narrators after the second and third generation, saying 'The Prophet said such' is accepted according to Imam al-Karkhi, but Isa ibn Aban disagrees because the time after the three generations is a time of immorality. The Prophet, peace be upon him, did not testify to their uprightness, so their mursal hadith is not accepted. And that which is mursal from one chain and musnad from another chain is accepted by the majority, like the hadith 'There is no marriage except with a guardian' narrated by Isra'il ibn Yunus as musnad and by Shu'bah as mursal, so the [musnad] overcomes the [mursal]. And it is said that it is not accepted because musnad is like ta'dil (declaration of reliability) and mursal is like jarh (impugning), and when jarh and ta'dil combine, jarh prevails.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about the acceptance of mursal hadith (hadith with a missing link in the chain of narration). It begins by stating that mursal from a Companion is accepted by consensus because the Companion is presumed to have heard directly from the Prophet, even if there is a possibility he heard from another Companion. The text then discusses mursal from the second and third generations (tabi'in and their followers). The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) accepts their mursal, while Imam al-Shafi'i rejects it unless supported by another evidence. The Hanafi argument is that a trustworthy narrator would not intentionally misattribute, and if he were unsure, he would name his source. The text then considers mursal from later generations: Imam al-Karkhi accepts it, but Isa ibn Aban rejects it due to the prevalence of immorality after the first three centuries. Finally, it covers the case of a hadith transmitted as mursal from one chain and musnad from another: the majority accepts the musnad version as outweighing the mursal, while some argue that mursal (jarh) should prevail over musnad (ta'dil) based on the principle of jarh overriding ta'dil.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits the Companion and directly quotes the Prophet, or where a link is missing.
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete, connected chain of narrators up to the Prophet.
إسناد (isnad): The chain of narrators; attributing the hadith to a specific source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under what condition is a mursal hadith from the second generation (tabi'i) accepted?
A) Only if supported by another hadith
B) Only if it contradicts a rational proof
C) Generally accepted because the narrator is presumed trustworthy
D) It is never accepted

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts mursal hadith from trustworthy narrators of the early generations, based on the presumption that upright people do not fabricate attributions to the Prophet.

Internal Defects (Batin) in Hadith: Criteria for Rejection
Explains hidden defects that render a hadith rejected despite apparent continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify internal defects in a hadith (narrator deficiency vs. contradiction with superior evidence) and apply these criteria to determine whether a hadith is rejected in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A hadith with a connected chain may still be rejected due to a hidden defect: narrator weakness or contradiction with Quran, well-known Sunnah, or established practice.

A hadith may appear sound on the surface but contain a hidden flaw that makes it unacceptable as evidence. In this lesson, we explore the two categories of internal defects (batin) identified by Hanafi usul scholars: defects related to the transmitter and defects arising from contradiction with superior sources. Understanding these criteria is essential for evaluating hadith properly, especially when they conflict with established rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of batin defects
The text states that internal defects are of two kinds: first, a deficiency in the narrator (such as disbelief, sin, childhood, or negligence) that violates the conditions of narrators; second, a contradiction (mukhalafa) with a superior evidence (dalil fa'iq). Note that the first type has been covered previously; this lesson focuses on the second.
The second type is further subdivided into four subtypes based on what is contradicted.
2
Examine each subtype of contradiction
The text provides four examples: (a) contradiction with the Quran, e.g., the hadith 'No prayer without al-Fatiha' versus the general command to recite what is easy; (b) contradiction with well-known Sunnah, e.g., the hadith on touching the penis requiring wudu versus the practice of the Companions; (c) contradiction with well-known practice (amal), e.g., the hadith of audible basmala in prayer contravening continuous practice; (d) abandonment by early scholars, e.g., the hadith about zakat on orphan's wealth ignored by Companions.
Each example illustrates how a hadith can be rejected despite an apparent connected chain.
3
Understand the concept of 'superior evidence' (dalil fa'iq)
The superior evidence can be the Quran, a well-known Sunnah (hadith mutawatir or mashhur), or a well-known practice (amal mustamirr) that was continuously observed from the Prophet's time. When a solitary hadith contradicts such evidence, the solitary hadith is rejected or interpreted allegorically to resolve the conflict.
Hanafi usul places great weight on 'amal' as a criterion, especially in matters of worship.
4
Apply the criteria to a new hadith example
Given a hadith that appears to have a sound chain but contradicts a well-known practice, determine whether it is rejected based on the principles above. For instance, a hadith stating that raising hands in prayer after takbir is recommended contradicts the established Hanafi practice of not raising hands in every movement.
Practice this analysis to develop the skill of applying these criteria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْبَاطِنُ فَنْوَعَانِ: أَنْ يَكُونَ الْاتِّصَالُ فِيهِ ظَاهِرًا وَلَكِن وَقَعَ الْخَلَلُ بِوَجْهِ آخَرَ وَهُوَ فَقْدُ شُرُوطِ الرَّاوِي أَوْ مُخَالَفَتُهُ لِدَلِيلٍ فَائِقٍ فَإِنْ كَانَ لِنُقْصَانٍ فِي النَّاقِلِ فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا مِنْ عَدَمِ قَبُوْلِ خَبَرِ الْكَافِرِ وَالْفَاسِقِ وَالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمُغَفَّلِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِالْعَرْضِ بِأَنْ خَالَفَ الْكِتَابَ كَحَدِيْثِ لَا صَلَاةَ إِلَّا بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ يُخَالِفُ لِعُمُومِ قَوْلِهِ فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ وَكَحَدِيْثِ مَنْ مَسَّ ذَكَرَهُ فَلْيَتَوَضَّا يُخَالِفُ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى فِيْهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَدْحِ قَوْمٍ يَسْتَنْجُونَ بِالْمَاءِ وَفِيْهِ مَسُّ الذَّكَرِ أَوِ السُّنَّةِ الْمَعْرُوفَةِ كَحَدِيْثِ الْقَضَاءِ بِشَاهِدٍ وَيَمِينٍ يُخَالِفُ قَوْلَهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ الْبَيِّنَةُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعِي وَالْيَمِينُ عَلَى مَنْ أَنْكَرَ وَهُوَ مَشْهُورٌ أَوِ الْحَادِثَةِ الْمَشْهُورَةِ كَحَدِيْثِ الْجَهْرِ بِالتَّسْمِيَةِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الَّذِي رَوَاهُ أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ فَإِنَّ حَادِثَةَ الصَّلَاةِ مَشْهُورَةٌ مُسْتَمِرَّةٌ كَانَ يُحْفِرُهَا أُلُوفٌ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ وَلَمْ يَسْمَعِ التَّسْمِيَةَ إِلَّا أَبُو هُرَيْرَةَ وَهَذَا شَيْءٌ عَجِيْبٌ أَوْ أَعْرَضَ عَنْهُ الْأَئِمَّةُ مِنَ الصَّدْرِ الْأَوَّلِ يَعْنِي أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ إِذَا تَكَلَّمُوا فِيْمَا بَيْنَهُمْ فِي وُجُوبِ الزَّكَاةِ عَلَى الصَّبِيِّ بِالرَّأْيِ وَلَمْ يَلْتَفِتُوا إِلَى قَوْلِهِ ابْتَغُوا فِي مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ خَيْرًا كَيْلًا تَأْكُلَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ فَعَلِمَ أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ ثَابِتٍ أَوْ مُؤَوَّلٌ بِتَأْوِيلٍ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالصَّدَقَةِ النَّفَقَةُ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ نَفَقَةُ الْمَرْءِ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ صَدَقَةٌ كَانَ مَرْدُودًا مُنْقَطِعًا أَيْضًا جَوَابُ إِنْ يَكُونُ الْخَبَرُ فِي كُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْمَوَاضِعِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ مَرْدُودًا كَمَا فِي النَّوْعِ الْأَوَّلِ
As for the internal defect, it is of two types: that the continuity is apparent but a defect occurred in another manner, namely the lack of conditions of the narrator or its contradiction with a superior evidence. If it is due to a deficiency in the transmitter, then it is as we mentioned: the non-acceptance of the report of a disbeliever, a sinner, a child, and a careless person. And if it is due to contradiction: either with the Book, like the hadith 'There is no prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' which contradicts the general meaning of His saying 'Recite what is easy of the Quran'; and like the hadith 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu' which contradicts His saying 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' because it is praising people who perform istinja with water, and touching the penis is mentioned; or with the well-known Sunnah, like the hadith of judgment with one witness and an oath which contradicts his saying 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the denier' and it is well-known; or with the well-known practice, like the hadith of saying the basmala aloud in prayer narrated by Abu Hurayrah, for the practice of prayer is well-known and continuous, thousands of men observed it but only Abu Hurayrah heard the basmala, which is something strange; or that the imams of the first generation turned away from it, meaning that when the Companions discussed among themselves regarding the obligation of zakat on a child by opinion and did not pay attention to his saying 'Seek out good in the wealth of the orphan lest charity consumes it', then it is known that it is not established, or it is interpreted to mean that charity means spending on him, as he said 'A man's spending on himself is charity', then it is rejected and disconnected. So the answer is that the hadith in each of these four contexts is rejected as in the first type.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage explains internal defects (batin) in hadith that render it rejected despite an apparently connected chain. The author classifies defects into two categories: first, a defect in the narrator himself (such as being a disbeliever, sinner, child, or negligent person), in which case the hadith is rejected based on earlier rules. Second, a defect in the content of the hadith due to contradiction with a stronger evidence. The text then provides four examples: (1) Contradiction with the Quran: the hadith that prayer is invalid without al-Fatiha contradicts the general Quranic command to recite what is easy. (2) Contradiction with the well-known Sunnah: the hadith that touching the penis requires wudu contradicts the practice of the Companions who understood the verse about purification to refer to istinja with water, not to touching. (3) Contradiction with well-known practice: the hadith that the basmala should be recited aloud in prayer is contradicted by the continuous practice of thousands who observed the Prophet's prayer and did not report that, only Abu Hurayrah did. (4) Abandonment by early scholars: the Companions did not consider the hadith about zakat on the orphan's wealth as binding, interpreting it differently. In all these cases, the hadith is deemed rejected.

Key Terms
باطن (batin): A hidden defect in a hadith that makes it unacceptable despite an apparent connected chain
مخالفة لدليل فائق (mukhalafa li-dalil fa'iq): Contradiction with a superior evidence (Quran, well-known Sunnah, or well-known practice) that leads to rejection
حادثة مشهورة (haditha mashhura): A well-known continuous practice (amal) that was observed by the community from the Prophet's time; used as a criterion to judge hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a reason for rejecting a hadith due to internal defect?
A) Contradiction with the Quran
B) Contradiction with well-known Sunnah
C) Contradiction with a mathematical proof
D) Abandonment by early scholars

Key Takeaway
A hadith may appear to have a connected chain but still be rejected in Hanafi usul if it has a hidden defect, especially if it contradicts a superior evidence such as Quran, well-known Sunnah, or established practice.

Ruling on a Hadith Transmitted as Mursal from One Chain and Musnad from Another
Explains the acceptance of a hadith with mixed chain status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a musnad chain overrides a mursal chain when evaluating a hadith transmitted through both, and critically assess the counter-argument based on the principle of jarh outweighing ta'dil.

Core Idea
When a hadith is musnad from one chain, it overrides any mursal chain, making the hadith acceptable.

In Hanafi usul, the status of a hadith's chain is critical. This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a hadith narrated through two chains, one mursal (disconnected) and one musnad (connected). The majority of Hanafi scholars accept such a hadith because the connected chain is considered stronger. However, a minority objection exists. By studying this rule and the example of the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi wali', you will learn how to weigh conflicting chain transmissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of hadith
Recognize that the hadith has two transmissions: one mursal (disconnected at the Companion level) and one musnad (fully connected).
2
Recall the Hanafi rule
A hadith that is musnad from any chain is considered strong; if also mursal from another chain, the musnad chain prevails and the hadith is accepted.
This is the majority view (jumhur).
3
Examine the basis of the rule
The musnad chain provides ta'dil (positive evaluation) for the continuity, while mursal is like a flaw. In jarh wa ta'dil, specific criticism (jarh) usually outweighs praise, but here the musnad chain is a specific positive that overcomes the general flaw of irsal.
The principle: 'isnad is ta'dil, irsal is like jarh; but when a specific musnad chain exists, it outweighs.'
4
Analyze the counter-argument
Some scholars argue that irsal is like jarh, so the hadith should be rejected because jarh outweighs ta'dil.
They treat the mursal chain as a specific defect.
5
Apply the rule to the example
In the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi wali', Isra'il ibn Yunas narrated it as musnad, Shu'bah as mursal. The musnad chain overrides, so the hadith is accepted as proof.
This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَّذِى أرسلَ مِن وَجْهِ وَأُسئِدَ مِنْ وَجْه اور وہ حدیث جو ایک سند سے مرسل ہو اور ترجمه و تشریح دوسر کی سند سے مسند ہو۔ اکثر کے نزدیک مقبول ہے۔ جیسے حديث لا نكاح الأ بولي (ول کے بغیر نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوتا ) اس کو اسرائیل بن یونس نے مسند آروایت کیا ہے۔ اور حضرت شعبہ نے مرسلا روایت کیا ہے لہذا ان کی اسناد حضرت شعبہ کی ارسال پر غالب ہو گئی۔ بعض نے کہا ہے کہ قبول نہ کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اسناد کا درجہ تعدیل کا ہے اور ارسال مجروح کے مانند ہے اور جب جرح اور تعدیل ایک روایت میں اور جمع ہوں گے تو جرح غالب ہو جاتا ہے۔
And that which is sent (mursal) from one aspect and connected (musnad) from another aspect: and that hadith which is mursal from one chain and musnad from another chain. According to most, it is accepted. For example, the hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian' was narrated by Isra'il ibn Yunus as musnad, and by Shu'bah as mursal, so the isnad of Isra'il overrides the irsal of Shu'bah. Some have said it is not accepted, because the status of isnad is ta'dil, and irsal is like being majruh, and when jarh and ta'dil are combined, jarh prevails.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a hadith that is narrated through two chains, one mursal (disconnected) and one musnad (connected). The author states that the majority of scholars consider such a hadith acceptable because the connected chain strengthens it. An example is the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi wali' narrated by Isra'il ibn Yunus as musnad and by Shu'bah as mursal. The argument is that the musnad chain is deemed stronger, similar to how ta'dil outweighs jarh in a narrator. However, a minority argue that irsal is like a flaw, and jarh outweighs ta'dil, so the hadith is rejected. The Hanafi position aligns with the majority view, accepting such hadith as proof in legal matters.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the chain is disconnected at the Companion level, usually missing the Companion from the Prophet.
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete, connected chain going back to the Prophet.
جرح و تعدیل (jarh wa ta'dil): Criticism and praise of narrators; jarh makes a narrator unreliable, ta'dil establishes reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the ruling on a hadith that is mursal from one chain and musnad from another?
A) It is rejected because irsal is a defect.
B) It is accepted because the musnad chain overrides the mursal.
C) It is accepted only if the mursal chain is from a reliable narrator.
D) It is rejected unless the mursal chain is from the Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
A hadith that is musnad from one chain is accepted even if mursal from another; the musnad chain outweighs.

First Internal Defect: Deficiency in the Narrator
Defines internal defect due to narrator deficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four narrator types whose deficiency leads to hadith rejection according to the Hanafi school, and explain the legal consequence.

Core Idea
A hadith with a deficient narrator is rejected even if its chain appears connected.

In this lesson, we examine the first category of internal defect in hadith: a hidden flaw that arises from the narrator's failure to meet the conditions of acceptance. The author explains that even if a hadith appears outwardly sound, if the narrator is a disbeliever, sinner, child, or heedless person, the report cannot be accepted. We will parse this definition and understand its implications for hadith authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context
The passage defines the first type of internal defect (khalal baatin) in hadith criticism. It contrasts with external defects like a broken chain.
2
Identify the cause
The defect arises from a deficiency in the narrator (naqisan fi al-naqil). The narrator lacks one or more essential conditions for acceptance.
The condition of the narrator is a hidden aspect, not apparent from the chain alone.
3
List the four deficient narrator types
The passage specifically names four types: kafir (disbeliever), fasiq (sinner), sabi (child), and mughaffal (heedless).
These are the primary categories mentioned; other schools may have additional types.
4
Understand the consequence
The hadith is rejected (mardud) and cannot be used as proof in legal rulings. This is a ruling of non-acceptance.
Rejection here means the hadith is not considered a valid source of law.
5
Connect to earlier principles
This reiterates earlier rulings on narrator conditions: a narrator must be Muslim, just, adult, and attentive (ضابط).
Hanafi usul emphasizes thorough vetting of narrators; mursal of a reliable narrator is acceptable, but a deficient narrator's report is rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظَاهِرًا وَلَكِن وَقَعَ الْخَلَلُ بِوَجْهِ آخَرَ وَهُوَ فَقْدُ  َشرَائِطُ الرَّاوِي أَوْ مُخَالِفَتُهُ لِدَلِيل فَوتَهُ فَإِنْ كَانَ لِنَقْصَانِ فِي النَّاقِلِ فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا مِنْ عَدَمَ قَبُوْلِ خَبَرِ الْكَافِرِ وَالْفَاسِقِ وَالصَّبِى وَالْمُغَفِلِ
فَإِن كَانَ نُقْصَان الخ اگر اس خلل کے سبب ہے ہو جو اس کے راوی کے اندر ہو تو اس کا حکم وہی ہے۔ جیسے ہم نے پہلے ذکر کیا ہے۔ یعنی کافر کی خبر فاسق، میں ، اور مغفل کی خبر کا مقبول نہ ہونا۔
Apparently, but the defect occurred in another way, and it is the loss of the conditions of the narrator or his opposition to a superior proof. So if it is due to a deficiency in the transmitter, then it is as we mentioned regarding the non-acceptance of the report of the disbeliever, the sinner, the child, and the heedless. This is the explanation: if the defect is due to the narrator, its ruling is as previously stated: the reports of the disbeliever, sinner, child, and heedless are not accepted.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage defines the first type of internal defect (خلل باطن) in hadith: a defect arising from the narrator's failure to meet acceptance conditions. The chain may appear connected, but the narrator is disqualified (kafir, fasiq, sabi, or mughaffal). In such cases, the hadith is rejected (mardud). This reiterates earlier rulings from the text on the conditions for narrators. The Hanafi school emphasizes that such defects render the hadith unreliable, as the transmitter's deficiency affects the authenticity of the report.

Key Terms
خلل باطن (khalal baatin): A hidden defect in a hadith that is not apparent from the chain but comes from the narrator's condition.
راو (rawi): The narrator who transmits the hadith; must meet conditions for acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a reason for rejecting a hadith due to narrator deficiency?
A) The narrator is a disbeliever.
B) The narrator is an innovator (mubtadi').
C) The narrator is a child.
D) The narrator is heedless (mughaffal).

Key Takeaway
A hadith is rejected if its narrator is a disbeliever, sinner, child, or heedless person, regardless of the chain's apparent soundness.

Conditions for Rejecting a Khabar: Contradiction with Stronger Sources
Explaining when a report is rejected due to contradiction with Quran, sunnah, or consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi grounds for rejecting a khabar and apply them to evaluate a hadith that appears to contradict the Quran or sunnah.

Core Idea
A khabar is rejected if it contradicts a stronger source — Quran, sunnah mashhurah, famous practice, or the Ijma of the Sahabah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwaar outlines the Hanafi criteria for rejecting a khabar when it conflicts with stronger evidence. The author presents four categories of contradiction, illustrating each with concrete examples. Understanding these criteria is essential for usul al-fiqh, as it determines which ahad reports are acceptable and which are set aside. The discussion also touches on the inter-madhhab differences, particularly with the Shafi'i school regarding the specification of Quran by ahad hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions for rejection
Scan the passage and list the four categories: contradiction with Quran, contradiction with well-known sunnah, contradiction with a famous incident, and when the Sahabah turn away from the hadith.
Each condition has an example; note them carefully.
2
Analyze the first condition: contradiction with Quran
Example: hadith 'No prayer without Fatihah' vs. Quran 73:20. The Quranic command is general (amm) and qat'i; the hadith is ahad and zanni. A zanni report cannot specify a qat'i text in Hanafi usul.
This is a key difference with the Shafi'i school.
3
Examine the second condition: contradiction with sunnah mashhurah
Example: hadith of judgment with one witness and oath contradicts the famous hadith 'Evidence is on the claimant, oath on the denier'. Sunnah mashhurah is considered mutawatir in meaning, thus stronger than ahad.
Sunnah mashhurah is between ahad and mutawatir in authority.
4
Understand the third condition: contradiction with a famous incident
Example: basmalah in prayer – only Abu Hurairah reported hearing it aloud despite thousands present. The widespread practice of the community (amal) serves as evidence against the report.
This is a practical application of tawatur fi'li.
5
Grasp the fourth condition: i'rad al-Sahabah
Example: hadith about seeking good in orphan's wealth; the Sahabah ignored it. This indicates either the hadith is not authentic or must be interpreted differently (e.g., 'sadaqah' means nafaqah).
This condition is unique to Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِن كَانَ بالعَرْض اور اگر وصول کی مخالفت کی سبب سے ہو مثلا کتاب اللہ کے خلاف ہو جیسے لا مثلوة إلا بقائمة الكتاب نماز بغیر سورہ فاتحہ کے نہیں ہوتی والی حدیث اللہ تعالی کے اس قول کے عموم کے خلاف واقع ہوتی ہے قول یہ ہے فَاقْرَهُ و مَا تَسرَ مِنَ القُرآنِ پس جو قرآن میں تم کو آسان معلوم ہو پڑھو۔ اس میں کسی آیت یا سور ہ کی تعیین نہیں ہے اور جیسے مَن مَس الذَّكَرَ فَليتوضا (جو شخص بحالت - وضو ا پنے عضو مخصوص کو چھو لے تو چاہئے کہ وضو کر لے) یہ حدیث اللہ تعالی کے اس قول کے خلاف ہے۔ فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُعِبُونَ أَن يَتَطَهُرُوا۔ اس میں ایسے لوگ ہیں جو اچھی طرح طہارت کو پسند کرتے ہیں جن لوگوں کی اس میں تعریف ہے وہ استجاہ بجائے ڈھیلہ کے پانی سے کیا کرتے تھے۔ اور پانی کے استعمال میں خود میں ذکر پایا جاتا ہے۔ اگر میں ذکر تناقض للوضو ہو تا تو پانی کے استعمال سے عمدہ طہارت حاصل نہ ہوتی۔ اور قرآن مجید نے ان کی اس فصل کی تعریف کی ہے معلوم ہو اس ذاکر ناقض وضو نہیں ہے۔ ملکریمی أو السنَّة المَعْرُوقه یا سخت معروفہ کے خلاف ہو جیسے حدیث ہے کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ایک شہادت اور ایک قسم پر مدعی کے حق پر فیصلہ فرمایا یہ حدیث القضاء يشاہد ویمین کی اس مشہور حدیث کے مخالف ہے۔ حدیث مشہور یہ ہے البَيْنَهُ عَلى المُدَّعِي وَاليَمِينُ عَلَى مَن انكر ثبوت مرگی کے ذمہ ہے وریہ اور مگر یہ قسم واجب ہے۔ أو الحادثة المشهور کہ نماز میں بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم کا بالجبر پر بھنا جس کو ابو ہر مرڈ نے روایت کیا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہ نماز والا قصہ ایک مشہور واقعہ ہے۔ اور مستمر ہے نماز میں ہزاروں آدمی حاضر ہوئے تھے۔ اس کے باوجود بسم اللہ کو چہر آکسی نمازی نے نہیں سنا صرف حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ عنہ نے سنا ایک عجیب کی بات ہے۔ او اعرض عنه الائمة الخ یا اس سے صہ اول کے ائمہ کرام (صحابہ) نے اعراض کیا ہو۔ یعنی جب صحابہ کرام سب یا ہم آپس میں ایک دوسرے سے رائے اور قیاس سے بات کریں اور حدیث کی طرف کی دھیان نہ دیں تو ان کا یہ فصل حدیث کے انتطاح کی دلیل ہوگا۔ جیسے روایت ہے کہ حضرات صحابہ بچہ کے مال کی زکوۃ واجب ہونے نہ ہونے کے بارے میں ایک دوسرے سے مختلف الرائے ہو گئے اور حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی حدیث ابْتَغُوا فِى مَالَ الْيَتَامَى خَيْرًا كَيْلاً تأكلة الصندقة تیموں کے بالوں میں تمہارت کی تلاش کرتے رہو ۔ تاکہ ان کے مال کو صدقہ نہ کھا جائے) کی طرف بالکل توجہ نہیں دی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ حدیث ثابت نہیں ہے اور اگر ثابت بھی ہے تو اس میں تاویل کی گئی ہے کہ صدقہ سے مراد نفقہ ہے۔ جیسا کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے نَفَقَةُ المَرْءِ عَلَى نَفْسيه صندق ( انسان کا نفقہ اپنے نفس پر صدقہ ہے)۔ كَانَ مَرْدُودًا منقطعاً أيضاً
And if it is by way of opposition, like opposing the Book of Allah: e.g., the hadith 'No prayer except with Surah al-Fatihah' contradicts the generality of Allah's saying 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' which does not specify any verse. And like the hadith 'Whoever touches his private part should perform wudu' contradicts the verse 'In it are men who love to purify themselves'... or opposing the well-known sunnah, like the hadith of judgment with one witness and oath opposes the famous hadith 'Evidence is on the claimant and the oath is on the denier'. Or opposing a famous incident like the basmalah in prayer, as only Abu Hurairah heard it despite thousands present. Or the Imams (Sahabah) turned away from it, like the hadith about seeking good in orphan's wealth, which they ignored, indicating it is not proven or is interpreted.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a rule: a khabar (report) is rejected when it contradicts a stronger source. The author lists four cases. First, contradiction with the Quran: the hadith that negates prayer without Fatihah conflicts with the general command to recite what is easy. Second, contradiction with a well-known sunnah: the hadith of judgment with one witness and oath conflicts with the established rule that evidence is on the claimant and oath on the denier. Third, contradiction with a famous incident: the basmalah hadith is weak because no one but Abu Hurairah heard it. Fourth, when the Sahabah turned away from a hadith, as they did regarding zakat on orphan's wealth, indicating the hadith is either not authentic or is interpreted differently.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report attributed to the Prophet, a Companion, or anyone; a single report (khabar wahid) is the subject of discussion.
مخالفة بالعرض (mukhalafah bi al-'ard): Opposition by way of contradiction to a stronger source such as Quran, sunnah mashhurah, or practice of the Sahabah.
سنة معروفة (sunnah ma'rufah): A well-known and widely transmitted sunnah, considered mashhurah or mutawatir in meaning.
حادثة مشهورة (hadithah mashhurah): A famous incident or practice known to a large number of people, serving as a check on isolated reports.
إعراض الصحابة (i'rad al-Sahabah): The turning away of the Companions from a hadith, either by not acting upon it or by ignoring it in their discussions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it contradicts the Quranic verse praising those who use water for purification.
B) Because it is a weak hadith with unreliable narrators.
C) Because it contradicts a well-known sunnah.
D) Because all Sahabah rejected it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects a khabar when it contradicts a stronger source, preserving the primacy of qat'i evidence over zanni reports.

Khabar Wahid: Acceptance Conditions in Huquq Allah and Huquq al-Ibad
Explaining acceptance conditions of khabar wahid in different categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for accepting khabar wahid in different categories (huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad) and explain the relevance of the condition of number ('adad) in matters involving liability.

Core Idea
Khabar wahid suffices for rights of Allah; for rights of people with liability, full testimony conditions apply.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, the author explains how the Hanafi school distinguishes between different types of cases when accepting a single reporter's narration. Understanding this distinction is essential for a mufti or judge to correctly apply hadith evidence in various legal contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The passage divides matters into huquq Allah (rights of Allah) and huquq al-ibad (rights of people). Determine which category a given case falls into.
Huquq Allah includes worship and penalties; huquq al-ibad includes debts and property.
2
For huquq Allah, evaluate the condition of number
Khabar wahid is accepted without requiring a specific number of narrators. Cite the hadith of Aisha as proof. However, note the counterargument from the hadith of Dhul-Yadain, which some use to require a second witness.
3
For huquq al-ibad with liability, list the conditions
If the matter involves pure liability (ilzam), such as debt or pledge, all conditions of testimony apply: sanity, integrity, retention, Islam, number (two), word 'ashhadu', and free status.
4
Recognize the dispute with al-Karkhi
Al-Karkhi holds that khabar wahid is not accepted in penalties (uqubat) because of doubt in continuous transmission, while the Hanafi position accepts it. Understand the reasoning on both sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

سے ، مگر سنت کی بحث میں اسے ذکر کرنا جمہور سلف کی مشہور مسامحات ) میں سے ایک ہے اور ایسا امام فخر الاسلام کی پیروی میں کیا گیا ہے۔ فَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ حُقوقِ اللهِ تَعَالَى :. پس اگر محل غیر حقوق اللہ کے قسم میں سے ہو، تو خبر واحد اس میں حجت ہوگی۔ برابر ہے کہ وہ از قسم عبارات ہو یا عقوبات میں سے ہو ۔ یادونوں کے درمیان دائر ہو ( یعنی اس میں یا ہو۔ یا دونوں چیز پائی جاتی ہوں عبادات بھی ہوں عقوبات بھی یا ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ اس کی مؤیتہ (ذمہ داری ہو) اور بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ خبر واحد بلا کسی عدد کی شرط کے حجت ہے کیوں کہ صحابہ نے حديث إِذَ التَقَى الْكِتَانَانِ (جب دونوں شرم گاہیں ایک دوسرے سے مل جائیں) کو تنہا حضرت عائشہ کی روایت سے قبول کیا ہے، اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ عدد کی شرط کے ساتھ خبر واحد قبول کی جائے گی، کیوں کہ جناب رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ذوالیدین کی تنہا خبر کو قبول نہیں فرمایا جو صلوۃ کے نام نہ ہونے کے بارہ میں تھی جب تک کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ان کے ساتھ دوسرے صحابہ کی خبر شامل نہیں فرمالیا۔ خِلافًا لِلْكَرَخِي فِي الْعقوبات لیکن امام کرخی عقوبات میں اختلاف کرتے ہیں۔ وہ عقوبات میں خبر واحد کو قبول نہیں کرتے ، اور حدود کو اس سے ثابت نہیں کرتے ہیں، کیونکہ خبر واحد کے حضور تیک متصل ہونے میں شبہ ہے، اور حدود شبہات سے دفع ہو جاتے ہیں ، البتہ قاضی کے پاس صدور کو بینات سے ثابت کرنے کا مسئلہ تو یہ خلاف قیاس نص ہی سے جائز ہے۔ اور نص اللہ تعالی کا قول فاستشنہ دُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةُ مِنْكُمْ ہے (ان) فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عورتوں کے خلاف اپنوں میں سے چار گواہ بنالو ) اور اس جیسے دوسرے اقوال ہیں۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ حدود بینات سے ثابت نہیں ہوتے بلکہ حدود کے اسباب بینات سے ثابت ہو جاتے ہیں، اور حدود کتاب سے ثابت ہیں۔ وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ حُقوق العباد : اور اگر حقوق العباد کی اس قسم سے ہو جس میں الزام محض ہو جیسے ویون (قرض) کے باب میں کسی پر کسی کے حق کے ثابت ہونے کی خبر یا وقف شدہ چیزوں کی خبر یا رہن رکھی ہوئی چیز کی خبر اس طرح شی منصوب کی خیبر ( یہ الزام محض کی مثالیں ہیں) تُشتَرَطَ فِيْهِ سَائِرُ شَرَائِطِ الاخبار تو اس میں تمام اخبار کی شرطیں جیسے عقل عدالت، ضبط اور اسلام مع العد دو لفظ الشہادت مع عدد اور لفظ شہادت کے اور ولایت کے بایں طور کہ گواہی دینے والے دو ہوں اور لفظ اشہد (میں گواہی دیتا ہوں) کو زبان سے کہا اور اس گواہی دینے کا اہل بھی ہو۔ یعنی آزاد (حر) ہو ۔ جب یہ تینوں شرطیں مع سابقہ چاروں شرائط کے جمع ہوں گی تو خبر واحد قاضی کی مجلس میں مقبول ہو گی ، ان معاملات میں جن میں مدعی علیہ پر الترام ہو۔ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا الْزَامَ فِيْهِ أَصْلاً كَخَبَرِ الْوِكَالَةِ وَالْمُصَارَيَةِ وَالرِّسَالَةِ فِي الْهَدَايَا
Ashraf al-Anwar sharh Urdu Nur al-Anwar volume three. Five categories [are made]. And the division of absolute khabar wahid is general whether it is a report of the Messenger or of the noble Companions or of the general people, from the market people, but mentioning it in the discussion of Sunnah is one of the famous concessions of the majority of the Salaf, and it has been done following Imam Fakhr al-Islam. Then if it is from the rights of Allah: then if the subject is from the category of rights of Allah, then khabar wahid will be a proof in it. It is equal whether it is from the category of acts of worship or from penalties, or falls between them (i.e., contains both or with one of them its liability). And some people have said that khabar wahid is a proof without any condition of number because the Companions accepted the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet' from the sole narration of Aisha, and some have said that khabar wahid will be accepted with the condition of number, because the Messenger of Allah did not accept the sole report of Dhul-Yadain concerning forgetfulness in prayer until he included the report of other Companions with it. Contrary to al-Karkhi in penalties: Imam al-Karkhi disagrees in penalties. He does not accept khabar wahid in penalties, and does not establish hudud through it, because there is doubt in the connection of khabar wahid to the time of the Prophet, and hudud are repelled by doubts. However, the issue of establishing adultery before a judge through evidence is permissible against analogy only by nass. And the nass is the saying of Allah: 'And call to witness four witnesses from among you' and similar other sayings. Secondly, hudud are not established through evidence; rather, the causes of hudud are established through evidence, and hudud are established from the Book. And if it is from the rights of people: and if it is from the category of rights of people in which there is pure liability, like in the chapter of debt, a report proving someone's right upon another, or a report of endowed properties, or a report of a mortgaged item, similarly a thing set up as a pledge (these are examples of pure liability). Then all the conditions of reports are required in it: like intellect, integrity, retention, Islam, along with number, the word of testimony with number, and the word of testimony, and capacity for giving testimony, such that the testifiers be two and the word 'ashhadu' be uttered, and they be qualified for giving testimony, i.e., free. When these three conditions together with the previous four conditions are met, then khabar wahid will be accepted in the judge's court in those matters in which there is liability upon the defendant. And if there is no liability at all, like a report of agency, partnership, and messenger regarding gifts.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains the conditions for accepting khabar wahid (a single report) in different categories of cases. It begins by stating that khabar wahid can be from the Prophet, Companions, or common people, but in discussions of Sunnah, it is a concession from the Salaf to include it. The main discussion then classifies matters into rights of Allah and rights of people. For rights of Allah, khabar wahid is accepted without requiring a specific number of narrators, as seen when the Companions accepted the hadith about ritual impurity being caused by genital contact from Aisha alone. However, some scholars (like al-Karkhi) make an exception for penalties (uqubat) because hudud are repelled by doubts due to possible lack of continuous transmission. For rights of people with liability (ilzam), such as debts, endowments, or pledges, all conditions of testimony are required: the reporters must be sane, upright, precise, Muslim, two in number, use the word 'ashhadu', be free, and have legal capacity. If these conditions are met, the report is accepted in court. This contrasts with the next category where there is no liability, which begins at the end of this passage.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur.
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights that belong to Allah, such as acts of worship and penalties.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-'ibad): Rights that belong to individuals, such as debts and property claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is required for accepting khabar wahid in rights of people with liability (like debt)?
A) Only that the reporter be trustworthy
B) All conditions of testimony, including number ('adad) and the word 'ashhadu'
C) No conditions, just report of any Muslim
D) Only that the reporter be sane and adult

Key Takeaway
Khabar wahid is accepted in huquq Allah without number condition; in huquq al-ibad with liability, all testimony conditions apply.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate

Khabar Wahid in Non-Binding Matters and Dispute on 'Azl and Hijr
Specifies conditions for khabar wahid in rights of people without liability and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that non-binding reports require only tamyiz, and distinguish the mixed-liability case where Abu Hanifa requires a shatri shahada, unlike the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Non-binding reports need only a discerning reporter; mixed-liability cases require testimony, sparking internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

We have learned that khabar wahid is accepted in muamalat with conditions. This passage examines reports with no liability—like announcements of gifts, agency, or partnership—where only tamyiz (discernment) is required. But when a report involves both binding and non-binding aspects, such as the dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakil) or restriction of a minor (hijr al-ma'dun), Abu Hanifa demands a higher standard of proof, leading to a dispute with his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson will unpack each category and the rationale behind the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of reports
First, distinguish reports that involve no liability at all (e.g., 'so-and-so gave you a gift' or 'you are appointed agent')—these are accepted with only tamyiz. Second, identify reports that have mixed liability, like 'your agent is dismissed'—these affect the agent/minor and thus require more conditions according to Abu Hanifa.
The key is whether the report imposes an obligation on the recipient or a third party.
2
State the Hanafi rule for no-liability reports
For reports where the recipient is free to accept or reject (e.g., gift, agency, partnership), the only condition is that the informer be a discerning person (mumayyiz). No 'adalah (integrity) or number of witnesses is required—even a child, slave, non-Muslim, or fasiq suffices.
The rationale is that requiring full conditions would hinder daily transactions.
3
Analyze the dalil for the no-liability rule
The text cites the Prophet's practice of accepting gift reports from both righteous and sinful individuals. This shows that in non-binding matters, the conditions of testimony (like 'adalah) are not needed.
This is a sunnah of fi'li (action), classified as khabar wahid with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Examine the mixed-liability case ('azl and hijr)
Reports of dismissing an agent (azl al-wakil) or restricting a minor (hijr al-ma'dun) have two aspects: (1) the principal acts in his own right, so no liability on him; (2) the agent/minor is harmed (liability). Abu Hanifa balances both sides by requiring one shatri shahada—either two witnesses or one just witness.
The Sahibayn hold that no additional conditions are needed because the principal is exercising his own right.
5
Compare the two positions and note the consensus
Abu Hanifa requires one of the two halves of testimony (number and 'adalah). The Sahibayn require only tamyiz. However, if the informant is an appointed agent or messenger of the principal, there is consensus that no conditions apply—the messenger's word equals the principal's.
The thamarah (practical outcome): a report from a single fasiq about an agent's dismissal is accepted by Sahibayn but not by Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَيُبَاشِرُهُ لأَن الإِنْسانَ قَلْمًا يَجِدُ رَجُلاً مُسْتَجْمعًا للشرَائِطِ يَبْعَثُهُ عَلَى وَكَيْلِهِ. لَوْ غُلامِهِ  ِبالْخَبَرِ فَلَوْ شَرِطَت فيه الشروط لتَعَلتْ الْمَصَالِحُ فِي الْعَالَمِ وَلَان الْخَيْرُ غَيْرُ مُلْزِمٌ فِي الْوَاقِعِ فَلَا تُعْتَبَرُ فِيْهِ شَرَائِط الإلزام وَالنَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السلام كَانَ يَقْبَلُ خَيْرَ الْهَدَيَةِ مَنِ البَرِ وَالْفَاجِرِ وَأَنْ كَانَ فِيهِ الْرَام ضَرَرْ عَلَى الْوَكِيْلِ وَالْعَبْدِ فَلِهَذَا يَسْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ أَحَدٌ شطْرَى الشَّهَادَةِ عِنْدَ أبَى حَنِيفَةَ يَعْنِي الْعَدَدَ وَالْعَدَالَة أى لابد أن يَكُونَ الْمُكْبَرُ اثْنَيْنِ أَوْ وَاحِدًا عَدْلاً رِعَايَةً لِشِبْهِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ الْرَامًا مَحْضًا فِيهِ كِلاَهُمَا وَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ الْزَامًا أصلاً ما شرِطَ فِيهِ شَيْءٌ مِنْهُمَا فَوَفْرْنَا حَظًّا مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ فِيهِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لا يَشْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ شَيْءٌ بَلْ يَثْبُ الْحِجَرُ وَالْعَزْلِ يَخَيْرِ كُلِّ مُمَيْرٍ وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الْمُكْبِرُ فَضَوْلِيًا فَإِنْ كَانَ وَكِيْلاً أَوْ محل حقوق العباد کی اس قسم میں سے ہے جس میں سرے سے ترجمہ و تشریح کوئی الزام نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کسی کے وکیل ہونے کی خبر ۔ اور شریک مال ہونے کی خبر اور ہدیہ میں قاصد ہونے کی خبر اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے چیزوں کی خبریں۔ مثلاً کوئی کہے تم کو فلاں نے وکیل بنایا ہے۔ بالا نے تجھ کو اس چیز میں شریک بنالیا ہے۔ یا فلاں نے یہ چیز تمہیں ہدیہ میں دی ہے۔ ان مثالوں میں کسی پر الزام نہیں ہے بلکہ جسے خبر دی گئی ہے وہ چاہے اس ہدیہ، وکالت، شرکت کو قبول کرنے یا قبول نہ کرے اس کو دونوں باتوں کا اختیار ہے۔ ويُثبت بأخبار الآحاد : تو یہ اخبار آحاد سے ثابت ہو گا، بشرطیکہ خبر دینے والا صاحب تمیز ہو۔ نہ اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ مخیر صاحب عدالت ہو۔ یعنی شرط یہ ہے کہ مخیر امتیاز پیدا کرانے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو، جو کہ دہ
And the like of that when he says: 'So-and-so appointed you as agent' or 'made you a partner in this' or 'gave you this thing as a gift' – then there is no liability upon anyone; rather, he chooses between accepting the agency, partnership, and gift and not accepting. It is established through khabar ahad with the condition of tamyiz (discernment) without the condition of 'adalah (integrity). That is, with the condition that the informer be a discerning person, whether child or adult, free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever, just or sinful. So the person informed of the agency or partnership may act upon it and undertake it, because a person rarely finds a man possessing all the conditions to send as his agent. If conditions were stipulated, benefits would be cut off in the world, and because the report is not binding in reality, so the conditions of binding are not considered. And the Prophet used to accept the report of a gift from the righteous and the sinful. And if it has binding from one aspect but not from another – like the report of dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakil) and restriction of a minor (hijr al-ma'dun) – from the perspective that the principal and master act in their own right in dismissal and restriction just as they act in appointment and permission, so there is no liability at all; and from the perspective that the action is confined to the agent and slave after the dismissal and restriction, and liability of responsibility is attached, so there is liability and harm upon the agent and slave. Therefore, Abu Hanifa stipulates one of the two halves of testimony in it, i.e., number and integrity: two witnesses or one just witness, doing justice to both sides, because if it were pure liability, both would be required, and if there were no liability at all, nothing would be required. So we gave a share from both sides. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), nothing is required; rather, dismissal and restriction are established by the report of any discerning person. And this is when the informer is a volunteer. If he is an appointee or messenger from the principal or master, then integrity and number are not required by consensus, because the expression of the appointee and messenger is like the expression of the appointer and sender.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of khabar wahid in rights of people, now focusing on cases without any liability (la ilzam). Examples include someone informing you that you have been appointed as an agent (wakil), entered into a partnership (musarabah), or given a gift (hiba). In these cases, since there is no obligation on the recipient to act, the report is accepted with only the condition that the informer be discerning (mumayyiz), regardless of age, freedom, religion, or moral character. The rationale is that requiring full conditions would hinder daily transactions; even the Prophet accepted reports of gifts from good and bad people. A special case arises when the report involves both binding and non-binding aspects, such as the dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakil) or restriction of a minor (hijr al-ma'dun). From one angle, the principal is acting within his own rights, so there is no liability; but from another, the agent or minor incurs restrictions and liability. Abu Hanifa therefore requires one of the two halves of testimony – either two witnesses or one just witness – balancing both perspectives. His two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no conditions are needed; any discerning informant suffices. However, if the informant is an appointed agent or messenger of the principal, then there is consensus that no integrity or number conditions apply, because the messenger's statement is like the principal's own statement.

Key Terms
تمييز (tamyiz): The ability to discern and understand, typically attained by a child around age 7.
عزل الوكيل (azl al-wakil): Dismissal of an agent from his agency.
حجر المأذون (hijr al-ma'dun): Restriction of a minor who had been given permission to trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for accepting a khabar wahid about the dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakil) according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The report must come from two witnesses or one just witness.
B) The report must come from a discerning person with no condition of 'adalah.
C) The report must be in writing or have a seal.
D) The report must be from an appointee or messenger of the principal.

Key Takeaway
Non-binding reports need only a discerning informer; mixed-liability reports trigger a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on requiring testimony conditions.

The Four Types of Khabar and Their Transmission Aspects
Classification of khabar and its transmission aspects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of khabar according to Hanafi usul and explain the three aspects of transmission (hearing, memorization, delivery) along with their strict and relaxed methods.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid has four types; only the preponderant type from a just, reliable transmitter is legally actionable.

Understanding the nature of reports (khabar) is foundational to Islamic legal theory. The Hanafi school classifies single-person reports into four categories based on the likelihood of truth. This lesson unpacks that classification and introduces the three essential aspects of transmission — hearing, memorization, and delivery — each with its own strict and relaxed methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of khabar
Read the passage and list the four categories: certainly true, certainly false, equiprobable, and preponderant. Note the examples given.
2
Distinguish the preponderant type
Focus on type 4: the report of a just person who fulfills all conditions (hearing, memorization, delivery). Understand why this type is the intended one for legal evidence.
3
Recognize the three aspects of transmission
Identify the three atraf: hearing (sama'), memorization (hifz), and delivery (ada'). Each is essential for the validity of the report.
4
Differentiate azima and rukhsa
For each aspect, note the strict method (azima) and the concession (rukhsa). Understand the reasoning behind the preference for each.

وَالتَّقْسِيْمُ الرَّابِعُ فِي بَيَانِ نَفْسِ الْخَبَرِ وَهَذَا التَّقْسِيْمَ أَيْضًا لِمُطْلَقِ خَيْرُ الْوَاحِدِ أَعَمُ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ خَيْرَ الرَّسُوْلِ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ وَهُوَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ قِسمْ يُحِيْطُ الْعِلْمِ بِصَدَقَةٍ كَخَبَرِ الرَّسُولِ إِنْ لَا دِلَّة الْقَطْعِيَةُ قَائِمَةٌ عَلَى عِصمَتِهِ عَنِ الْكِذَبِ وَسَائِرِ الذُّنُوبِ وَقِسم يُحِيطُ العِلْمَ بِكذِّبِهِ كَدَعْوَىٰ فِرْعَوْنَ الرَّبُوْبِيَةٌ لأَنْ الْحَادِثِ الْفَانِئ لآيَكُونُ إِلَها بِالْبَدَامَةِ وَقِسمْ يَحْتَمِلُهُمَا عَلى السَّوَاءِ كَخَبَرِ الْفَاسِقِ فَإِنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْ اِسلامِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ الصدق وَمِنْ حَيْثُ فِسْقِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ الكذب فَهُوَ وَاجِبْ التَّوَقُفِ وَقِسمْ يُتَرَبَّحُ أَحَدُ احْتِمَالَيْهِ عَلى الآخرِ كَحْبَرٍ الْعَدْلِ الْمُسْتَجْمِعِ لِلشَّرَائِطِ وَلِهَذَا النَّوْعِ الْآخِيْرِ الْمَقْصُودُ هَبْنَا أَطْرَافٌ فَلَتَهُ طَرْفَ السَّمَاعِ بَأَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْحَدِيثِ عَنِ الْمُحَدِّثِ أَوْ لَا وَطَرْفُ الْحِفْظِ بِأَنْ يَحْفَظُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ أَوْلِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ وَطَرَفُ الآدَاءِ بِأَنْ يُلْقِيَة إِلَى الْآخَرِ لِتَفْرُغَ ذِمَّتُهُ وَفِي كُلِّ طَرْفٍ مِنهَا عَزِيْمَةٌ وَرُخْصَةٌ فَالأَوَّلُ طَرْفُ السَّمَاعِ وَذَلِكَ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُون عَزِيمَةٌ وَهُوَ مَا يَكُونُ مِنْ جِنْسِ الأَسْمَاعِ أَنْ يَسْمَعُ الظُّلْمِيذُ عِبَارَةَ الْحَدِيثِ مُشافَهَةٌ أَوْ مُغَايَبَةُ بِأَنْ تَقْرَأْ عَلَى الْمُحَدِّثِ مِنْ كِتَابِ أَوْ حَفْظ وَهُوَ يَسْمَعُ كُمْ تَقُولُ لَهُ أَهْوَ كَمَا قَرَأْتُ عَلَيْكَ فَيَقُولُ هُوَ نَعَمْ وَهَذَا أَحْوَطُ لأَنَّهُ إِذَا قَرَاءَ بِنَفْسِهِ كان أشدُّ عِنَايَةً فِي ضَبْطِ الْمَتَنِ لأَنه عَامِلُ لِنَفْسِهِ وَالْمُحَدِثُ عَامِل لِغَيْرِهِ أَوْ يَقْرَأ عَلَيْكَ الْمُحَدِّثُ بَنَفْسِهِ مِنْ كِتَابِ أَوْ حِفْظِ وَأَنْتَ تَسْمَعَهُ وَقِيلَ هَذَا أَحْسَنُ لَأَنْ كَانَ - وَظِيفَة النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ وان : الأُمَّةِ وَكَانَ مَامُونًا عَنِ الْخَطَاءِ وَالْحَوَابُ أَنَّهُ وَالنَّسيَانِ وَالاِحْتِيَاطُ فِي حَقْنَا هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ أَوْ يَكْتُبَ إِلَيْكَ كِتَابًا عَلَى رَسمِ الْكَتِبِ بِأَنْ يَكْتُبَ قَبْلَ التَّسْمِيَةِ مِنْ فَلَآنِ اِبْنِ فُلان إِلَى فَلانِ بْنِ فُلانٍ ثُمَّ يُسمّى وَيُثْنِي وَيُذْكُرُ فِيهِ حَدَّثَنِي فُلان بن فلان آه أى إِلَى أَنْ يَتَّصِلَ بِالرسول صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسلم ويَذْكُرُ بَعْدَ ذالك مَثْنَ الْحَدِيث ثُمَّ يَقُولُ فِيهِ إِذا بَلَغَكَ كِتَابِي هَذَا وَفَهِمْتَهُ فَحَدَّتْ بِهِ عَنِّى فَهَذَا مِنَ الغَائِبِ كَالْخِطَابِ مِنَ الْحَاضِرِ فِي جَوَازِ الرَّوَايَةِ.
And the fourth division concerning the nature of the report itself. And this division is also for absolute single-person report, whether it is the report of the Messenger or other than him. For this reason, he said: It has four parts: (1) a part that knowledge encompasses its truthfulness, like the report of the Messenger, because decisive proofs are established for his infallibility from lying and all sins; (2) a part that knowledge encompasses its falsehood, like Pharaoh's claim of divinity, because the transient and originated cannot be a deity by necessity; (3) a part that implies both equally, like the report of a sinner, for from the perspective of his Islam it implies truth, and from the perspective of his sinfulness it implies falsehood, so it is obligatory to withhold; (4) a part in which one of its possibilities outweighs the other, like the report of a just person who fulfills all conditions. And this last type is the intended one. For it there are aspects: the aspect of hearing, i.e., that he hears the hadith from the teacher or not; the aspect of memorization, i.e., that he memorizes thereafter from beginning to end; and the aspect of delivery, i.e., that he conveys it to another to discharge his responsibility. In each of these aspects there is a strict method (azima) and a concession (rukhsa). The first is the aspect of hearing. That is either strict: it is what falls under the genus of hearing: that the student hears the wording of the hadith face-to-face or in absence, such that he reads to the teacher from a book or memory and the teacher listens, saying to him: 'Is it as I read to you?' and he says 'Yes'. This is more precautionary because when he reads himself he is more attentive in mastering the text, since he is acting for himself while the teacher is acting for another. Or the teacher reads to you himself from a book or memory and you listen to him. It is said that this is better because it was the function of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And the Ummah was [model?]. And he was immune from error, and the correct view is about forgetfulness, and precaution for us is the first. Or he writes to you a letter in the form of correspondence: that he writes before the basmalah: 'From so-and-so son of so-and-so to so-and-so son of so-and-so', then he begins with the name of Allah and praises, and mentions therein 'so-and-so ibn so-and-so narrated to me...' until he connects to the Messenger (peace be upon him), and after that he mentions the text of the hadith, then says therein: 'When my letter reaches you and you understand it, then narrate it on my authority.' So this from an absent person is like addressing a present person in terms of permissibility of narration.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth classification in the study of khabar (report), specifically concerning the nature of the report itself. It applies to any khabar al-wahid (single-person report), whether it is a report from the Prophet or from someone else. The report is divided into four types: (1) certainly true, like the Prophet's report due to his infallibility proven by decisive evidence; (2) certainly false, like Pharaoh's claim of divinity, as the created and perishable cannot be eternal God; (3) equally probable of truth and falsehood, like the report of a fasiq (sinner) — in this case, one must withhold judgment (tawaqquf) because his Islam suggests truthfulness but his sinfulness suggests falsehood; (4) where one probability outweighs the other, like the report of a just person who meets all conditions. The fourth type is the one intended for practical use. The passage then explains the three 'aspects' (atraf) of this type: hearing (samaa), memorization (hifz), and delivery (ada). Each aspect has a strict method (azima) and a concession (rukhsa). For hearing, the strict method involves the student reading to the teacher and the teacher confirming; this is more cautious because the student is more diligent. Another method is the teacher reading to the student, which is considered better by some because it was the Prophet's practice. A third method is receiving a written letter from the teacher with proper form, which is permissible as if it were a face-to-face authorization.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or narration, classified into four types based on the possibility of truth
الأطراف الثلاثة (al-atraf al-thalatha): The three aspects of transmission: hearing, memorization, and delivery
عزيمة ورخصة (azima wa rukhsa): Strict rule and concession; in transmission, azima is the more cautious method, rukhsa is the easier one

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should be done with a report from a fasiq (sinner) according to this classification?
A) Accept it because of his Islam
B) Reject it because of his sin
C) Withhold judgment (tawaqquf) until further evidence
D) Accept it as a witness testimony

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of khabar al-wahid into four types helps determine which reports are reliable for legal evidence, and the three aspects of transmission ensure the integrity of the narration process.

The Four Types of Khabar in Hanafi Usul
Defines four types of khabar and their rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of khabar based on probability of truth/falsehood and state the Hanafi ruling for each type.

Core Idea
The ruling on a khabar depends on its probability—certain acceptance, certain rejection, suspension, or conditional acceptance.

In Hanafi usul, not all reports are treated equally. The validity of a report depends on the likelihood of its truthfulness. The author divides khabar into four categories, ranging from necessarily true to necessarily false. Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating narrators and hadith authentication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four types of khabar mentioned in the text: (1) necessarily true, (2) necessarily false, (3) equally probable (fasiq), (4) one probability outweighs the other (adl).
The first three are briefly mentioned; the fourth is the main focus.
2
Understand the probability basis
Each category is defined by the probability of truth: necessary (qat'i), impossible, muhtamil (equal), or preponderant (rajih).
This probability determines the ruling (hukm).
3
Note the ruling for each type
Type 1: must be accepted (ilm yabtani). Type 2: rejected. Type 3: wājib al-tawaqquf (suspend judgment). Type 4: accepted if conditions of narrator are met.
The text explicitly states that the fasiq's report is wājib al-tawaqquf.
4
Apply to examples
Consider a report from a known liar (fasiq) – it is suspended. Consider a report from a reliable narrator – it is of the fourth type and may be accepted if conditions met.
This application is key for practical hadith criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْفَاسِقِ فَإِنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِسْلَامِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ الصِّدْقَ وَمِنْ حَيْثُ فِسْقِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ الْكَذِبَ فَهُوَ وَاجِبُ التَّوَقُفِ. وَقِسْمٌ يَتَرَجَّحُ أَحَدُ احْتِمَالَيْهِ عَلَى الْآخَرِ كَخَبَرِ الْعَدْلِ الْمُسْتَجْمِعِ لِلشَّرَائِطِ. وَلِهَذَا النَّوْعِ الْآخِرِ الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهُ أَطْرَافٌ: فَلَهُ طَرَفُ السَّمَاعِ بِأَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْحَدِيثَ عَنِ الْمُحَدِّثِ أَوْ لَا، وَطَرَفُ الْحِفْظِ بِأَنْ يَحْفَظَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ أَوَّلِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ، وَطَرَفُ الْأَدَاءِ بِأَنْ يُلْقِيَهُ إِلَى الْآخَرِ لِيَتَفَرَّغَ ذِمَّتُهُ. وَفِي كُلِّ طَرَفٍ مِنْهَا عَزِيمَةٌ وَرُخْصَةٌ. فَالْأَوَّلُ طَرَفُ السَّمَاعِ: وَذَلِكَ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ عَزِيمَةً وَهُوَ مَا يَكُونُ مِنْ جِنْسِ الْإِسْمَاعِ: أَنْ يَسْمَعَ التِّلْمِيذُ عِبَارَةَ الْحَدِيثِ مُشَافَهَةً أَوْ مُغَايَبَةً: بِأَنْ تَقْرَأَ عَلَى الْمُحَدِّثِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ أَوْ حِفْظٍ وَهُوَ يَسْمَعُ، ثُمَّ تَقُولُ لَهُ: أَهُوَ كَمَا قَرَأْتُ عَلَيْكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: نَعَمْ. وَهَذَا أَحْوَطُ لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا قَرَأَ بِنَفْسِهِ كَانَ أَشَدَّ عِنَايَةً فِي ضَبْطِ الْمَتْنِ لِأَنَّهُ عَامِلٌ لِنَفْسِهِ وَالْمُحَدِّثُ عَامِلٌ لِغَيْرِهِ. أَوْ يَقْرَأَ عَلَيْكَ الْمُحَدِّثُ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ أَوْ حِفْظٍ وَأَنْتَ تَسْمَعُهُ. وَقِيلَ هَذَا أَحْسَنُ لِأَنَّهُ كَانَ وَظِيفَةَ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَهُوَ مَأْمُونٌ عَنِ الْخَطَاءِ وَالنِّسْيَانِ. وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّهُ وَالنَّسْيَانِ[؟] وَالِاحْتِيَاطُ فِي حَقِّنَا هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ. أَوْ يَكْتُبَ إِلَيْكَ كِتَابًا عَلَى رَسْمِ الْكِتَابِ: بِأَنْ يَكْتُبَ قَبْلَ التَّسْمِيَةِ مِنْ فُلَانِ بْنِ فُلَانٍ إِلَى فُلَانِ بْنِ فُلَانٍ، ثُمَّ يُسَمِّي وَيُثَنِّي وَيَذْكُرُ فِيهِ حَدَّثَنِي فُلَانُ بْنُ فُلَانٍ إِلَى أَنْ يَتَّصِلَ بِالرَّسُولِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وَيَذْكُرُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مَتْنَ الْحَدِيثِ، ثُمَّ يَقُولُ فِيهِ: إِذَا بَلَغَكَ كِتَابِي هَذَا وَفَهِمْتَهُ فَحَدِّثْ بِهِ عَنِّي. فَهَذَا مِنَ الْغَائِبِ كَالْخِطَابِ مِنَ الْحَاضِرِ فِي جَوَازِ الرِّوَايَةِ.
The [report] of the fasiq: indeed from the aspect of his Islam it may be true, and from the aspect of his sinfulness it may be false, so it is obligatory to suspend [judgment]. And a type in which one of its two probabilities outweighs the other, like the report of the just [narrator] who fulfills the conditions. And for this last type, which is intended, there are aspects: it has the aspect of hearing, that he hears the hadith from the muhaddith or not; and the aspect of memorization, that he memorizes it after that from beginning to end; and the aspect of delivery, that he conveys it to another to free his responsibility. And in each aspect there is a strict method and a concession. The first is the aspect of hearing: that either it is strict, which is of the kind of making hear: that the student hears the wording of the hadith orally or absently: by reading to the muhaddith from a book or memory while he listens, then you say to him: 'Is it as I read to you?' He says: 'Yes.' This is more precautionary because when he reads himself, he is more careful in preserving the text, since he is acting for himself, while the muhaddith is acting for another. Or the muhaddith reads to you himself from a book or memory while you listen. It is said this is better, because it was the practice of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and he was protected from error and forgetfulness. The answer is that he and forgetfulness[?] and precaution for us is the first. Or he writes to you a letter in the form of writing: that he writes before the basmalah: 'From so-and-so son of so-and-so to so-and-so son of so-and-so', then he says the basmalah and praises and mentions in it: 'So-and-so son of so-and-so narrated to me' until he connects to the Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace, and after that he mentions the text of the hadith, then he says in it: 'When this my letter reaches you and you understand it, then narrate it from me.' So this from the absent is like speech from the present regarding the permissibility of narration.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of khabar (report) in Hanafi usul. It first divides khabar into four types: (1) that whose truth is known necessarily (e.g., the Prophet's report); (2) that whose falsehood is known necessarily (e.g., Pharaoh's claim of divinity); (3) that which is equally probable of truth and falsehood (e.g., the report of a fasiq, which is muhtamil and thus wājib al-tawaqquf - must be suspended); (4) that where one probability outweighs the other (e.g., a just narrator's report). The passage focuses on the fourth type, which is the basis for accepting ahad reports. It then explains three aspects (atrāf) of this fourth type: (a) samā‘ (hearing), (b) hifz (memorization), and (c) adā’ (delivery). For each, there is a strict method ('azīma) and a concession (rukhṣa). The hearing aspect is elaborated with three methods: (1) the student reads back to the teacher (more precautionary), (2) the teacher reads to the student (some say better because it was the Prophet's way, but the answer is that first method is more precautionary for us), (3) the teacher writes a letter with full isnad and instructs the recipient to narrate it. This last method is permissible as a form of riwāya. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each division and method with Hanafi precision.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or narration that can be true or false; a statement that conveys information about a past event.
واجب التوقف (wājib al-tawaqquf): Suspending judgment; neither accepting nor rejecting the report until further evidence.
عدل (ʿadl): A just, reliable narrator who fulfills the conditions of probity (taqdīs) and does not commit major sins or persist in minor ones.
سماع (samāʿ): The act of hearing the hadith from the teacher, either directly or through reading back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the report of a fāsiq (sinful narrator)?
A) It is accepted unconditionally.
B) It is rejected unconditionally.
C) It is suspended (wājib al-tawaqquf).
D) It is treated like the report of a ʿadl.

Key Takeaway
Khabar is classified by probability of truth, and the fasiq's report requires suspension, not rejection.
