Three Aspects (Atrāf) of the Preponderant Khabar
Explains three aspects of the preponderant khabar and methods of hearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three aspects of the preponderant khabar (hearing, memorization, delivery) and distinguish between the 'azīma and rukhṣa in the hearing aspect.

Core Idea
Transmitting hadith requires hearing, memorization, and delivery; each has a strict method (azima) and a concession (rukhsa).

Once we identify a khabar as preponderant (fourth type), we must ensure its correct transmission. The author breaks down the transmission process into three aspects: hearing the hadith, memorizing it, and delivering it to others. For each, there is a strict method (azima) and a concession (rukhsa). Understanding these helps us evaluate the reliability of the transmission chain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three aspects
List the three atrāf mentioned: (1) samā‘ (hearing), (2) hifz (memorization), (3) adā’ (delivery).
These are the three stages of tahammul and ada’.
2
Understand ‘azīma and rukhṣa for each
Each aspect has a strict method ('azīma) and a relaxed method (rukhṣa). The text explains the methods for hearing in detail.
For hearing, the strict method is the student reading back; a concession is the teacher reading directly; another is written correspondence.
3
Analyze the hearing aspect
Three methods: (1) student reads to teacher (azima, more precautionary), (2) teacher reads to student (rukhṣa, some say better but answer is first is precautionary), (3) teacher writes a letter (rukhṣa, permissible).
The text argues that method 1 is more precautionary because the student is more careful.
4
Apply to a scenario
Choose the method that ensures the most reliable transmission. For example, in a hadith class, the student reading back is the strict method.
The choice between azima and rukhṣa depends on the situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْفَاسِقِ فَإِنَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِسْلَامِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ الصِّدْقَ وَمِنْ حَيْثُ فِسْقِهِ يَحْتَمِلُ الْكَذِبَ فَهُوَ وَاجِبُ التَّوَقُفِ. وَقِسْمٌ يَتَرَجَّحُ أَحَدُ احْتِمَالَيْهِ عَلَى الْآخَرِ كَخَبَرِ الْعَدْلِ الْمُسْتَجْمِعِ لِلشَّرَائِطِ. وَلِهَذَا النَّوْعِ الْآخِرِ الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهُ أَطْرَافٌ: فَلَهُ طَرَفُ السَّمَاعِ بِأَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْحَدِيثَ عَنِ الْمُحَدِّثِ أَوْ لَا، وَطَرَفُ الْحِفْظِ بِأَنْ يَحْفَظَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ أَوَّلِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ، وَطَرَفُ الْأَدَاءِ بِأَنْ يُلْقِيَهُ إِلَى الْآخَرِ لِيَتَفَرَّغَ ذِمَّتُهُ. وَفِي كُلِّ طَرَفٍ مِنْهَا عَزِيمَةٌ وَرُخْصَةٌ. فَالْأَوَّلُ طَرَفُ السَّمَاعِ: وَذَلِكَ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ عَزِيمَةً وَهُوَ مَا يَكُونُ مِنْ جِنْسِ الْإِسْمَاعِ: أَنْ يَسْمَعَ التِّلْمِيذُ عِبَارَةَ الْحَدِيثِ مُشَافَهَةً أَوْ مُغَايَبَةً: بِأَنْ تَقْرَأَ عَلَى الْمُحَدِّثِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ أَوْ حِفْظٍ وَهُوَ يَسْمَعُ، ثُمَّ تَقُولُ لَهُ: أَهُوَ كَمَا قَرَأْتُ عَلَيْكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: نَعَمْ. وَهَذَا أَحْوَطُ لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا قَرَأَ بِنَفْسِهِ كَانَ أَشَدَّ عِنَايَةً فِي ضَبْطِ الْمَتْنِ لِأَنَّهُ عَامِلٌ لِنَفْسِهِ وَالْمُحَدِّثُ عَامِلٌ لِغَيْرِهِ. أَوْ يَقْرَأَ عَلَيْكَ الْمُحَدِّثُ بِنَفْسِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ أَوْ حِفْظٍ وَأَنْتَ تَسْمَعُهُ. وَقِيلَ هَذَا أَحْسَنُ لِأَنَّهُ كَانَ وَظِيفَةَ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَهُوَ مَأْمُونٌ عَنِ الْخَطَاءِ وَالنِّسْيَانِ. وَالْجَوَابُ أَنَّهُ وَالنَّسْيَانِ[؟] وَالِاحْتِيَاطُ فِي حَقِّنَا هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ. أَوْ يَكْتُبَ إِلَيْكَ كِتَابًا عَلَى رَسْمِ الْكِتَابِ: بِأَنْ يَكْتُبَ قَبْلَ التَّسْمِيَةِ مِنْ فُلَانِ بْنِ فُلَانٍ إِلَى فُلَانِ بْنِ فُلَانٍ، ثُمَّ يُسَمِّي وَيُثَنِّي وَيَذْكُرُ فِيهِ حَدَّثَنِي فُلَانُ بْنُ فُلَانٍ إِلَى أَنْ يَتَّصِلَ بِالرَّسُولِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وَيَذْكُرُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مَتْنَ الْحَدِيثِ، ثُمَّ يَقُولُ فِيهِ: إِذَا بَلَغَكَ كِتَابِي هَذَا وَفَهِمْتَهُ فَحَدِّثْ بِهِ عَنِّي. فَهَذَا مِنَ الْغَائِبِ كَالْخِطَابِ مِنَ الْحَاضِرِ فِي جَوَازِ الرِّوَايَةِ.
The [report] of the fasiq: indeed from the aspect of his Islam it may be true, and from the aspect of his sinfulness it may be false, so it is obligatory to suspend [judgment]. And a type in which one of its two probabilities outweighs the other, like the report of the just [narrator] who fulfills the conditions. And for this last type, which is intended, there are aspects: it has the aspect of hearing, that he hears the hadith from the muhaddith or not; and the aspect of memorization, that he memorizes it after that from beginning to end; and the aspect of delivery, that he conveys it to another to free his responsibility. And in each aspect there is a strict method and a concession. The first is the aspect of hearing: that either it is strict, which is of the kind of making hear: that the student hears the wording of the hadith orally or absently: by reading to the muhaddith from a book or memory while he listens, then you say to him: 'Is it as I read to you?' He says: 'Yes.' This is more precautionary because when he reads himself, he is more careful in preserving the text, since he is acting for himself, while the muhaddith is acting for another. Or the muhaddith reads to you himself from a book or memory while you listen. It is said this is better, because it was the practice of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and he was protected from error and forgetfulness. The answer is that he and forgetfulness[?] and precaution for us is the first. Or he writes to you a letter in the form of writing: that he writes before the basmalah: 'From so-and-so son of so-and-so to so-and-so son of so-and-so', then he says the basmalah and praises and mentions in it: 'So-and-so son of so-and-so narrated to me' until he connects to the Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace, and after that he mentions the text of the hadith, then he says in it: 'When this my letter reaches you and you understand it, then narrate it from me.' So this from the absent is like speech from the present regarding the permissibility of narration.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of khabar (report) in Hanafi usul. It first divides khabar into four types: (1) that whose truth is known necessarily (e.g., the Prophet's report); (2) that whose falsehood is known necessarily (e.g., Pharaoh's claim of divinity); (3) that which is equally probable of truth and falsehood (e.g., the report of a fasiq, which is muhtamil and thus wājib al-tawaqquf - must be suspended); (4) that where one probability outweighs the other (e.g., a just narrator's report). The passage focuses on the fourth type, which is the basis for accepting ahad reports. It then explains three aspects (atrāf) of this fourth type: (a) samā‘ (hearing), (b) hifz (memorization), and (c) adā’ (delivery). For each, there is a strict method ('azīma) and a concession (rukhṣa). The hearing aspect is elaborated with three methods: (1) the student reads back to the teacher (more precautionary), (2) the teacher reads to the student (some say better because it was the Prophet's way, but the answer is that first method is more precautionary for us), (3) the teacher writes a letter with full isnad and instructs the recipient to narrate it. This last method is permissible as a form of riwāya. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each division and method with Hanafi precision.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or narration that can be true or false; a statement that conveys information about a past event.
واجب التوقف (wājib al-tawaqquf): Suspending judgment; neither accepting nor rejecting the report until further evidence.
عدل (ʿadl): A just, reliable narrator who fulfills the conditions of probity (taqdīs) and does not commit major sins or persist in minor ones.
سماع (samāʿ): The act of hearing the hadith from the teacher, either directly or through reading back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which method of hearing is considered the most precautionary ('azīma)?
A) The teacher reads to the student
B) The student reads to the teacher
C) The teacher sends a written letter
D) All methods are equally precautionary

Key Takeaway
For reliable transmission, the student reading back to the teacher is the strictest method of hearing (samā‘).

Classification of Reports and Methods of Hearing in Hanafi Usul
Classification of reports and methods of hearing in hadith transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of khabar in Hanafi usul, identify the three aspects of the fourth type, and apply the four determined methods of hearing to evaluate the reliability of a transmitted report.

Core Idea
A report where truth outweighs falsehood requires three aspects: hearing, memorization, delivery—each with determined and concessional methods.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar classifies reports (khabar) according to Hanafi usul, focusing on the fourth type—the report of a just transmitter where one probability outweighs another. This type is foundational for accepting hadith as evidence. The passage then details the three required aspects (atraf) of such a report and elaborates on the determined methods (ʿazīma) for the first aspect, hearing (samāʿ). Understanding these methods is vital for evaluating chains of transmission and the admissibility of reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth type of khabar and its precondition
Recognize that the fourth type refers to reports where one of two probabilities outweighs the other (e.g., from a just narrator).
The previous three types are not detailed here but include mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad without preponderance.
2
List the three aspects (atraf) of this type
The three aspects are: hearing (samāʿ), memorization (ḥifẓ), and delivery (adāʾ). Each is essential for the report to be considered reliable.
These aspects apply only to the fourth type.
3
Distinguish between determined (ʿazīma) and concessional (rukḥṣa) methods
For each aspect, there is a stricter ʿazīma method and a more lenient rukḥṣa method. The passage focuses on ʿazīma for hearing.
Rukḥṣa methods include ijaza, munawala, etc., which are not fully treated here.
4
Describe the four determined methods for the aspect of hearing
The four ʿazīma methods are: (1) student reads to teacher, (2) teacher reads to student, (3) teacher writes a letter, (4) teacher sends a messenger. The first two are considered more complete.
The passage explains why (1) is more cautious than (2) for non-infallible narrators.
5
Analyze the debate regarding the first two methods
Some prefer teacher-read because it follows prophetic practice; Hanafis prefer student-read because it ensures greater attention to the text, which is more cautious (ahwat).
This reflects a legitimate ikhtilaf within the tradition.

فاسق کی خر کیونکہ فاسق کی خبر کیونکہ فاسق اسلام اور مسلمان ہونے کی حیثیت سے اس کی خبر صدق کا احتمال رکھتی ہے اور فسق و فجور میں آلودگی کی حیثیت سے کذب کا احتمال رکھتی ہے لہذا ایسی خبر واجب التوقفہ ہے۔ وَقِسْمٌ لِيَتَرَجَعَ احد احتمالَيْهِ : ۔ اور چوتھی قسم وہ خبر ہے جس کے دو احتمال میں سے ایک احتمال دوسرے پر غلب ہو جیسے اس عادل کی خیر جس میں روایت کی ساری شرطیں جمع ہوں اور اس آخری قسم کے تین اطراف میں اور یہی قسم یہاں مقصود ہے (۱) طرف السماع بایں طور کے محدث سے حدیث کو سنا ہے یا نہیں (۲) طرف الحفظ بائیں طور کے اس حدیت کو از اول تا آخر سننے کے بعد حفظ کر لیا ہے۔ (۳) طرف الاداء۔ دوسرے تک پہنچا دیا ہو تا کہ اس کا ذمہ فارغ ہو جائے (یعنی ذمہ داری پوری ہو جائے ) اور ان اطراف قلعہ میں ایک جانب مزمت کی ہے اور دوسر کی جانب رخصت کی ہے۔ فالأول طرت السماع : پہلی طرف سماع اس کی عزیمت یہ کہ وہ اسماع کی جنس سے ہو یعنی محدث شاگرد کو حدیث کی عبارت سنادے مشافیہ سنادے یا غائبانہ طور پر۔ بأن تقرأ على المُحدَث : ۔ اس طریقے پر محدث کے سامنے پڑھے خواہ کتاب دیکھ کر پڑھے۔ یہ بانی پڑھے اور محدث سن رہا ہو ۔ پھر پڑھنے کے بعد کہے کہ آیا یہ حدیث اس طرح پر ہے جس طرح میں نے آپ کے سامنے پڑھی ہے تو محدث کہے تم (ہاں) یہ طریقہ احوط ( زیادہ احتیاط رکھنے والا ہے) کیونکہ شاگر رجب خود پڑھے گا۔ تو متن حدیث کے ضبط کرنے میں زیادہ توجہ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ خود پڑھ رہا ہے۔ اور محدث عامل لغیرہ ہے۔ أوْ يَقْرَأُ عَلَيْكَ الْمُحدّث بنفسه (۲) یا اس طور پر کہ محدث تمہارے سامنے خود ہی پڑھے۔ خواہ کتاب دیکھ کر پڑھے یا زبانی پڑھے۔ اور تم اس کو سنتے ہو۔ بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ یہ طریقہ احسن ہے۔ یا کیونکہ جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا یہ طرز عمل تھا( معمول مبارک یہی تھا) اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پوری امت کے معلم تھے۔ اور خطا و نسیان سے مامون تھے اس لئے ہمارے حق میں طریقہ اول زیادہ احتیاط کا ہے۔
أَوْيَكْتُبُ إِلَيْكَ كِتَابًا على رسم الكتب (۳) یا اس طور پر محدث تحر یر ا تمہارے پاس ایک خط لکھ کر بھیج دے مثلا شروع خط کے انداز میں لکھے۔ از فلاں بن فلاں برائے فلاں بن فلاں پھر بسم اللہ لکھے اور شا لکھے۔ وَيَذْكُرَ فِيْهِ حَدَّثَنَى الخ جس میں حد معنی فلاں بن فلاں کے طریق پر حدیث کو ذکر کرے۔ یہاں تک کہ سند کو جناب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تک متصل کرے اس کے بعد حدیث کا متن تحریر کرے۔ ثُمَّ يَقُولُ فِيْهِ۔ پھر اس میں یہ لکھے کہ (اے طالب حدیث ) جب تمہارے پاس ہمارا یہ خطہ پہونچ جائے اور تم اسے سمجھ لو۔ تو تم اسے میری طرف سے بیان کرتے رہو ۔ یہ طریقہ کتابت غائب کی طرف سے ویسا ہی ہے جیسے خطابت کا طریقہ ۔ یعنی اس باب میں کہ روایت جائز ہے جس طرح حاضر کی جانب سے طریقہ خطابی جائز ہے اس طرح غائب کی جانب سے بھی جائز ہے۔
وَكَذَالِكَ الرِّسَالَةُ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ المُحَدِّثُ لِلرَّسُوْلِ بِلْغَ عَلَى فَلَانًا أَنْه قَدْ حَدَّثَنِي بِهَذَا الْحَدِيثِ فَلاَنُ بْنُ فُلاَنِ امْ فَإِذَا بَلَغَكَ رِسالَتِي هَذِهِ فَارُوعَنِّي بهذا الْحَدِيثِ فَيَكُونَانِ أَي الْكِتَابِ وَالرِّسَالَةُ حُجْتَيْنِ إِذَا ثُبَتَا بَالْحُجْةِ أَنْ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ أَنْ هَذَا كِتَابُ فَلانِ أَوْرَسُوْلِ فَلاَنِ عَلى مَا عُرِف فِي كِتَابِ الْقَاضِي هذِهِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَام للعَزِيمَةِ فِي طَرْفِ السَّمَاءِ وَالأَوْلَانِ أَكْمَلانَ مِنَ الأَخِيْرَيْنِ
The report of a fasiq: because the report of a fasiq, due to his status as a Muslim, has the possibility of truth, but due to his sinfulness, it has the possibility of falsehood, so such a report must be suspended. And a category in which one of two probabilities outweighs the other: and the fourth type is the report whose two probabilities one outweighs the other, like the report of a just person in whom all conditions of transmission are found. And this last type has three aspects, and this is the type intended here: (1) Aspect of hearing: whether the hadith has been heard from the narrator or not. (2) Aspect of memorization: whether after hearing from beginning to end it has been memorized. (3) Aspect of delivery: have you transmitted it to others to fulfill your responsibility. And these aspects include one side of determination and another side of concession. As for the first, hearing: its determination is that it be of the genus of making hear, meaning the narrator makes the student hear the wording of the hadith, either orally or in absentia. Such that you read before the narrator: this method is more cautious because the student himself reads, so he pays more attention to the text, and the narrator is just a listener. Or the narrator reads to you himself: some say this is better because the Prophet ﷺ acted this way, but the response is that the Prophet was the teacher of the entire ummah and infallible, so for us the first method is more cautious. Or he writes you a letter in the manner of written correspondence: he writes in the beginning 'from so-and-so to so-and-so', then basmalah, then writes 'hadathani' etc., connecting the chain to the Prophet, then writes the text, then says: 'when this letter reaches you and you understand it, then transmit it from me'. This method of writing is like the method of oration: just as transmission from a present person by oration is permissible, so too from an absent one. And likewise the sending of a messenger in the same way: the narrator says to the messenger 'convey to so-and-so that so-and-so narrated this hadith to me, so when my message reaches you, transmit it from me'. So these two, the book and the message, are proofs when they are established by evidence, as known in the book of the judge. These are four divisions of determination regarding the aspect of hearing, and the first two are more complete than the latter two.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains the classification of reports (khabar) in Hanafi usul, focusing on the fourth type where one probability outweighs the other, i.e., the report of a just transmitter. The passage then introduces the three aspects (atraf) of this type: the aspect of hearing (samāʿ), memorization (hifẓ), and delivery (adāʾ). Each aspect has a determined method (ʿazīma) and a concessional method (rukḥṣa). The commentary details the first aspect, hearing, and provides four methods of determination: (1) the student reads to the teacher, considered the most cautious because the student is actively engaged; (2) the teacher reads to the student, argued by some to be better due to prophetic practice, but the author rebuts this for our context; (3) the teacher writes a letter to the student; (4) the teacher sends a messenger. All four are valid when properly evidenced. The passage emphasizes the importance of direct oral transmission and careful attention to the wording, reflecting the Hanafi concern for precision in hadith transmission.

Key Terms
طرف السماع (ṭarf al-samāʿ): The aspect of hearing: whether the hadith has been directly heard from the narrator.
طرف الحفظ (ṭarf al-ḥifẓ): The aspect of memorization: whether the hadith has been memorized from first to last after hearing.
طرف الاداء (ṭarf al-adāʾ): The aspect of delivery: whether the hadith has been transmitted to others to fulfill responsibility.
عزیمت (ʿazīma): The determined or stricter method of transmission, involving direct oral contact.
رخصت (rukḥṣa): The concessional method, such as ijaza or munawala, allowing transmission without direct hearing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a determined method (ʿazīma) for the aspect of hearing according to the passage?
A) The student reads to the teacher
B) The teacher reads to the student
C) The teacher sends a written letter
D) The teacher grants ijaza (permission to transmit)

Key Takeaway
The fourth type of khabar, where truth outweighs falsehood, requires three aspects: hearing, memorization, and delivery; for hearing, the Hanafi school prioritizes the student-read method as the most cautious ʿazīma.

Ijaza and Munawala: Concessional Methods of Transmission
Explains the concessional methods of ijaza and munawala and the condition for ijaza to be a proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ijaza and munawala as concessional methods of hadith transmission and apply the Hanafi condition that ijaza requires prior knowledge of the book's contents to be a valid proof (hujja).

Core Idea
Ijaza without prior knowledge is a blessing, not a proof.

This passage introduces the concessional methods of hadith transmission, specifically ijaza (permission) and munawala (handing over). Unlike direct hearing (samāʿ), these methods do not involve face-to-face discussion. The Hanafi school stipulates a crucial condition: the recipient must already know the book's contents for the ijaza to serve as a valid proof. Otherwise, it is merely a benedictory act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concession
Recognize that the passage contrasts full hearing (samāʿ) with concessional methods. What makes these methods 'concessional'? They do not require direct oral discussion.
2
Define ijaza and munawala
Ijaza is permission to narrate a specific book. Munawala is the teacher physically handing over his hearing book. The passage notes that munawala requires ijaza, but ijaza can stand alone.
Munawala combines a tangible object with permission.
3
Apply the condition for ijaza
The passage states that for ijaza to be a valid proof (hujja), the mujaz lahu must be knowledgeable of the book's contents before receiving the ijaza. If not, it is only a blessing (tabarruk).
This condition is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Distinguish valid ijaza from tabarruk
An example: if a student has studied a book independently and later receives ijaza, it becomes a valid chain. If he intends to study after ijaza, it is not a proof.
The key factor is prior knowledge.
5
Note the Hanafi position
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on verification and knowledge in transmission. The school is cautious about accepting chains that lack personal acquaintance with the content.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَوْ يَكُونُ رُخْصَةً وَهُوَ الَّذِى لا أستمَاعَ فِيهِ أَى لَمْ تُكُن مُذَاكَرَةَ الْكَلامِ فِيْمَا بَيْنَ لَا غَيْبًا وَلَا مُشافَبَةً كَا الإِجَازَةِ بِأَنْ يَقُولُ الْمُحَدِّثُ لِغَيْرِهِ أَجَرْتُ لَكَ أَنْ تُرْوِيَ عَنِّى هَذَا الْكِتَابَ الَّذِي حَدْثَنِي فُلاَنٌ عَنْ فُلاَنٍ آه وَالْمُقَاوِلَةُ بِأَنْ يُعْطِيَ الشَّيْخُ كِتَابَ سمَاعِهِ بَيَدِهِ إِلَى الْمُسْتَفِيْدِ وَيَقُولُ هَذَا كِتَابُ سَمَاعِي مَنْ شَيْجِي فُلان أَجَزْتُ لَكَ أَنْ تُرْوِيَ عَنِّى هَذَا فَهُوَ لا يَصِحُ بِدُونِ الإِجَازَةِ وَالإِجَارَةُ تَصِحُ بِدُونِ الْمُنَاوَلَةِ فَالإجازة لاَبُدَّ مِنْهَا فِى كُلَّ حَالٍ وَالْمَجَارُ لَهُ إِنْ كَانَ عَالِمًا بِهِ أَيْ بِمَا فِي الْكِتَابِ قَبْلَ الإِجَارَةِ تَصبِحُ وَإِلا فَلا يَعْنِي إِذَا أَجَرْنَا بِكِتَابِ الْمِشْكَوةِ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ بِالْمُطَالَعَةِ بَقُوَّةِ نَفْسِهِ أَوْ بِإِعَانَةِ الشَّرُوْحِ أَوْ نَحْوِ ذَالِكَ وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ سَنَد صَحِيحٌ يَتْصِلُ بَالْمُصنفِ فَحِينَئِذٍ تَصِحُ إِجَازَتُنَا لَهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُكُن كَذَالِكَ بَلْ يَعْتَمِدُ عَلَى أَنْ يُطَالِعَ بَعْدَ الإِجَازَةِ ويُعَلِّمُ النَّاسَ كَمَا فِي زَمَائِنَا لَمْ تَكُن تِلْكَ - الإِجَازَةِ حُجَّةٌ بَلْ إِجَارَةُ تَبَرُكَ وَالثَّانِي طَرْفَ الْحِفْظِ وَالْعَزِيمَةُ فِيْهِ أَنْ يَحْفَظ الْمُسْمُوعَ مِنْ وَقْتِ السَّمَاعِ إِلى وَقْتِ الأَدَاءِ وَلَمْ يَعْتَمِدُ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ تمَعْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ كِتَابًا فِي الْحَدِيثِ وَلَمْ يَسْتَجِرُ الرَّوَايَةَ بِاعْتِمَادِ الْكِتَابِ وَكَانَ ذلِكَ سَبَبًا لِطَعْنِ الْمُتَعْصُبِينَ الْقَاصِرِينَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّيْنِ وَلَمْ يَفْهَمُوا وَرَعَهُ وَتَفْرُهُ وَلَا عَمَلَهُ وَهَدَاهُ. ترجمه تشريح وكذلك الرسالة المخ (۳) اى طرح قاصد بھیجنا مثلا ایک محدث قاصد سے کہے فلاں اسی خص کو میری جانب سے پہونچا دو کہ مجھ سے یہ حدیثے فلاں بن طلال محدث نے بیان کی اسے ہے لہذا جب یہ پیغام تمہارے پاس پہونچ جائے تو تم میری جانب سے اس حدیث کی روایت کرتا۔ فَيَكُونان پس یہ دونوں طریقے۔ طریقہ ارسال محط اور طریقہ ارسال قاصد حجتين إذا تبنا بالحجة اس وقت حجت ہوں گے جب یہ دونوں خود بھی دلیل سے ثابت ہوں۔ یعنی یہ ثابت ہو جائے کہ فلاں کا محط
Or it may be a concession, in which there is no hearing, i.e., there is no discussion of speech face to face or in absentia, such as ijaza, where the narrator says to someone: 'I grant you permission to narrate from me this book which so-and-so narrated to me from so-and-so...' And munawala: where the teacher gives his hearing book to the student and says: 'This is my hearing book from my teacher so-and-so, I grant you permission to narrate from me this.' So it is not valid without ijaza, and ijaza is valid without munawala. So ijaza is necessary in all cases. And the one given permission to narrate, if he is knowledgeable of the contents of the book before the ijaza, then the ijaza is valid; otherwise not. Meaning if we give ijaza for the book Mishkat after he has studied it by himself or with the help of commentaries, but he had no sound chain to the author, then our ijaza is valid. If not, but he intends to study after ijaza and teach people as in our times, then that ijaza is not a proof but a blessing. And the second aspect is that of memorization. The determination in it is that he memorizes what is heard from the time of hearing until the time of delivery, and does not rely on writing. For this reason, Abu Hanifa did not write a book in hadith and did not permit narration relying on writing. This was a cause for attack by biased shortsighted people until today; they did not understand his piety, his distinction, his deeds, and his guidance. Translation of Tashrih: Likewise the sending of a messenger, i.e., the narrator says to the messenger: 'Convey to so-and-so that so-and-so narrated this hadith to me, so when my message reaches you, transmit it from me.' So both these methods, the method of sending a letter and sending a messenger, are proofs when established by evidence, meaning it is established that it is the book of so-and-so or the messenger of so-and-so.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the aspect of hearing (samāʿ) by presenting the concessional methods (rukḥṣa): ijaza (permission) and munawala (handing over of the book). The text explains that ijaza is the minimal requirement for transmission, and it is valid only if the recipient already knows the book's contents. If the recipient has studied the book independently, then a later ijaza provides a valid chain. However, if the recipient has no prior knowledge and intends to study later, the ijaza is merely benedictory, not a proof. The passage then turns to the second aspect: memorization (ḥifẓ). The determined method is to commit the hadith to memory from first hearing until delivery, without relying on written notes. This was the practice of Imam Abu Hanifa, who did not write a hadith book and did not permit narration based solely on writing. His critics misunderstood his reliance on memory as a shortcoming, but the author defends it as a sign of his piety and precision.

Key Terms
الإجازة (al-ijāza): Permission granted by a narrator to another to transmit his book, even without direct hearing.
المناولة (al-munāwala): The teacher physically hands over his hearing book to the student, combining it with ijaza.
طرف الحفظ (ṭarf al-ḥifẓ): The aspect of memorization, where the determined method is to rely on memory, not writing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition does the Hanafi school require for an ijaza to be a valid proof (hujja) for transmission?
A) The teacher must read the entire book aloud to the student
B) The student must have already studied the book before receiving ijaza
C) The ijaza must be witnessed by two just witnesses
D) The ijaza must be in writing

Key Takeaway
A valid ijaza requires the recipient to know the book's contents beforehand; otherwise it is only a blessing, not a proof.

6 min
Memorization and Imam Abu Hanifa's Practice in Hadith
Discusses the importance of memorization in hadith transmission and defends Imam Abu Hanifa's reliance on memory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi emphasis on memorization over writing in hadith transmission and evaluate the criticism of Imam Abu Hanifa's practice of not writing a hadith book.

Core Idea
Memorization, not writing, is the determined method for reliable hadith transmission.

This passage also addresses the aspect of memorization (ṭarf al-ḥifẓ). The determined method is to commit the heard hadith to memory from the time of hearing until delivery, without relying on written notes. The author cites Imam Abu Hanifa's practice as a model: he did not author a hadith book and did not permit narration based solely on writing. This practice was misunderstood by his critics, but the author defends it as a sign of his deep piety and precision.

Guided Path
1
State the determined method
The passage says the 'azima (determined method) in the aspect of memorization is to memorize what is heard from the time of hearing until the time of delivery, without relying on writing.
This is the ideal standard for hadith transmission.
2
Identify the rationale
Relying on memory ensures personal connection and accuracy. Writing can introduce errors or become a crutch that weakens memorization.
The emphasis is on oral tradition.
3
Explain Abu Hanifa's practice
Imam Abu Hanifa did not write a book of hadith and did not permit narration based on writing. He transmitted entirely from memory.
This was his personal practice and a model for the school.
4
Evaluate the criticism
Critics attacked him for lacking a written book, but the passage defends him: they did not understand his piety, his distinction, and his deeds.
The author sees the criticism as shortsighted.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul
This emphasis on memory reflects the Hanafi school's priority on direct hearing and oral transmission, and wariness of relying solely on written texts.

Reliance on Written Hadith: Hanafi Imam Disputes
Dispute among imams on accepting written hadith without oral transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Muhammad regarding reliance on written hadith and evaluate the practical implications of their differences.

Core Idea
Written hadith is not accepted by Abu Hanifa for narration, but the Sahibayn allow it; Muhammad permits it as a concession.

This passage presents an important usul al-fiqh dispute about the validity of written hadith for narration and action. While the strict Hanafi position requires oral transmission, later Imams introduced concessions for ease. Understanding these positions helps us appreciate how the Hanafi school balances textual authority with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Positions
List each Imam's view on accepting written hadith: Abu Hanifa (rejects), Abu Yusuf & Muhammad (accept), Anas (conditional), and a narration from Muhammad (concession).
Note that the text begins with 'سواء' implying Abu Hanifa disallows both own and others' writing.
2
Understand the Basis
Why does Anas require the document to be in one's own hand or trustee's hand? Because of fear of tampering. Why does Muhammad allow even without possession? As a concession (rukhsah) for ease.
The basis is the reliability of the written record; strict view requires oral verification.
3
Distinguish Azima vs Rukhsah
Identify that Abu Hanifa's view is the azima (strict rule), while Muhammad's later narration is a rukhsah (concession) to facilitate people.
In Hanafi usul, rukhsah does not negate the azima but permits action under need.
4
Determine Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a hadith known only in writing cannot be narrated or acted upon; under the Sahibayn it can; under Muhammad's concession, even if the book is not in hand, it can be used.
This affects how scholars cite hadith from written sources in their fatwas.
5
Relate to Modern Scholarship
Consider how this dispute applies to modern printed books and digital hadith databases. Does possession of a book or file grant authority to narrate?
The issue is alive today with verified electronic texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سَوَاءٌ كَانَ خَطَّهُ أَوْ خَطَّ غَيْرِهِ وَعِنْدَهُمَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي يَجُوزُ لَهُ الرِّوَايَةُ وَيَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِهَا وَعِنْدَ أَنَسٍ يَجُوزُ الإِعْتِمَادُ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كَانَ فِي يَدِهِ أَوْ فِي يَدِ أَمِينِهِ فَلا يَجُوزُ إِنْ كَانَ فِي يَدِ غَيْرِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُؤْمَنُ عَنِ التَّغْيِيرِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ يَجُوزُ الْعَمَلُ بِالْخَطِّ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي يَدِهِ فَذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ رُخْصَةً وَتَيْسِيرًا عَلَى النَّاسِ
Whether it is his own writing or the writing of someone else, according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i, it is permissible for him to narrate and acting upon it is obligatory. According to Anas, reliance on writing is permissible if it is in his hand or in the hand of his trustee; it is not permissible if it is in the hand of someone else because it is not safe from alteration. According to Muhammad, acting upon writing is permissible even if it is not in his hand; he adopted this as a concession and ease for people.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a key dispute in hadith transmission regarding reliance on written documents. The text first states the position of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam al-Shafi'i: they allow narration from a written hadith and deem acting upon it obligatory, regardless of whose handwriting it is. Then it mentions the view of Anas ibn Malik, who permits reliance only if the document is in the narrator's own hand or that of a trusted person, because if it is in someone else's hand, there is fear of tampering. Finally, a narration from Imam Muhammad allows acting upon a written hadith even if it is not in his possession; he regarded this as a concession (rukhsah) to facilitate people. The omitted view of Abu Hanifa (indicated by the opening 'sawaa'' = same) is that he does not accept writing at all for narration, whether it is his own or another's. The passage thus highlights the spectrum of opinions within the Hanafi school on the validity of written transmission.

Key Terms
الخط (al-khatt): The written text of a hadith, as opposed to oral transmission.
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A concession allowing a normally prohibited or discouraged action under certain circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Imam Muhammad's view on relying on a written hadith that is not in his possession?
A) It is not permissible because of tampering risk.
B) It is permissible only if the handwriting is his own.
C) It is permissible as a concession for ease.
D) It is obligatory to act upon it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains multiple positions on written hadith, ranging from strict rejection to permissive concession, reflecting a balance between authenticity and ease.

Narrating Hadith by Meaning: Text Categories and Permissibility
Detailed conditions for narrating hadith by meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for narrating hadith by meaning by distinguishing between muhkam, zahir, and jawami' al-kalim texts and identifying who is permitted to paraphrase each category.

Core Idea
Narrating hadith by meaning is permissible only for muhkam texts for non-mujtahids, and for zahir only for mujtahids; jawami' al-kalim and ambiguous texts are never permitted.

This passage explores the nuanced rules of transmitting hadith by meaning, a critical issue for preserving the integrity of prophetic teachings. It distinguishes between strict adherence (azima) and concession (rukhsah), providing a detailed classification of texts that determines when meaning-based narration is valid. Understanding these categories is essential for scholars and students to correctly evaluate the authenticity and juristic weight of paraphrased narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of transmission
Recognize the contrast between azima (strictly transmitting exact wording) and rukhsah (concession to convey meaning). This sets the framework for the discussion.
Azima is always allowed; rukhsah is conditional.
2
Understand the general permissibility and the opposing view
Note that the majority (including Hanafis) accept meaning-based transmission based on Companion practice. Some scholars reject it due to the Prophet's gift of jawami' al-kalim.
The dispute is over the scope of permissibility, not the principle.
3
Analyze the detailed classification by the author
The passage breaks down texts into muhkam (clear, no alternatives), zahir (apparent but admits other meanings, e.g., 'amm), and categories like jawami' al-kalim, mushkil, mushtarak, and mujmal.
Each category has a different ruling on meaning-based transmission.
4
Apply conditions for each category
For muhkam: anyone with Arabic proficiency may transmit by meaning. For zahir: only a mujtahid may do so. For jawami' al-kalim, mushkil, mushtarak, mujmal: no one, not even a mujtahid, may paraphrase.
The example of 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' illustrates the danger of misinterpreting 'amm.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The ruling affects the validity of paraphrased narrations in juristic reasoning. A wrong paraphrase could lead to incorrect fiqh rulings.
Modern application: checking if a hadith cited by meaning is acceptable as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثَّالِثُ طَرْفُ الْأَدَاءِ وَالْعَزِيمَةُ فِيهِ أَنْ يُؤَدِّيَ عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي سَمِعَ بِلَفْظِهِ وَمَعْنَاهُ وَالرَّخْصَةُ أَنْ يَنْقُلَهُ بِمَعْنَاهُ أَي يَلْفِظَ لَفْظًا آخَرَ يُؤَدِّي مَعْنَى الْحَدِيثِ وَهَذَا صَحِيحٌ عِنْدَ الْعَامَّةِ لِأَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كَانُوا يَقُولُونَ قَالَ كَذَا أَوْ قَرِيبًا مِنْهُ أَوْ نَحْوًا مِنْهُ وَعِنْدَ الْبَعْضِ لَا يَجُوزُ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَخْصُوصٌ بِجَوَامِعِ الْكَلِمِ فَلَا يُؤْمَنُ فِي النَّقْلِ بِالْمَعْنَى مِنَ الزِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ وَالْحَقُّ هُوَ التَّفْصِيلُ الَّذِي ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِقَوْلِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُحْكَمًا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ غَيْرَهُ يَجُوزُ نَقْلُهُ بِالْمَعْنَى لِمَنْ لَهُ بَصَرٌ فِي جَوْدَةِ اللُّغَةِ إِذْ لَا يَشْتَبِهُ مَعْنَاهُ عَلَيْهِ بِحَيْثُ يَحْتَمِلُ الزِّيَادَةَ وَالنُّقْصَانَ وَإِنْ كَانَ ظَاهِرًا يَحْتَمِلُ غَيْرَهُ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ عَامًّا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّخْصِيصَ أَوْ حَقِيقَةً يَحْتَمِلُ الْمَجَازَ فَلَا يَجُوزُ نَقْلُهُ بِالْمَعْنَى إِلَّا لِلْفَقِيهِ الْمُجْتَهِدِ لِأَنَّهُ يَقِفُ عَلَى الْمُرَادِ فَلَا يَقَعُ الْخَلَلُ فِي نَقْلِهِ بِمَعْنَاهُ مَثَلًا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ بَدَّلَ دِينَهُ فَاقْتُلُوهُ كَلِمَةُ مَنْ عَامَّةٌ تُخَصُّ مِنْهَا الْمَرْأَةُ فَإِنْ نَقَلَهُ نَاقِلٌ وَقَالَ كُلُّ مَنْ بَدَّلَ دِينَهُ فَاقْتُلُوهُ يَشْمَلُ الْمَرْأَةَ أَيْضًا فَيَقَعُ الْخَلَلُ فِي الْأَحْكَامِ وَمَا كَانَ مِنْ جَوَامِعِ الْكَلِمِ بِأَنْ كَانَ لَفْظًا وَجِيزًا تَحْتَهُ مَعَانٍ جَمَّةٌ كَقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْغُرْمُ بِالْغُنْمِ وَالْخَرَاجُ بِالضَّمَانِ وَالْعَجْمَاءُ جُبَارٌ أَوِ الْمُشْكِلَ أَوِ الْمُشْتَرَكَ أَوِ الْمُجْمَلَ لَا يَجُوزُ نَقْلُهُ بِالْمَعْنَى لِكُلٍّ بَلْ لَا لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ وَلَا لِغَيْرِهِ أَمَّا فِي جَوَامِعِ الْكَلِمِ فَلِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ مَخْصُوصًا بِهِ فَلَا يَقْدِرُ أَحَدٌ عَلَى نَقْلِهِ وَأَمَّا فِي الْمُشْكِلِ وَالْمُشْتَرَكِ فَلِأَنَّمَا يَنْقُلُهُ بِتَأْوِيلٍ مَخْصُوصٍ لَا يَكُونُ حُجَّةً عَلَى غَيْرِهِ وَأَمَّا فِي الْمُجْمَلِ فَلِعَدَمِ الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى مَعْنَاهُ بِدُونِ الِاسْتِفْسَارِ مِنَ الْمُجْمَلِ
The third aspect is the mode of performance. The strictness therein is that he should transmit it in the exact manner he heard it, in both wording and meaning. The concession is that he should convey it by its meaning, i.e., utter another wording that conveys the meaning of the hadith. This is valid according to the majority because the Companions used to say: 'He said such and such' or 'close to it' or 'similar to it.' According to some, this is not permissible because he (peace be upon him) was distinguished with comprehensive speech (jawamiʿ al-kalim), so one is not safe from increase or decrease in meaning-based transmission. The truth is the detail mentioned by the author in his statement: 'If the hadith is muhkam (decisive) admitting no alternative, its meaning-based transmission is permissible for one who has insight into language proficiency, since its meaning is not ambiguous to him such that it might admit increase or decrease. If it is zahir (apparent) admitting alternatives, i.e., being general (ʿamm) admitting specification or being literal (haqiqah) admitting metaphorical interpretation, then its transmission by meaning is not permissible except for a jurist-mujtahid, because he grasps the intended meaning and thus no defect occurs in his meaning-based transmission. For example, his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' – the word 'man' is general from which women are excluded. If a transmitter transmits it and says 'Everyone who changes his religion, kill him,' that includes women as well, and thus a defect occurs in rulings. As for what is from jawamiʿ al-kalim, i.e., a concise wording containing many meanings, like his statement (peace be upon him): 'Profit goes with liability, and produce is against guarantee, and the beast is a loss' or the mushkil (ambiguous), mushtarak (homonymous), or mujmal (equivocal) – its meaning-based transmission is not permissible for anyone, neither for the mujtahid nor for others. As for jawamiʿ al-kalim, because he was specifically endowed with it, so no one can transmit it. As for mushkil and mushtarak, because one transmits it only with a specific interpretation that is not a proof for others. As for mujmal, because one cannot grasp its meaning without seeking explanation from the one who said it.'
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-hadith discussion on narrating hadith by meaning. It begins by defining two approaches: azima (strict adherence) which requires transmitting the exact wording, and rukhsah (concession) which allows conveying the meaning in other words. The author notes that the majority (al-ʿammah) accept meaning-based transmission, citing the practice of the Companions who would paraphrase. Some scholars reject it due to the Prophet's unique gift of concise speech (jawamiʿ al-kalim). The correct position, however, is the detailed one by the author: if the hadith is muhkam (clear with no alternative meaning), it is allowed for anyone with Arabic proficiency. If it is zahir (apparent but admitting other possibilities like generality or literalness), only a jurist-mujtahid may transmit by meaning because he can correctly identify the intended scope. The example of the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' illustrates the risk: the word 'man' is general but excludes women; transmitting 'everyone' would cause an error in ruling. Finally, jawamiʿ al-kalim, mushkil, mushtarak, and mujmal texts are completely excluded from meaning-based transmission, even for mujtahids, because of their unique nature, dependence on specific interpretation, or lack of clarity without further explanation.

Key Terms
مُحْكَم (muḥkam): A text that is clear and admits no alternative meaning.
ظَاهِر (ẓāhir): A text that is apparent but admits another possible interpretation, such as general or literal.
جَوَامِع الْكَلِم (jawāmiʿ al-kalim): Concise speech containing many meanings; a special gift to the Prophet.
رُخْصَة (rukhṣah): A concession permitting an action normally prohibited or discouraged.
عَزِيمَة (ʿazīmah): The strict rule that is normally required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the detailed view in this passage, who is permitted to narrate a ẓāhir hadith by meaning?
A) Anyone with Arabic proficiency
B) Only a jurist-mujtahid
C) Only a hadith specialist
D) No one

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of narrating hadith by meaning depends on the text's clarity and the narrator's expertise, a nuanced rule essential for preserving legal accuracy.

Ambiguous Criticism (الطعن المبهم) in Hanafi Usul
Clarifies that vague criticism does not harm a narrator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on ambiguous criticism and identify when it is accepted as valid jarh.

Core Idea
Vague criticism from hadith scholars does not harm a narrator; only specific universally agreed defects count.

In Hanafi usul, not every negative remark about a narrator is accepted as valid disparagement. This passage clarifies that ambiguous statements like 'this hadith is munkar' are not sufficient to reject a narrator unless the defect is clearly explained and universally agreed. Additionally, the critic must be known for sincerity, not partisanship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criticism type
Determine whether the criticism is vague ('majruh', 'munkar') or specific. Vague criticism is not accepted unless explained.
Vague means lacking detail about the defect.
2
Check for explanation (tafsir)
If the criticism is explained (mufassar) and the defect is universally recognized (muttafaq alayh), it may be accepted. If it is a matter of dispute among scholars, it is not accepted.
The passage uses the phrase 'bi ma huwa jarhun mathalan alayhi al-kull' meaning an agreed-upon defect.
3
Evaluate the critic's integrity
The critic must be known for sincere advice (nasiha) and free from partisanship. Criticism from biased 'deficient' (qasirin) people is disregarded.
This condition ensures fairness.
4
Apply the rule to the narrator
If the criticism fails any of these conditions, the narrator remains trustworthy and his narration is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالطَّعْنُ الْمُبْهَمُ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ الْحَدِيثِ لَا يَجْرَحُ الرَّاوِيَ عِنْدَنَا بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: هَذَا الْحَدِيثُ مَجْرُوحٌ أَوْ مُنْكَرٌ أَوْ نَحْوُهَا. فَيُعْمَلُ بِهِ إِلَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ مُفَسَّرًا بِمَا هُوَ جَرْحٌ مَثْمَلَ عَلَيْهِ الْكُلُّ لَا مَلَ فِيهِ بِحَيْثُ يَكُونُ جَرْحًا عِنْدَ بَعْضٍ دُونَ بَعْضٍ. وَمَعَ ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ الْجَرْحُ صَادِرًا مِمَّنِ اسْتَمَرَّ بِالنَّصِيحَةِ دُونَ الْعَصَبِيَّةِ. فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ بِجَرْحِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْقَاصِرِينَ. حَتَّى لَا يُقْبَلَ الطَّعْنُ بِالتَّدْلِيسِ، وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ: كِتْمَانُ عَيْبِ السِّلْعَةِ عَنِ الْمُشْتَرِي، وَفِي اصْطِلَاحِ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ: كِتْمَانُ التَّفْصِيلِ فِي الْإِسْنَادِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: حَدَّثَنَا فُلَانٌ عَنْ فُلَانٍ، وَلَا يَقُولُ: حَدَّثَنَا فُلَانٌ قَالَ: أَخْبَرَنَا فُلَانٌ. لِأَنَّ غَايَتَهُ أَنَّهُ يُوهِمُ شُبْهَةَ الْإِرْسَالِ، وَحَقِيقَةُ الْإِرْسَالِ لَيْسَتْ بِجَرْحٍ. فَتَبَهُهُ أَوْلَى.
And ambiguous criticism from the imams of hadith does not cause the narrator to be disparaged in our view: when one says: 'This hadith is defective (majruh) or objectionable (munkar) or the like.' So it is acted upon, unless it occurs explained as that which is a defect agreed upon by all, with no ambiguity in it, such that it is a defect according to some but not others. And along with that, the criticism must come from one who is known for sincere advice (nasiha) not partisanship. So the criticism of such deficient ones is not considered. So much so that criticism by tadlis is not accepted. Tadlis linguistically: concealing the defect of a commodity from the buyer. In the terminology of the hadith scholars: concealing the detail in the isnad, such that he says: 'So-and-so narrated to us from so-and-so' but does not say: 'So-and-so narrated to us: so-and-so informed us.' Because its utmost is that it gives the illusion of disconnection (irsal), and the reality of irsal is not a defect. So his [the narrator's] being clear (tabahhu) is more proper.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses two important topics in hadith criticism: (1) ambiguous criticism (ṭaʿn mubham) and (2) tadlis. The Hanafi position is that vague criticisms like 'this hadith is defective' or 'objectionable' do not actually harm the narrator's credibility. Such criticism is only accepted if it is clearly explained (mufassar) and constitutes a universally recognized defect. Additionally, the critic must be known for sincerity (naṣīḥa) rather than partisanship; criticism from biased individuals is disregarded. Regarding tadlis: linguistically, it refers to hiding a defect in merchandise; technically, it is when a narrator omits details in the chain, e.g., saying 'so-and-so from so-and-so' instead of explicitly stating who informed whom. The Hanafi view is that tadlis does not automatically make a narrator unreliable because it only creates a suspicion of irsal (disconnection) but is not actual irsal. Since irsal itself is not a defect (jarḥ) in the Hanafi school (mursal hadith is accepted under certain conditions), tadlis is not cause for rejection. The narrator's clarity (tabahhu) is preferred but not required.

Key Terms
الطعن المبهم (al-ṭaʿn al-mubham): Vague criticism that does not specify the defect
جرح مفسر (jarḥ mufassar): Explicit defect detailed in criticism
النصيحة (al-nasīḥa): Sincere advice; a condition for the critic

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule in this passage, when is vague criticism (ṭaʿn mubham) accepted?
A) Always, if the critic is a well-known hadith imam
B) Only if the criticism is explained (mufassar) and the defect is universally agreed
C) Never, under any circumstances
D) Only if the critic is from the Hanafi school of thought

Key Takeaway
Vague criticism does not harm a narrator; only specific, universally agreed defects from a sincere critic constitute valid jarh in Hanafi usul.

Tadlis as a Form of Criticism in Hanafi Usul
Defines tadlis and explains it is not a defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tadlis is not considered a defect (jarh) in Hanafi usul and apply the ruling to evaluate hadith narrators.

Core Idea
Tadlis is not a defect because it only creates suspicion of irsal, and irsal itself is not a defect in Hanafi school.

Tadlis (concealing isnad details) is often cited as a form of deception. However, the Hanafi school takes a lenient view: since tadlis only gives the illusion of disconnected chain (irsal), and mursal hadith is acceptable under Hanafi usul, tadlis does not automatically disqualify a narrator. This lesson unpacks the definition and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Define tadlis linguistically and technically
Linguistically, tadlis means hiding a defect in merchandise. Technically, it is omitting details in the chain, e.g., saying 'from so-and-so' without specifying hearing.
The passage gives the technical definition: كتمان التفصيل في الإسناد
2
Identify the effect of tadlis
Tadlis creates the illusion (yuḥimu shubuha) of irsal (disconnection), but it does not actually create irsal.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle on irsal
Since irsal (mursal hadith) is not considered a defect (laysat bi jarḥ) in Hanafi usul, the suspicion of it does not harm the narrator.
Irsal is accepted under conditions in Hanafi school.
4
Conclude on tadlis
Therefore, criticism based on tadlis is not accepted. The narrator's clarity (tabahhu) is preferred but not required.
The final phrase 'fatabahuhu awlā' indicates clarity is better but not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالطَّعْنُ الْمُبْهَمُ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ الْحَدِيثِ لَا يَجْرَحُ الرَّاوِيَ عِنْدَنَا بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: هَذَا الْحَدِيثُ مَجْرُوحٌ أَوْ مُنْكَرٌ أَوْ نَحْوُهَا. فَيُعْمَلُ بِهِ إِلَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ مُفَسَّرًا بِمَا هُوَ جَرْحٌ مَثْمَلَ عَلَيْهِ الْكُلُّ لَا مَلَ فِيهِ بِحَيْثُ يَكُونُ جَرْحًا عِنْدَ بَعْضٍ دُونَ بَعْضٍ. وَمَعَ ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ الْجَرْحُ صَادِرًا مِمَّنِ اسْتَمَرَّ بِالنَّصِيحَةِ دُونَ الْعَصَبِيَّةِ. فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ بِجَرْحِ هَؤُلَاءِ الْقَاصِرِينَ. حَتَّى لَا يُقْبَلَ الطَّعْنُ بِالتَّدْلِيسِ، وَهُوَ فِي اللُّغَةِ: كِتْمَانُ عَيْبِ السِّلْعَةِ عَنِ الْمُشْتَرِي، وَفِي اصْطِلَاحِ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ: كِتْمَانُ التَّفْصِيلِ فِي الْإِسْنَادِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: حَدَّثَنَا فُلَانٌ عَنْ فُلَانٍ، وَلَا يَقُولُ: حَدَّثَنَا فُلَانٌ قَالَ: أَخْبَرَنَا فُلَانٌ. لِأَنَّ غَايَتَهُ أَنَّهُ يُوهِمُ شُبْهَةَ الْإِرْسَالِ، وَحَقِيقَةُ الْإِرْسَالِ لَيْسَتْ بِجَرْحٍ. فَتَبَهُهُ أَوْلَى.
And ambiguous criticism from the imams of hadith does not cause the narrator to be disparaged in our view: when one says: 'This hadith is defective (majruh) or objectionable (munkar) or the like.' So it is acted upon, unless it occurs explained as that which is a defect agreed upon by all, with no ambiguity in it, such that it is a defect according to some but not others. And along with that, the criticism must come from one who is known for sincere advice (nasiha) not partisanship. So the criticism of such deficient ones is not considered. So much so that criticism by tadlis is not accepted. Tadlis linguistically: concealing the defect of a commodity from the buyer. In the terminology of the hadith scholars: concealing the detail in the isnad, such that he says: 'So-and-so narrated to us from so-and-so' but does not say: 'So-and-so narrated to us: so-and-so informed us.' Because its utmost is that it gives the illusion of disconnection (irsal), and the reality of irsal is not a defect. So his [the narrator's] being clear (tabahhu) is more proper.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses two important topics in hadith criticism: (1) ambiguous criticism (ṭaʿn mubham) and (2) tadlis. The Hanafi position is that vague criticisms like 'this hadith is defective' or 'objectionable' do not actually harm the narrator's credibility. Such criticism is only accepted if it is clearly explained (mufassar) and constitutes a universally recognized defect. Additionally, the critic must be known for sincerity (naṣīḥa) rather than partisanship; criticism from biased individuals is disregarded. Regarding tadlis: linguistically, it refers to hiding a defect in merchandise; technically, it is when a narrator omits details in the chain, e.g., saying 'so-and-so from so-and-so' instead of explicitly stating who informed whom. The Hanafi view is that tadlis does not automatically make a narrator unreliable because it only creates a suspicion of irsal (disconnection) but is not actual irsal. Since irsal itself is not a defect (jarḥ) in the Hanafi school (mursal hadith is accepted under certain conditions), tadlis is not cause for rejection. The narrator's clarity (tabahhu) is preferred but not required.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlīs): Concealing details in the isnad to give an illusion of direct hearing
الإرسال (al-irsāl): A narrator omitting the Companion and attributing directly to the Prophet
تبهه (tabahuhu): The narrator's being clear (explicit) in stating the chain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does tadlis not constitute a defect (jarh)?
A) Because the narrator may have repented
B) Because its ultimate effect is only suspicion of irsal, and irsal is not a defect
C) Because it is a common practice among all narrators
D) Because the Prophet himself allowed it

Key Takeaway
Tadlis is not a defect because it only suggests irsal, and irsal is not a defect in Hanafi usul; thus narrators who practice tadlis remain trustworthy.

Preference of Affirmative over Negative: The Case of Barirah
Applying the principle of al-muthbit muqaddam to Barirah's khayar dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of al-muthbit muqaddam to resolve conflicting reports and determine the ruling on khayar al-mu'taqah in the case of Barirah.

Core Idea
An affirmative report based on evidence overrides a negative report based on mere presumption.

In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi school resolved a conflict between two reports about the status of Barirah's husband. One report said he was a slave, another said he was free. Our objective is to understand the usul principle that gave priority to the affirmative report and the implications for the legal ruling on khayar al-mu'taqah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting reports
The passage mentions two reports: one that Barirah's husband was still a slave (nafi), and another that he had become free (muthbit). Identify which is negative and which is affirmative.
2
Analyze the basis of each report
The negative report is based on the original state (asl) – since he was originally a slave, the presumption is he remained so. This is 'zahir al-hal' (apparent state) without specific evidence. The affirmative report is based on direct knowledge (samāʿ and khabar).
3
Apply the principle of al-muthbit muqaddam
In Hanafi usul, when a muthbit reporter bases his report on evidence, and the nafi reporter only relies on presumption, the muthbit is given precedence. This overrides the original state.
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Therefore, Barirah's husband is considered free, and she has the option (khayar) to annul the marriage, regardless of his status. This contrasts with the Shafi'i position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زَوْجَهَا عَبْدًا أَمْ صَارَ حُرًّا؟ فَقِيلَ إِنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا عَلَى حَالِهِ وَهُوَ مُخْتَارُ الشَّافِعِيِّ حَيْثُ لَا يُثْبِتُ الْخِيَارَ لِلْمُعْتَقَةِ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ زَوْجُهَا عَبْدًا. وَقِيلَ قَدْ صَارَ حُرًّا وَهُوَ مُخْتَارُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ حَيْثُ يُثْبِتُ الْخِيَارَ لِلْمُعْتَقَةِ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ زَوْجُهَا عَبْدًا أَوْ حُرًّا أَوْ كَانَ مِمَّا يَشْبَهُ حَالُهُ. فَالْحُرِّيَةُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أَصْلِيَّةً فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَالْعُبُودِيَّةُ عَارِضَةٌ، وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا اتَّفَقَتِ الرُّوَاةُ عَلَى أَنَّ زَوْجَهَا كَانَ عَبْدًا فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ، وَإِنَّمَا وَقَعَ الِاخْتِلَافُ فِي الْحُرِّيَّةِ الْعَارِضَةِ، كَانَ خَبَرُ الْعُبُودِيَّةِ نَافِيًا لِلْحُرِّيَّةِ الْعَارِضَةِ وَمُبْقِيًا لَهُ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ، وَخَبَرُ الْحُرِّيَّةِ مُثْبِتًا لِلْأَمْرِ الْعَارِضِيِّ. فَخَبَرُ النَّفْيِ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهَا أُعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا عَبْدٌ مِمَّا لَا يُعْرَفُ إِلَّا بِظَاهِرِ الْحَالِ، وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا فِي الْأَصْلِ، فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ بَقِيَ كَذَلِكَ، وَلَيْسَتْ لِلْعَبْدِ عَلَامَةٌ وَدَلِيلٌ يُعْرَفُ بِهَا وَيُمَيَّزُ عَنِ الْحُرِّ. فَلَمْ يُعَارِضِ الْإِثْبَاتَ، وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهَا أُعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا حُرٌّ، لِأَنَّ مَنْ أَخْبَرَ بِالْحُرِّيَّةِ لَا شَكَّ أَنَّهُ قَدْ وَقَفَ عَلَيْهَا بِالْأَخْبَارِ وَالسَّمَاعِ، فَكَانَ عِلْمُهُ مُسْتَنِدًا إِلَى دَلِيلٍ. فَأَصْحَابُنَا قَدْ عَمِلُوا بِالْمُثْبِتِ وَأَثْبَتُوا الْخِيَارَ لَهَا حِينَ كَوْنِ زَوْجِهَا حُرًّا.
Was her husband a slave or did he become free? It was said he was still a slave, which is the choice of al-Shafi'i who does not establish the option for the freed slave woman except when her husband is a slave. And it was said he had become free, which is the choice of Abu Hanifa who establishes the option for the freed slave woman whether her husband is a slave or free or of ambiguous status. Freedom is the original state in the Abode of Islam, while slavery is accidental. But since all narrators agreed that her husband was in fact a slave, and the difference was only about the accidental freedom, the report of slavery negates the accidental freedom and keeps him on the original state, while the report of freedom establishes an accidental matter. So the negative report – that she was freed while her husband was a slave – is only known through the apparent state, i.e., that he was originally a slave, so the apparent is that he remained so, and a slave has no marker or evidence by which he is recognized and distinguished from a free man. Thus it does not contradict the affirmative report – that she was freed and her husband was free – because the one who reported freedom undoubtedly learned of it through reports and hearing, so his knowledge was based on evidence. Therefore our companions acted on the affirmative and established the option for her when her husband was free.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith dispute concerning Barirah (may Allah be pleased with her). The key usul principle applied here is 'al-muthbit muqaddam' (the affirmative takes precedence over the negative). The passage identifies two conflicting reports regarding the status of Barirah's husband at the time she was given the option (khayar) after being freed: one report that he was a slave, another that he had become free. The author explains the reasoning behind preferring the affirmative report (that he was free). The negative report is based on the apparent state (zahir al-hal) – since he was originally a slave, the presumption is he remained so. But this presumption lacks specific evidence. In contrast, the affirmative report is based on direct knowledge (the reporter heard or was informed). Therefore, the Hanafi school (our companions) acts on the affirmative, establishing khayar for Barirah. This example illustrates the usul rule that when a negative (nafi) is based on mere presumption (zahir) and an affirmative (muthbit) is based on dalil, the affirmative is given precedence.

Key Terms
مثبت (muthbit): A narrator or report that affirms a change from the original state, based on evidence.
نفي (nafi): A narrator or report that denies a change, asserting the continuation of the original state.
خيار المعتقة (khayar al-mu'taqah): The option granted to a freed slave woman to annul her marriage upon emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, why is the report that Barirah's husband was free preferred over the report that he was a slave?
A) Because the husband's freedom is the original state in Dar al-Islam.
B) Because the affirming reporter had direct knowledge, while the negating report relied on presumption.
C) Because the narrators agreed he was a slave.
D) Because the Shafi'i school also prefers the affirmative.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that an affirmative report based on evidence overrides a negative report based on mere presumption is exemplified in the case of Barirah's khayar.

Resolving Conflicting Reports: Khabar al-Nafi vs Khabar al-Ithbat
Explaining how to resolve contradictory reports using evidence and narrator credibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between khabar al-nafi and khabar al-ithbat, and apply the Hanafi method of tarjih to resolve conflicting reports using narrator reliability (ضبط and إتقان).

Core Idea
An affirming report (ithbat) based on evidence overrides a negating report (nafi) based on apparent state; when both conflict equally, prefer the more reliable narrator.

In Hanafi usul, conflicting reports about a legal matter are common. This passage from Ashraf al-Anwaar teaches us how to weigh evidence: reports that affirm a change (ithbat) with direct proof are stronger than those that merely negate based on original state (nafi). When two reports conflict and are equal in evidentiary basis, the narrator's reliability becomes decisive. Let us explore the examples of Barirah and Maymunah to see these principles in action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of reports
Recognize khabar al-nafi (negating report) which relies on the apparent original state (zahir al-hal) without evidence, and khabar al-ithbat (affirming report) which is based on direct evidence (dalil).
In the text, the slave's continued slavery is a nafi report; the report of freedom is ithbat.
2
Analyze the Barirah example
Understand why the affirming report (that she was freed) is given precedence: it is based on knowledge and evidence, while the negating report (that her husband remained a slave) is mere assumption from the original state.
The ruling: she has the option (khiyar) to annul the marriage if her husband is not freed.
3
Examine the Maymunah dispute
Two conflicting reports: Prophet married Maymunah while in ihram (khabar nafi, negating halal) vs while halal (khabar ithbat, affirming halal). Note that both reports have some evidence, so they conflict equally.
The text explains that the ihram report is based on observable signs (dress, nails, hair), making it a report known by evidence.
4
Apply tarjih based on narrator reliability
When two reports conflict equally, preference (tarjih) is given by examining the narrators. Ibn Abbas (reported ihram) is more reliable in precision and retention (ضبط وإتقان) than Yazid ibn al-Asamm (reported halal).
Thus the Hanafi position: marriage in ihram is permissible.
5
Extend the principle to water and food
The original states (tahara of water, halal of food) are nafi reports. A report of impurity or prohibition is ithbat based on evidence. If a reporter merely states the original state, his report is weak unless he also relies on evidence.
This shows the general rule: affirming reports with evidence take precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَبْدٌ مِمَّا لا يُعرف إِلا بِظَاهِرِ الْحَالِ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا الْأَصْلِ فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ بَقَى كَذَالِكَ وَلَيْسَت لِلْعَبْدِ عَلامَةٌ وَدَلِيْلٌ يُعْرَفُ بهَا وَيُمَيِّرُ عَنِ الحُرُ فَلَمْ يُعَارِض الإِثْبَات وَهُوَ مَا رُوى أَنْهَا أُعْتِقَتْ زَوْجَهَا حُرِّ لَأَنَّ مَنْ أَخْبَرَ بالحرية لاشك أنه قَدْ وَقَفَ عَلَيْهَا بِالأخْبَارِ وَالسَّمَاءِ فَكَانَ عِلْمُهُ مُسْتَقِدًا إِلَى دَلِيْلٍ فَاصْحَابُنَا هبْنَا عَمَلُوا بِالْمُثْبِت وَاثْبُتُوا الْخِيَارَ لَهَا حِيْنَ كَوْنِ زَوْجِهَا حُرُّ وَفِي حَدِيثٍ ميْمُونَةٌ مِثَالَ لِكَوْنِ النّفى مِنْ جِئْسِ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ وَذَالِكَ أَنَّ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ مُحْرِمَا فَتَزَوْجَ مَيْمُونَةً بِنَفْسِهِ وَلَكِنَّهُمْ اِخْتَلَفُوْا فِي أَنَّهُ مَلْ بَغِى عَلَى الإِحْرَامِ حِيْنَ النِّكَاحَ أَمْ نَقَضَهُ فَقِيلَ إِنَّهُ نَقَضَهُ ثُمَّ تَزَوْجَ وَبِهِ أَخَذَ الشافعِي حَيْثُ لا يُحِلُّ النِّكَاحَ فِي الإِحْرَامِ كَمَا لأَيُحِلُّ الْوَطى بالاتِّفَاقِ وَقِيلَ كان باقِيًا عَلَى الإِحْرَامَ حِيْنَ النِّكَاح وبه أَخَذَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةً حَيْثُ يُحل النِّكَاح لِلْمُحْرِمِ وَإِنْ حَرُمَ الْوَطِيُّ فَالإِحْرَامُ وَ إِنْ كَانَ عَارِضا فِي بَنِي آدَمَ وَالْجِلُّ أَصْلاً لكنة لَمَّا اتَّفَقَتِ الرُّوَاةُ الهُ كَانَ أَحْرَمَ الْفِتْةَ وَإِنَّمَا الْاِخْتِلَافُ فِي ابْقَائِهِ وَنَقْضِهِ كَانَ خَيْرَ الإِحْرَامِ نَافِيًا للحل الطَّارِئَ عَلَيْهِ وَخَبَرُ الْحِلَّ مُثْبِنَا لِلأَمْرِ الْعَارِضى فَخَبَرُ النُّفْي فِى بَابِ حَدِيْثِ مَيْمُوْنَةِ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ مِمَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ وَهُوَ هَيَّةُ الْمُحْرِم مِنْ لَبْس غَيْرِ الْمَخِيْطِ وَعَدَم تَقَلُّم الإظافير وَعْدَم حَلْق الشعر فهذا عِلَّمٌ مَستند إلى ديين مغارص الإِثْبَاتِ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ تزَوْجَهَا وَهُوَ حَلاَلُ لأَن مَن أَخْبَرُ بِهذا لأَسْنَكَ أَنَّهُ قَدْ رَأَى عَلَيْهِ لِبَاسَ الْمُحلِينَ وَزِيهُمْ فَلَمَّا تَعَارَضَ الْخَبَرَانِ عَلَى سَوَاءٍ اِحْتِيْجَ إِلَى تَرْجِيحٍ أَحَدِهِمَا بِحَالِ الرَاوِئ وَجُعِلَ رِوَايَةُ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ أَوْلَى مِنْ رِوَايَةٍ يزيد بن الأصم وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَجَهَا وَهُوَ حَلالَ لأَنَّهُ لا يَعْدِلُهُ فِي الضَّبْطِ وَالإِثْقَانِ فَصَارَ خَبَرُ النَّفْي هَبْنَا مَعْمُوْلاً بِهَذِهِ الْوَتِيْرَةِ وَطَهَارَةُ الْمَاءِ وَحِلُّ الطَّعَامِ مِنْ جئْسٍ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ مِثَالَ لِكَيْنِ الرَّاوِى بِمَا اعْتَمَدَ عَلَى دَلِيْلِ الْمَعْرِفَةِ وَفِي الْعِبَارَةِ مُسَامْحَةُ وَالأَوْلى أَنْ يَقُولَ وَطَهَارَةُ الْمَاءِ وَحِلُّ الطَّعَامِ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا تَشتَبِه حَالُهُ لَكِنْ إِذَا عُرِف أَنَّ الرَّاوِي إِعْتَمَدَ دَلَيْلَ الْمَعْرِفَةِ يَكُونُ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ وَبَيَانُهُ أَنَّ الأَصلَ فِي الْمَاءِ الطَّهَارَةُ وَفِي الطَّعَامِ الْجِلْ فَإِذَا تَعَارَضَ مُحْبَرَانِ فِيْهِ فَيَقُولُ اَحَدُهُمَا إِنَّهُ نَجسَ أَوْ حَرَامٌ فَلا شك أنَّهُ خَبَرٌ مُثْبت للأمْرِ الْعَارِضى مَا أَخْبَرَ بِهِ قَائِلُهُ إِلا بِالدَّلِيلِ ثُمَّ جَاءَ آخَرُ يَقُولُ إِنَّهُ طَاهِرٌ أو حَلالَ فَلا بُدْ مِنْ أَنْ يُتَفَحْصِ مِنْ حَالِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ خَبَرُهُ بِمُجَرَدُ أَن الأَصل فيه
A slave is from what is not known except by apparent state, and that is that he was a slave originally, so the apparent is that he remained as such. And there is no sign or evidence for the slave by which he is known and distinguished from the free. So the negating report does not oppose the affirming report, which is what is narrated that she was freed while her husband was a slave. Because he who reported freedom, there is no doubt that he came upon it by report and hearing, so his knowledge was based on evidence. So our companions acted on the affirming report and established the option for her when her husband was free. And in the hadith of Maymunah is an example of the negating report being from the type that is known by its evidence. That is, the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم was in ihram and married Maymunah himself. But they differed whether he had broken his ihram at the time of marriage or not. It was said he broke it then married, and this is what al-Shafi'i adopted, as he does not permit marriage in ihram just as he does not permit intercourse by consensus. And it was said he remained in ihram at the time of marriage, and this is what Abu Hanifa adopted, as he permits marriage for the muhrim while intercourse is forbidden. So ihram, even if it is accidental in humans and permissibility is original, but when the narrators agreed that he had worn ihram, and the difference is only in its continuation or annulment, the report of ihram becomes a negator of the accidental permissibility, and the report of permissibility becomes an affirmer of the accidental matter. So the negating report in the case of the hadith of Maymunah, which is what is narrated that he married her while in ihram, is from what is known by its evidence, which is the appearance of the muhrim: wearing non-stitched clothes, not cutting nails, not shaving hair. So this is a knowledge based on evidence. It opposes the affirming report, which is what is narrated that he married her while halal, because the one who reported that, you would think that he had seen on him the dress and manner of the halal people. So when the two reports conflicted equally, there was need for preference of one of them by the condition of the narrator. The narration of Ibn Abbas that he married her while in ihram was made preferable to the narration of Yazid ibn al-Asamm that he married her while halal, because he is not his equal in precision and reliability. So the negating report here is acted upon in this manner. And the purity of water and permissibility of food are of the type that is known by its evidence, as an example of the narrator relying on evidence of knowledge. There is leniency in the expression, and it would be better to say: purity of water and permissibility of food are of the type whose state is ambiguous, but when it is known that the narrator relied on evidence of knowledge, it becomes of the type that is known by its evidence. Its explanation: the original in water is purity, and in food is permissibility. So when two reports conflict in it, one says it is impure or forbidden, there is no doubt that it is a report affirming the accidental matter; its reporter does not report it except with evidence. Then another comes and says it is pure or permissible. Then one must investigate his condition: if his report is merely that the original in it...
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis from a Hanafi usul work, explaining how to resolve contradictory reports (khabar nafi vs khabar ithbat) using the principles of apparent state (zahir al-hal) and evidence (dalil). The author uses two examples: the case of Barirah and the case of Maymunah. In Barirah's case, the report that she was freed while her husband was a slave is an affirming report based on evidence, so it is given precedence over the negating report that assumes the husband remains a slave based on original state. This leads to the ruling that she has the option (khiyar) to annul the marriage if her husband is not freed. In Maymunah's case, the conflicting reports are about whether the Prophet married her while in ihram or while halal. The report of ihram is considered a negating report because it negates the original permissibility, and it is known by evidence (the appearance of a muhrim). The affirming report (that he was halal) is based on assumption. Since both reports conflict equally, the text teaches that preference (tarjih) is given to the more reliable narrator: Ibn Abbas's narration is preferred over Yazid ibn al-Asamm because of Ibn Abbas's superiority in precision and reliability. Therefore, the ruling adopted by the Hanafi school is that marriage is permissible for a muhrim. Finally, the author extends the principle to water and food: the original state of water is purity and food is permissibility. If one reports impurity or prohibition, that is an affirming report based on evidence. If another reports purity or permissibility merely based on original state, it is a negating report and may be given less weight unless the reporter also relies on evidence. The conclusion is that affirming reports (based on evidence) are given precedence over negating reports (based on apparent state) when they conflict.

Key Terms
خَبَرُ النَّفْي (khabar al-nafi): A report that negates a change from the original state, relying on the apparent condition (zahir al-hal) without evidence.
خَبَرُ الإِثْبَات (khabar al-ithbat): A report that affirms a change from the original state, based on direct evidence (dalil).
تَرْجِيح (tarjih): Preference given to one conflicting report over another based on narrator reliability, evidence, or other factors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the report that the Prophet married Maymunah while in ihram given precedence over the report that he married her while halal?
A) Because the report of ihram is based on the original state (zahir al-hal).
B) Because the report of ihram is based on evidence (observable signs of ihram) and its narrator Ibn Abbas is more reliable than the narrator of the halal report.
C) Because the report of halal is a negating report and thus always weaker.
D) Because Abu Hanifa personally favored that report without evidence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when reports conflict: (1) an affirming report based on evidence (ithbat) overrides a negating report based on assumption (nafi); (2) if both reports are equal in evidentiary basis, preference is given to the report of the more reliable narrator (tarjih bi al-rawi).

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
Khabar al-Nafi: The Principle of Report of Negation in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the principle of khabar al-nafi with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a report of negation (khabar al-nafi) is only accepted when supported by observable evidence, and distinguish it from a report of affirmation (khabar al-ithbat).

Core Idea
A report claiming the default is accepted only if the reporter observed it, not assumed it.

In Hanafi usul, not all reports are treated equally. When two narrators conflict, the key is whether the claim is a negation of a change (khabar al-nafi) or an affirmation of a change (khabar al-ithbat). This lesson unpacks the principle using the famous dispute about the Prophet's marriage in ihram and the practical example of water purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of reports
In the Maymunah hadith, one report says he married while muhrim (negation of halal), another says he married while halal (affirmation of a change). Determine which is khabar al-nafi and which is khabar al-ithbat.
Khabar al-nafi claims the default continues; khabar al-ithbat claims a change.
2
Understand the default ruling
For ihram, the default is halal; for water, the default is pure; for food, the default is permissible. The negation report claims the default state remains.
The default ruling is the original state before any change.
3
Recognize the need for evidence
A negation report must be based on direct observation (e.g., seeing the water source or the Prophet's ihram attire). If it merely asserts the default without evidence, it is rejected.
Merely stating the default is not evidence; the reporter must have observed the object.
4
Apply tarjih when reports conflict
When both reports have evidence, preference is given to the more reliable narrator (higher ضبط and اتقان). In the Maymunah case, Ibn Abbas is preferred over Yazid.
Tarjih is based on narrator qualities, not just the content.
5
Test with the water example
If someone says water is pure only because it's the default, his report is insufficient. If he observed the water from a clean source and handled it himself, his report is accepted as 'known by evidence'.
This applies similarly to food and other default rulings.
