نور الانوار جلد سوم مثال ہے جو دلیل سے معلوم کی گئی ہو صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ جناب بی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ سلم حرم تھے ہیں حضرت میمونہ رضی اللہ علما کا نکاح آپ نے اپنے سے کر لیا لیکن اس بارے میں اختلاف واقع ہوا ہے کہ وقت نکاح بھی احرام کی حالت میں تھے یا اس کو توڑ دیا تھا تو ایک قول یہ ہے کہ آپ نے اولا حرام کو توڑا پھر اس کے بعد نکاح کیا اس کو امام شافعی نے اختیار کیا ہے کیوں کہ ان کے یہاں احرام کی حالت میں نکاح حلال نہیں ہے جس طرح بالاتفاق بحالت احرام و طی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نکاح کے وقت احرام کی حالت میں تھے اس کو امام ابو حنیفہ نے اختیار فرمایا ہے کیوں کہ ان کے نزدیک محرم کے لئے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے ولی اگر چہ حرام ہے لہذا احرام کی حالت اگر بنی آدم کے لئے عارضی ہے اور حلال ہونے کی حالت اصلی ہے لیکن جب کہ تمام راوی اس امر میں متفق ہیں کہ نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے احرام باندھ رکھا تھا اور یہ صورت یقینی تھی البتہ اس بات میں اختلاف واقع ہو گیا ہے کہ آپ نے احرام باقی رکھا تھا یا توڑ دیا تھا تو احرام (یعنی محرم ہونے کی خبر نانی ہوگئی؟ اس حالت پر جو آپ پر طاری ہو گئی تھی اور حلال ہونے کی خبر (حدیث) امر عارضی کو ثابت کرنے والی ہو گئی۔
فَخَبَرُ النُّفْي فِى بَابِ حَدِيْثِ مَيْمُوْنَةِ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ مِمَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ وَهُوَ هَيْئَةُ الْمُحْرِم مِنْ لَبْس غَيْرِ الْمَخِيْطِ وَعَدَم تَقْلِيم الأظافير وَعَدَم حَلْق الشعر فهذا عِلْمٌ مُسْتَنِدٌ إِلَى دَلِيلٍ مُغَايِرٍ لِلْإِثْبَاتِ وَهُوَ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَهُوَ حَلَالٌ لِأَنَّ مَنْ أَخْبَرَ بِهَذَا لَا يَشُكُّ أَنَّهُ قَدْ رَأَى عَلَيْهِ لِبَاسَ الْمُحِلِّينَ وَزِيَّهُمْ فَلَمَّا تَعَارَضَ الْخَبَرَانِ عَلَى سَوَاءٍ اِحْتِيْجَ إِلَى تَرْجِيحٍ أَحَدِهِمَا بِحَالِ الرَّاوِي وَجُعِلَ رِوَايَةُ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ أَوْلَى مِنْ رِوَايَةِ يَزِيدَ بْنِ الْأَصَمِّ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَهُوَ حَلَالٌ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَعْدِلُهُ فِي الضَّبْطِ وَالْإِتْقَانِ فَصَارَ خَبَرُ النَّفْي هَاهُنَا مَعْمُولًا بِهَذِهِ الْوَتِيرَةِ. وَطَهَارَةُ الْمَاءِ وَحِلُّ الطَّعَامِ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ مِثَالٌ لِكَوْنِ الرَّاوِيَ بِمَا اعْتَمَدَ عَلَى دَلِيلِ الْمَعْرِفَةِ وَفِي الْعِبَارَةِ مُسَامَحَةٌ وَالْأَوْلَى أَنْ يَقُولَ وَطَهَارَةُ الْمَاءِ وَحِلُّ الطَّعَامِ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا تَشْتَبِهُ حَالُهُ لَكِنْ إِذَا عُرِفَ أَنَّ الرَّاوِيَ اعْتَمَدَ دَلِيلَ الْمَعْرِفَةِ يَكُونُ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ. وَبَيَانُهُ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِي الْمَاءِ الطَّهَارَةُ وَفِي الطَّعَامِ الْحِلُّ فَإِذَا تَعَارَضَ مُخْبَرَانِ فِيهِ فَيَقُولُ أَحَدُهُمَا إِنَّهُ نَجَسٌ أَوْ حَرَامٌ فَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّهُ خَبَرٌ مُثْبِتٌ لِلْأَمْرِ الْعَارِضِي مَا أَخْبَرَ بِهِ قَائِلُهُ إِلَّا بِالدَّلِيلِ ثُمَّ جَاءَ آخَرُ يَقُولُ إِنَّهُ طَاهِرٌ أَوْ حَلَالٌ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ أَنْ يُتَفَحَّصَ مِنْ حَالِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ خَبَرُهُ بِمُجَرَّدِ أَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِيهِ الطَّهَارَةُ أَوِ الْحِلُّ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ خَبَرُهُ لِأَنَّهُ نَفْيٌ بِلَا دَلِيلٍ. وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ أَخَذَهُ مِنَ الْعَيْنِ الْجَارِيَةِ أَوِ الْحَوْضِ الْعَشَرَةِ فِي الْعَشَرَةِ وَجَعَلَهُ بِنَفْسِهِ فِي الْإِنَاءِ الطَّاهِرِ الْجَدِيدِ أَوِ الْمُسَيَّلِ بِحَيْثُ لَا يَشُكُّ فِي طَهَارَتِهِ وَلَمْ يُقَارِقْهُ مُنْذُ أَلْقَى الْمَاءَ فِيهِ حَتَّى يُتَوَهَّمَ أَنَّهُ أُلْقِيَ فِيهِ النَّجَاسَةَ أَحَدٌ كَانَ هَذَا النَّفْيُ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا يُعْرَفُ بِدَلِيْلِهِ.

اور یہ تفصیل اس کی ہے کہ پانی کی اصل طہارت ہے اور طعام میں اصل حلت ہے جب اس کی خبر دینے والوں میں تعارض واقع ہوا آپس میں دونوں میں سے ایک کہتا ہے کہ نجس یا حرام ہے تو اس میں شک نہیں کہ یہ امر عارضی کو ثابت کرتی ہے اس قائل نے دلیل ہی سے کہا ہو گا پھر دوسرا آیا اور کہتا ہے کہ یہ طاہر ہے یا حلال ہے تو ضروری ہو گیا کہ اس راوی کی حالت کی تلاش و تحقیق کی جائے اگر اس کی خبر صرف یہ ہے کہ اصل اس میں طہارت یا حلت ہے تو اس کی خبر قبول نہ کی جائے گی کیوں کہ یہ نفی بلادلیل کے ہے۔
Ashraf al-Anwar Urdu commentary page 59. Example of something known by evidence: that the Prophet ﷺ was in ihram, and he married Maymunah رضي الله عنها. There is disagreement whether he was in ihram at the time of marriage or had broken it. One position (al-Shafi'i) says he broke ihram first then married, because marriage in ihram is not permissible just as sexual intercourse is not permissible. Others (Abu Hanifah) say he married while in ihram, because marriage for a muhrim is permissible even though intercourse is forbidden. Thus the state of ihram for humans is accidental, and the state of halal is original. But all narrators agree that the Prophet had ihram, but disagree whether he kept it. So the report of being muhrim (negation of halal) became about an accidental state, and the report of being halal became about establishing a change. So the report of negation in the case of Maymunah's hadith, which is narrated that he married her while in ihram, is from the type known by its evidence, which is the appearance of a muhrim: wearing unsewn clothes, not clipping nails, not shaving hair. This is knowledge based on a different evidence than the report of affirmation, which is that he married her while halal, because the one who reported that surely saw him wearing the clothes of the non-muhrim. When the two reports conflicted equally, preference was needed based on the narrator's condition. Ibn Abbas's narration (that he married while muhrim) was preferred over Yazid ibn al-Asamm's (that he married while halal) because he is not equal in accuracy and precision. So the report of negation here is acted upon in this manner. And the purity of water and permissibility of food are from the type of what is known by its evidence, an example of a narrator relying on evidence of knowledge. There is a leniency in the expression; it would be better to say: purity of water and permissibility of food are from the type of things whose state is ambiguous. But when it is known that the narrator relied on evidence of knowledge, it becomes from the type known by its evidence. Explanation: The original ruling for water is purity, and for food is permissibility. When two reporters conflict about it, one says it is impure or forbidden, there is no doubt that this report establishes the accidental state, and its reporter only reported it with evidence. Then another comes and says it is pure or permissible, then his state must be examined. If his report is merely that the original ruling is purity or permissibility, his report is not accepted because it is negation without evidence. But if he took it from a flowing spring or a ten-by-ten pool, and himself placed it in a pure new vessel or a channel such that he has no doubt about its purity, and he never left it since he put the water in it so that someone could suspect that impurity was thrown into it, then this negation is from the type known by its evidence. And this explanation is that the origin of water is purity and of food is permissibility. When there is conflict between two reporters, one says it is impure or forbidden, there is no doubt that this is a report establishing the accidental state, the reporter only said it with evidence. Then another comes and says it is pure or permissible, so his state must be investigated. If his report is only that the origin is purity or permissibility, his report is not accepted because it is negation without evidence.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains a key usul principle: reports of negation (khabar al-nafi) must be supported by observable evidence (dalil), not merely by asserting the default ruling. The author first presents a fiqh dispute about the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah while in ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i holds marriage in ihram is invalid, so the Prophet must have broken ihram first. Imam Abu Hanifah holds it is valid, so the Prophet remained in ihram. This dispute illustrates how conflicting reports can be reconciled. The passage then states that the hadith reporting the Prophet married while muhrim is of the type 'known by its evidence' (ma'ruf bi dalilihi), meaning the reporter observed the physical signs of ihram (unsewn clothes, uncut nails, unshaved hair). The opposing report (that he was halal) is based on direct observation of him wearing non-ihram clothes. When two reports conflict equally, we prefer the one from a more reliable narrator (Ibn Abbas over Yazid). Thus the report of negation (being muhrim) is acted upon. The author then gives another example: water and food. The default ruling is that water is pure and food is permissible. If someone claims water is impure or food is forbidden, that report is considered affirmative (muthbit) because it changes the default, and it must be based on evidence. If someone else claims it is still pure/permissible, we must examine if his report is merely citing the default (which is not accepted) or if he has actual evidence (e.g., he saw the water from a clean source and handled it himself, so his claim of purity is based on observation). In the latter case, it becomes a report known by evidence. This is a Hanafi approach to evaluating conflicting reports.

Key Terms
خبر النفي (khabar al-nafi): A report that negates a default ruling (e.g., claims impurity or prohibition).
ما يعرف بدليله (ma yu'rafu bi dalilihi): A report that is known by its evidence, i.e., the reporter has observed physical signs or has direct knowledge.
ترجيح (tarjih): Preferring one report over another based on narrator's qualities (accuracy, precision).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the water example, why is the report of purity accepted when the narrator observed the water from a clean source and handled it himself?
A) Because he is a trustworthy narrator.
B) Because he relied on direct observation, which constitutes evidence.
C) Because the default ruling is purity.
D) Because he cited the default.

Key Takeaway
A report of negation is only reliable if the reporter has direct evidence; otherwise, it is rejected as mere assumption.

The Four Categories of the Prophet's Actions (Af'al al-Nabi)
Classifies the Prophet's actions into four types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of the Prophet's actions and identify which category a given action belongs to, based on the Hanafi classification.

Core Idea
The Prophet's deliberate actions are legislated for us in four categories: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, fard.

This passage begins by classifying the Prophet's actions (excluding mistakes) into four legal categories. Understanding this classification is essential for usul al-fiqh because it determines how we derive rulings from the Prophet's practice (sunnah fi'liyyah). We explore the definition of each category and the condition that the action must be deliberate and not specific to the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the text, list the four categories: mubah (permissible), mustahabb (recommended), wajib (obligatory), and fard (obligatory with stronger evidence). Note that the passage groups wajib and fard as two types of obligation.
The passage says 'arba'atu aqsam' – four parts.
2
Understand the definition of each category
For each category, think about the legal consequence for the Ummah. For example, a mustahabb action is rewarded if done but not punishable if left; a fard action is required and its omission is sinful.
The text mentions that this division is relative to us (the Ummah), not to the Prophet himself.
3
Apply the condition of being deliberate and not specific
The classification applies only to actions that were deliberate (not mistakes) and not proven to be specific to the Prophet. Check if an action is a natural habit (e.g., way of sleeping) – such actions are not legislated for us in the same way.
The text excludes 'zalalah' (mistakes) from the categories.
4
Recognize the significance of this classification
This classification is foundational for usul al-fiqh because it determines the extent of iqtida' (following). Not all prophetic actions are equally binding; they range from obligatory to simply permissible.
Ali al-Karkhi's view on iqtida' (presumption of permissibility) will be discussed in another lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ الْمُصنف عَنْ تَقْسِيْمِ الْبَيَانِ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ السُّنَّةِ الْفَعْلِيَةِ اقْتِدَاءُ بِقَدْرِ الإِسْلامِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَذْكُرَها بَعْدَ السُّنَّةِ الْقَوْلِيَةِ مُتْصِلاً كَمَا فَعَلَهُ صَاحِبُ التَّوْضِيح فَقَالَ . فَصَلَ أَفْعَالُ النَّبِيِّ سوَى الزَّلَّةِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسام مُبَاحُ وَمُسْتَحَبُّ وَوَاجِبٌ وَفَرَضْ مِمَّا يُقتدى به وهى اسمُ لِفِعْلِ حَرَامٍ وَقَعَ فِيهِ بِسَبَبِ الْقَصْدِ لِفِعْلِ مُبَاحٍ فَلَمْ يَكُن فمندُهُ لِلْحَرَامِ ابْتِدَاءً وَلَا يَسْتَقِرْ عَلَيْهِ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوعِ كَمِثْلِ مَنْ أَحتَى فِي الطَّرِيقِ فَخَرُ مَنْهُ ثُمَّ قَامَ عَاجِلاً فَمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَصْدِهِ الْحَرُورِ وَمَا اسْتَقَرُ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَصْدِ مُوسى عَلَيْهِ السَّلام وَبالضَّرْبِ تَارِيْبَ القِطْبِي فَقَضى عَلَيْهِ بِالْقَتْلِ فَلَمْ يَكُن الْقَتْلُ مَقْصُودَهُ وَلَمْ يَبْقَ عَلَيْهِ بَلْ نَدِمَ وَقَالَ هَذَا مِنْ عَمَل الشَّيْطَان وَلَكِنْ هَذَا التقسيم بالنسبة الينا والا ففي حقه لَمْ يَكُنْ شتّى وَاجِبًا اصطلاحيًّا لأنَّهُ مَاثْبَتَ بِدَلِيلٍ فِيهِ شَبْهَةٌ وكانت دلائل كلها قطعية في حقه ثم انهم اختلفا في اقتداء افعال لم تصدر عنه سهوا ولم تكن طبعا مخصوصة به فقال بعضم يحب التوقف فيه حيث يظهر ان النبي عليه السلام على أى وجه فعله من الاباحة والندب والوجوب وقال بعضهم يجب اتباعه مالم يقم دليل المنع وقال الكرخى يعتقد فيه الاباحة ليتنها اه اذا دل الدليل على الموجوب والندب.
اور جب مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ بیان کی تقسیم سے فارغ ہو گئے تو امام فخر الاسلام نزدوی کی اقتداء ترجمہ و تشریح میں سنت فعلیہ کا بیان شروع فرمایا ہے حالانکہ مناسب یہ تھا کہ منت تولیہ کے بیان کرنے کے بعد متصل اس کو بیان فرماتے جیسا کہ صاحب توضیح نے ایسا ہی کیا ہے مگر بیان و توضیح میں مصنف کے اپنے رجحان کا بھی دخل ہوتا ہے اس لئے فرمایا۔
And when the author finished from the division of bayan, he began to explain the active sunnah, following the extent of Islam. And it would have been appropriate to mention it after the verbal sunnah consecutively, as the author of al-Tawdih did. So he said: A section: The actions of the Prophet, except for mistakes, are four categories: permissible, recommended, obligatory, and a fard from which we follow. And 'it' (i.e., a type) is a name for an action that is haram that occurred due to intending a permissible act, so his intention was not for the haram initially and he does not persist in it after it occurs, like someone who crosses the road and something falls from him, then he stands quickly, so the fall was not his intention and he did not persist in it, as was the case with Musa عليه السلام when he struck the Copt and killed him, so the killing was not his intention and he did not remain with it, rather he regretted and said 'This is from the work of Satan.' But this division is relative to us, otherwise with respect to him it was not something obligatory in the technical sense because it was established by a proof that had ambiguity, but all proofs were definitive with respect to him. Then they differed about following actions that did not occur from him mistakenly and were not naturally specific to him: some said it is necessary to stop until it is clear on which basis the Prophet did it from permissibility, recommendation, or obligation; others said it is obligatory to follow him as long as no proof of prohibition exists; and al-Karkhi said that permissibility is to be presumed unless evidence for obligation or recommendation is found.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of the Prophet's actions (af'al) into four categories: mubah (permissible), mustahabb (recommended), wajib (obligatory), and fard (obligatory with a higher status). It then discusses a special type of action that is haram (prohibited) but occurs due to an unintended consequence of a permissible act—this is not considered a sin because the intention was not for the haram and the person does not persist. The example of Musa (AS) killing the Copt is given. The text then moves to the debate about whether believers must follow the Prophet's actions that are not specific to him. Three views are presented: (1) stop until the nature is known, (2) follow unless there is evidence of prohibition, and (3) assume permissibility until evidence of obligation or recommendation. The Urdu commentary notes that the author began discussing the active sunnah after finishing the division of bayan, though it would have been more appropriate to mention it after the verbal sunnah, but authorial discretion plays a role.

Key Terms
سنة فعلية (sunnah fi'liyyah): The active sunnah, i.e., the actions of the Prophet that serve as a source of legislation.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the Prophet's actions in order to gain reward or fulfill obligations.
مباح (mubah): Permissible; an action that is neither rewarded nor punished.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three: wajib, mustahabb, and mubah
C) Four: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard
D) Five: adding haram

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's deliberate actions are divided into four legally significant categories: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard.

Unintended Haram Actions and the Dispute on Following the Prophet (Iqtida')
Discusses unintended haram and the iqtida' dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on unintended prohibited acts using the example of Musa (AS), and evaluate the three scholarly views on whether it is obligatory to follow the Prophet's actions.

Core Idea
Scholars differ on following the Prophet's actions: stop until clarity, follow unless prohibited, or presume permissibility until evidence of obligation.

This passage discusses two important topics: first, the concept that an action which is externally haram but occurred due to a permissible intention is not sinful, illustrated by the story of Musa (AS). Second, it presents a disagreement among scholars about iqtida' – following the Prophet's actions that are not specific to him. Understanding this ikhtilaf deepens our appreciation of hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Understand the story of Musa (AS)
The passage gives the example of Prophet Musa killing the Copt. His intention was not to kill; he struck the man and he died accidentally. Musa regretted and declared it from Satan. The ruling: the act is not sinful because the intention was for a permissible action (striking) and he did not persist in the haram.
This shows that some actions of the Prophet are not legislated for us because they were unintended.
2
Derive the principle from the example
The principle: if an action is haram in itself but occurs unintentionally as a side effect of a permissible act, and the person does not continue in it, it is not considered a sin. This distinguishes between deliberate and accidental acts.
This principle applies to everyone, not just prophets.
3
Identify the three views on iqtida'
The text presents three opinions among scholars: (1) tawaqquf – stop and wait until we know whether the Prophet's action was mubah, mustahabb, or wajib. (2) Ittiba' – it is obligatory to follow the action unless there is evidence that it is prohibited. (3) Ibahah – presume the action is permissible unless evidence indicates obligation or recommendation.
The third view is attributed to al-Karkhi, a prominent Hanafi usuli.
4
Analyze the basis of each view
Each view is rooted in a different usul principle: tawaqquf relies on the need for evidence before acting; the second view relies on the general command to obey the Prophet; the third relies on the principle of istishab al-ibahah (presumption of permissibility).
Al-Karkhi's view is more aligned with the Hanafi reliance on ibahah aslah.
5
Apply the views to a scenario
If you encounter a prophetic action with no additional evidence, under the first view you would do nothing; under the second, you would follow it as an obligation; under the third, you would consider it permissible to do or leave.
The Hanafi school generally follows al-Karkhi's view, making permissibility the default for prophetic actions.

Source Text

اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the Prophet's actions in order to gain reward or fulfill obligations.
اباحة (ibahah): Permissibility; the legal ruling that an action is allowed without reward or punishment.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspending judgment; refraining from ruling until evidence is clear.

Types of Prophetic Actions and the Hanafi Rule for Following Them
Defining the four types of Prophetic actions and the Hanafi rule for following them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of Prophetic actions (mubah, mustahabb, wajib, fard), define a slip (zallah), and apply the Hanafi rule for following actions whose legal basis is unknown.

Core Idea
Prophetic actions follow their basis: know the basis, follow accordingly; if unknown, assume ibaha.

In this passage, the author presents the foundational classification of the Prophet's actions (fi'liyyah) and clarifies how the Ummah is to follow them. He excludes slips (zallah) — unintended errors — as non-exemplary. He then addresses a key methodological dispute: what to do when the legal basis of an action (obligation, recommendation, or permissibility) is unknown. The preferred Hanafi view strikes a balance: follow where you know, assume permissibility where you don't.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories and the exclusion
The Prophet's actions (excluding slips) are mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard. Note that this division is from our perspective; for the Prophet himself, all his actions are based on decisive proofs.
2
Define a slip (zallah)
A slip is an unintentional forbidden act resulting from intentionally doing a permissible act, without persistence. Example: Musa (AS) striking the Copt. These slips are not to be followed.
3
Understand the dispute
When the basis of a Prophetic action is unknown (not inadvertent, not natural, not specific to him), scholars differed: some said stop until basis known; some said follow unless proof of prohibition; al-Karkhi said assume ibaha until evidence.
4
State the preferred (mukhtar) view
The author chooses: if we know the basis (wajib, nadb, ibaha), we follow on that basis; if we do not know, we assume the lowest level, ibaha, because the Prophet never committed haram or makruh.
5
Apply the rule
Given an action like the Prophet drinking while standing, if we find no evidence of the basis, we assume it is mubah for us, not wajib or mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ الْمُصنف عَنْ تَقْسِيْمِ الْبَيَانِ شَرَعَ فِي بَيَانِ السُّنَّةِ الْفَعْلِيَةِ اقْتِدَاءُ بِقَدْرِ الإِسْلامِ وَكَانَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَذْكُرَها بَعْدَ السُّنَّةِ الْقَوْلِيَةِ مُتْصِلاً كَمَا فَعَلَهُ صَاحِبُ التَّوْضِيح فَقَالَ . فَصَلَ أَفْعَالُ النَّبِيِّ سِوَى الزَّلَّةِ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسامٍ: مُبَاحٌ وَمُسْتَحَبٌّ وَوَاجِبٌ وَفَرْضٌ مِمَّا يُقْتَدَىٰ بِهِ. وَهِيَ اسْمُ لِفِعْلِ حَرَامٍ وَقَعَ فِيهِ بِسَبَبِ الْقَصْدِ لِفِعْلِ مُبَاحٍ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ قَصْدُهُ لِلْحَرَامِ ابْتِدَاءً وَلَا يَسْتَقِرُّ عَلَيْهِ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوعِ كَمِثْلِ مَنْ أَحْتَى فِي الطَّرِيقِ فَخَرَّ مِنْهُ ثُمَّ قَامَ عَاجِلاً فَمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَصْدِهِ الْحَرَامَ وَمَا اسْتَقَرَّ عَلَيْهِ. كَمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَصْدِ مُوسَىٰ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ بِالضَّرْبِ تَأْدِيبَ الْقِبْطِيِّ فَقَتَلَهُ فَلَمْ يَكُنِ الْقَتْلُ مَقْصُودَهُ وَلَمْ يَبْقَ عَلَيْهِ بَلْ نَدِمَ وَقَالَ هَٰذَا مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ. وَلَكِنْ هَذَا التَّقْسِيمُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا، وَإِلَّا فَفِي حَقِّهِ لَمْ يَكُنْ شَيْءٌ وَاجِبًا اصْطِلَاحِيًّا لِأَنَّهُ مَا ثَبَتَ بِدَلِيلٍ فِيهِ شُبْهَةٌ، وَكَانَتْ دَلَائِلُهُ كُلُّهَا قَطْعِيَّةً فِي حَقِّهِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّهُمُ اخْتَلَفُوا فِي اقْتِدَاءِ أَفْعَالٍ لَمْ تَصْدُرْ عَنْهُ سَهْوًا وَلَمْ تَكُنْ طَبْعًا مُخْتَصَّةً بِهِ. فَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: يَجِبُ التَّوَقُّفُ فِيهِ حَتَّىٰ يَظْهَرَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّىٰ اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلَىٰ أَيِّ وَجْهٍ فَعَلَهُ مِنَ الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالنَّدْبِ وَالْوُجُوبِ. وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: يَجِبُ اتِّبَاعُهُ مَا لَمْ يَقُمْ دَلِيلُ الْمَنْعِ. وَقَالَ الْكَرْخِيُّ: يَعْتَقِدُ فِيهِ الْإِبَاحَةَ لِيَتَبَيَّنَ، اهـ إِذَا دَلَّ الدَّلِيلُ عَلَى الْوُجُوبِ وَالنَّدْبِ. اور جب مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ بیان کی تقسیم سے فارغ ہو گئے تو امام فخر الاسلام نزدوی کی اقتداء ترجمہ و تشریح میں سنت فعلیہ کا بیان شروع فرمایا ہے حالانکہ مناسب یہ تھا کہ سنت قولیہ کے بیان کرنے کے بعد متصل اس کو بیان فرماتے جیسا کہ صاحب توضیح نے ایسا ہی کیا ہے مگر بیان و توضیح میں مصنف کے اپنے رجحان کا بھی دخل ہوتا ہے اس لئے فرمایا۔ اشرف الانوار شرح اردو 41 نور الانوار جلد سوم مبحث افعال النبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم فصل أَفْعَالُ النَّبِيِّ سِوَى الزَّلَّةِ الْخ - فصل یعنی نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے افعال کے سوائے لغزشوں کے چار قسمیں ہیں۔ مباح، مستحب، واجب اور فرض۔ لغزشوں کا استثنا اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ یہ باب ان افعال کے بیان کا ہے جو امت کی اقتداء کی غرض سے صادر ہوئے اور لغزشیں وہ افعال نہیں کہ ان کی اقتداء کی جائے۔ اور لغزش سے مراد اس جگہ یہ ہے کہ کوئی ممنوع شرعی صادر ہو جائے فعل مباح کے ارادہ سے (یعنی ارادہ سے پہلے اس فعل ممنوع کے کرنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو) اور صادر ہونے کے بعد اس پر قائم نہ رہے، جیسے کہ کوئی شخص راستہ میں چلتے ہوئے جھکا اور جھکتے ہی بے ارادہ میں گر پڑا اور گرتے ہی فوراً کھڑا ہو گیا تو اس شخص کا ارادہ گرنے کا نہ تھا اور گرنے کے بعد وہ قرار نہیں رہا بلکہ فوراً کھڑا ہو گیا۔ جس طرح حضرت سیدنا موسیٰ علیہ السلام کا قصد قبطی کو مارنے سے تادیب تھا، اس کے ہلاک کرنے کا نہ تھا، اور موسیٰ علیہ السلام اس پر قائم نہ رہے بلکہ فوراً نادم ہوئے اور فرمایا: "هَٰذَا مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ"۔ وَلَكِنْ هَذَا التَّقْسِيمُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا - لیکن مذکورہ تقسیم ہمارے لحاظ سے ہے، ورنہ کوئی چیز جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لحاظ سے کوئی عمل اصطلاحی واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اصطلاح میں واجب اس حکم کو کہتے ہیں جو ایسی حدیث سے ثابت ہو جس کے ثبوت میں شبہ ہو، اور آپ کے حق میں تمام دلائل قطعی ہیں۔ پھر علماء نے ان افعال کی اقتداء کے بارے میں باہم اختلاف کیا ہے جو افعال آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے نہ سہواً صادر ہوئے، نہ وہ افعال طبیعی تھے اور نہ آپ کے ساتھ مخصوص تھے۔ تو بعض نے کہا کہ ایسے افعال میں توقف واجب ہے یہاں تک کہ ظاہر ہو جائے کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے کس وجہ سے یہ افعال کئے ہیں، اباحت کی وجہ سے یا ندب کی وجہ سے یا وجوب کی وجہ سے۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ آپ کی اتباع واجب ہے جب تک منع پر کوئی دلیل نہ قائم ہو جائے۔ اور امام کرخی کا قول یہ ہے کہ اس فعل میں اباحت کا عقیدہ رکھے کیونکہ یہ یقینی ہے لیکن جب وجوب یا استحباب کی دلیل مل جائے تو ان وجوہات کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ وَالْمُصَنِّفُ تَرَكَ هَذَا كُلَّهُ وَبَيَّنَ مَا هُوَ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَهُ فَقَالَ: وَالصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا أَنَّ مَا عَلِمْنَا مِنْ أَفْعَالِهِ صَلَّىٰ اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَاقِعًا عَلَىٰ جِهَةٍ مِنَ الْوُجُوبِ وَالنَّدْبِ أَوِ الْإِبَاحَةِ يَقْتَدِي بِهِ فِي إِيقَاعِهِ عَلَىٰ تِلْكَ الْجِهَةِ حَتَّىٰ يَقُومَ دَلِيلُ الْخُصُوصِ. فَمَا كَانَ وَاجِبًا عَلَيْهِ يَكُونُ وَاجِبًا عَلَيْنَا، وَمَا كَانَ مَنْدُوبًا عَلَيْهِ يَكُونُ مَنْدُوبًا عَلَيْنَا، وَمَا كَانَ مُبَاحًا لَهُ يَكُونُ مُبَاحًا لَنَا. وَمَا لَمْ نَعْلَمْ عَلَىٰ أَيَّةِ جِهَةٍ فَعَلَهُ قُلْنَا: فَعَلَهُ عَلَىٰ أَدْنَىٰ مَنَازِلِ أَفْعَالِهِ وَهُوَ الْإِبَاحَةُ، لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَفْعَلْ حَرَامًا أَوْ مَكْرُوهًا الْبَتَّةَ، فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُبَاحًا. وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ تَقْسِيمِ السُّنَّةِ فِي حَقِّنَا شَرَعَ فِي تَقْسِيمِهَا فِي حَقِّهِ.
And when the author finished the division of bayan, he began the explanation of the Sunnah al-Fi'liyyah, following the example of the Imam of Islam, although it would have been appropriate to mention it after the Sunnah al-Qawliyyah consecutively, as the author of al-Tawdih did. He said: A section: The actions of the Prophet, aside from slips, are of four types: mubah, mustahabb, wajib, and fard — those which are followed. And it (the slip) is a name for a forbidden act that occurs due to the intention of a permissible act, so his intention was not for the forbidden initially, nor does he persist in it after occurrence. Like one who bends in the road and falls from it, then gets up immediately: he did not intend the forbidden, nor did he persist in it. Similarly, it was from the intention of Musa, peace be upon him, through striking to discipline the Copt, and he killed him; the killing was not his intention, nor did he remain upon it, rather he regretted and said: 'This is from the work of Satan.' But this division is relative to us; otherwise, with respect to him (the Prophet), nothing was wajib in the technical sense, because it (technical wajib) is established by a proof containing doubt, whereas his proofs were all definitive with respect to him. Then they differed regarding following actions that did not occur from him inadvertently and were not natural actions specific to him. Some said: It is obligatory to refrain until it becomes manifest on which basis the Prophet, peace be upon him, did it — from ibaha, nadb, or wujoob. Some said: It is obligatory to follow him unless a proof of prohibition stands. And al-Karkhi said: He should hold the belief of ibaha in it until it becomes clear; if in the proof indicates wujoob or nadb. And when the author finished, etc. In Urdu: When the author finished the division of bayan, he began the explanation of the Sunnah al-Fi'liyyah... (continues) The author left all of this and explained what is the chosen view in his opinion. He said: The correct view with us is that whatever we know of his actions, peace be upon him, occurring on a basis of wujoob, nadb, or ibaha, we follow him in performing it on that basis unless a proof of specificity arises. So what was wajib upon him is wajib upon us, what was mandub upon him is mandub upon us, and what was mubah for him is mubah for us. And what we do not know on which basis he did it, we say he did it upon the lowest level of his actions, which is ibaha, because he never did a forbidden or disliked act at all, so necessarily it must be mubah. And when he finished the division of the Sunnah with respect to us, he began its division with respect to him.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a definition and rule concerning the types of actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and how the Ummah should follow them. The author first defines four categories: mubah (permissible), mustahabb (recommended), wajib (obligatory), and fard (necessary). Slips (zallah) are excluded because they are not exemplary. A slip is defined as an unintended haram act resulting from intending a mubah act, without persistence. Examples given: a person who bends to pick something and accidentally falls; Musa (AS) striking the Copt to discipline but causing death — he regretted it. This division is only for us, because for the Prophet himself, all his actions are based on definitive proofs, unlike technical 'wajib' which relies on doubtful proof. Then a dispute is mentioned: if we do not know the basis of a Prophetic action (whether it was mubah, nadb, or wujoob), scholars differed: (1) some say we must stop until we discover the basis; (2) some say we must follow unless evidence prevents; (3) Imam al-Karkhi said to assume ibaha (since certainty is absent). The author then gives the preferred view (al-mukhtar): if we know the basis, we follow accordingly; if we do not know, we assume the lowest level, which is ibaha, because the Prophet never committed a haram or makruh act. This ruling is specific to actions not done inadvertently, not natural actions, and not specific to him. The author then transitions to discussing the division of the Sunnah with respect to the Prophet himself.

Key Terms
زلَّة (zallah): A slip: an unintentional forbidden act resulting from a permissible intention, not persisted in.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the Prophet's actions in worship and practice.
مباح (mubah): Permissible: an action that is legally allowed without reward or punishment.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended: an action that is encouraged, rewarded but not obligatory.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory: an action required by a proof that is not absolutely certain (zanni).
فرض (fard): Necessary: an action required by a definitive proof (qat'i).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mukhtar view in this passage, if we do not know the basis on which the Prophet performed an action (e.g., whether it was wajib, mustahabb, or mubah), what do we assume?
A) We must stop and not act until we find out
B) We assume it is wajib until proven otherwise
C) We assume it is mubah (permissible)
D) We assume it is mustahabb (recommended)

Key Takeaway
Prophetic actions are of four types; follow them according to their known basis, and when the basis is unknown, assume ibaha because the Prophet never did haram or makruh.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
10 min
Classification of Wahi and Ijtihad as Hidden Revelation
Hanafi classification of wahi and defense of prophetic ijtihad as batin wahi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the types of wahi according to Hanafi usul and evaluate the Hanafi argument that the Prophet's ijtihad is a form of hidden revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's ijtihad is hidden revelation, divinely guided and infallible.

This lesson explores the Hanafi classification of revelation into apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). You will learn how the Prophet's ijtihad is considered a protected form of hidden revelation, and how the school responds to objections based on Quran 53:3-4. Understanding this doctrine is essential for grasping the authority of the Prophet's personal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish zahir and batin wahi
Identify the two main categories. Zahir is perceived by the senses (angelic speech, indication, inspiration). Batin is attained through ijtihad and reflection.
2
List the three subtypes of zahir wahi
Name them: (1) Quran via Jibril, (2) angelic indication without words, (3) ilham directly into the heart. Note that some subtypes (hatif, dreams) were omitted as they did not establish legal rulings.
3
Explain the Hanafi claim about ijtihad as batin wahi
The Prophet's ijtihad is guided by divine approval; he never settles on error. It is considered wahi batin because it is based on reflection and divine decision.
4
Analyze the opposing argument from Quran 53:3-4
Opponents argue that all the Prophet's speech is wahi, so ijtihad cannot be a separate source. The Hanafi response: the verse refers specifically to the Quran, not all speech. Even if general, the Prophet's ijtihad is still wahi batin.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafis accept the Prophet's ijtihad as authoritative and protected; others may reject it as a source of law. This affects the weight given to the Prophet's actions based on his own reasoning.

وَفِي بَيَانِ طَرِيقَتِهِ فِى إظهارِ أَحْكَام الشرع بِالْوَحْيِ فَقَالَ وَالْوَحِي نَوْعَانِ ظَاهِرٌ وَبَاطِن فَا الظَّاهِرُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَنْوَاعِ الأَوَّلُ مَا ثَبَتَ بِلِسَانِ الْمَلَكِ وَهُوَ جِبْرَئِيلُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلاَمُ بِأنَّه جِبْرَئِيلَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ بِآيَةٍ قَاطِعَةٍ تُنَافِى الشك وَالاسْتِبَاهَ فِي أنَّه جبرئيل أو لأَ هو الَّذِي أَنْزَلَ عَلَيْهِ لِسَانُ الرُّوح الْأَمِينِ يَعْنِي الْقُرْآنَ الَّذِي قَالَ الله تَعَالى في حقه قُلْ نَزَّلَهُ رُوحُ القُدْسِ مِنْ رَبِّكَ بِالْحَق وَالثاني مَا بَيْنَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ أو ثبت عِنْدَهُ صلى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسلم بإشارَةِ المَلَكِ مِنْ غَيْرِ بَيَانِ بِالْكَلام كَما قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السلام إِنْ رُوحَ الْقُدْسِ نَفَثَ فِي رَوْعِي أَنْ نَفْسًا لَنْ تَمُوْتَ حَتَّى تَسْتَكْمِلُ رِزْقَهَا. مگر مصنف نے اس پوری تفصیل کو ترک کر دیا ہے اور صرف وہ بیان کیا ہے جو ان کا پسندیدہ اور ترجمہ و تشریح مختار قول ہے لہذا فرمايا و الصحيح عندنا ان ما علینا۔ ہمارے نزدیک تی یہ ہے کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے افعال میں سے جن کے بارے میں معلوم ہو کہ آپ نے بحیثیت وجوب ندب یا اباحت کیا ہے ان کو اسی حیثیت سے عمل میں لانے کے لئے آپ کی اقتداء کریں گے یہاں تک کہ کوئی دلیل مخصوص قائم ہو جائے (یعنی یہ کہ یہ فعل آپ کے ساتھ خاص ہے لہذا جو فعل آپ پر واجب ہے وہ ہم پر واجب ہوگا اور جو آپ کے لئے مندوب تھا وہ ہم پر مندوب ( مستحب ) ہو گا اور جو فصل آپ کے لئے مباح تھا وہ ہمارے لئے مباح ہوگا سو مالم يعلم على اى جهة فعلہ اور جن افعال کے بارے میں ہم کو معلوم نہیں کہ آپ نے کس حیثیت سے کیا ہے ان کے بارے میں کہیں گے کہ وہ جو از فصل کے ادنی مرتبہ میں ہیں یعنی اباحت کے درجہ میں کیونکہ یہ تو یقین ہے کہ انہوں نے کوئی حرام یا مکروہ فعل نہیں کیا ہے لہذ ا ضروری ہے کہ وہ فعل مباح ہو۔ اور مصنف جب ہمارے حق میں سنت کی تقسیم کے بیان سے فارغ ہوئے تو سنت کی تقسیم خود رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے حق میں شروع کر رہے ہیں یعنی وہ اقسام جتلانے والے ہیں جو آپ کی طرف نسبت کرنے سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں یعنی وحی کے ذریعہ احکام شرع کے اظہار میں آپ کے طریقے کیا کیا تھے یہاں پر ان کی تفصیل بیان کریں گے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا۔ الوحی نوعان الخ وحی دو طرح کی ہے ظاہر و باطن پس ظاہر کی تین قسمیں ہیں الاول ما ثبت بلستان الملك (1) اول دو و می جو فرشتے کے ذریعہ پہونچے اور وہ حضرت جبرئیل علیہ السلام و الموقع في سمه یعنی حضرت جبرئیل علیہ السلام کے ذریعہ آپ کے کان میں پہونچے اور آپ پہنچانے والے کو جانتے ہوں یعنی جناب نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے منا اس کے بعد آپ کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ یہ حضرت جبرئیل علیہ السلام میں ایسی دلیل قطعی جو شیک اور شبہ کی نفی کرتی ہے یعنی آپ کو تفتی دلیل سے معلوم ہو کہ یہ حضرت جبرئیل ہیں اور کوئی شک وشبہ باقی نہ رہ ہے۔ اشرف الانوار شرح اردو نور الانوار جلد موم وهُوَ الَّذِئ أَنْزلَ عَلَيْهِ بِلِسَانِ الرُّوح الامین اس سے دور کی مراد ہے جو آپ پر حضرت روح الامین علیہ السلام کی زبانی نازل کی گئی یعنی قرآن مجید جس کے بارے میں اللہ تعالی نے ارشاد فرمایا قل نزلة رُوحُ الْقُدْسِ مِن رَّبِّكَ بالحق ( آپ کہہ دیجئے کہ اس کو اتارا ہے پاک فرشتہ جبرئیل امنی نے آپ کی رس کی طرف سے بلا شبہ ) اور دوسرے وہ ہے جس کو اپنے اس قول سے بیان کیا ہے۔ اوثبت عندہ مصلی الله عليه وسلم باشارة الملك البح ) و روحی ہے جو آپ کے پاس زبانی کلام کے بغیر بذریعہ اشارہ فرشتہ ہونے جیسے کہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ بیشک روح القدس نے میرے قلب میں القاء فرمایا ہے کہ کوئی نفس ہر گز نہیں مریگا حتی کہ اپنار رقی پورا کرے۔ والثالث مَا بَيْنَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ أَوْ تَبدى لِقَلبِه بِلاشتبةِ بِالْمَام مِنَ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِأَنْ أَرَاهُ ينوْرٍ مِنْ عِنْدِهِ وَهذا هو المسمى بِالْإِنْمَام وَيَسْتَرِكَ فِيْهِ الْأَوْلِيَاءُ أَيْضاً وَإِن كَانَ اليامهم يحتمل الخطاة والصواب والهامة لاتحتمل إِلا الصَّوَابَ وَلَمْ يَذْكُرُ ما كَانَ بِالهاتف لأنه لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي شَانِهِ لَمْ تَثْبت بِهِ أَحْكَامُ الشَّرْعِ وَكَذَا لَمْ يَذْكُرْ مَا كَانَ فِي الْمَنَامِ لأَنَّهُ كَانَ فِي ابْتِدَاءِ النُّبُوَّةِ لَمْ تَثْبُتْ بِهِ أَحْكَامُ الشَّرْعِ وَالْبَاطِنُ مَا يَنَالُ بِالاجْتِمَادِ بِالثاملِ فِي الْأَحْكامِ الْمَنْصُوْصَةِ بِأَنْ يَسْتَنْبِطُ عِلْةٌ فِي الْحُكْمِ الْمَنْصَوْصِ وَيَقِيْسُ عَلَيْهِ مَالَمْ يَعْلَمْ حَالَة بالتمن كَمَا كَانَ شَـَانُ. سَائِرِ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فَابَى بَعْضُهُمْ أَنْ يَكُونَ هَذَا مِنْ حَظِّهِ لأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى قَالَ وَمَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْيٌ يُوحَى فَكُلُّ مَا تَكَلَّمَهُ لَأَبْدَ أَنْ يَكُونَ ثَابِتا بِالْوَحَى وَالاجْتِمَادِ لَيْسَ كَذالِكَ فَلا يَكُونُ هَذَا شَانُهُ وَالْجَوابُ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِهَذَا الْوَحْيِ هُوَ الْقُرْآنُ دُوْنَ كُلُّ مَا تَكَلَّمَ به وَلَئِنْ سُلْمَ أَنَّهُ عَامَ فَلَا تُسَلْمُ أَنْ بِهِ اجْتَمَادَهُ لَيْسَ بِوَحْيِ بَلْ هُوَ وَحْى بَاطِنٌ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْمَالِ وَالْقَرَارِ عَلَيْهِ وَعِنْدَنَا هُوَ مَامُورُ بِانْتِظارِ الْوَحْى فيما لَمْ يُرْحَ إِلَيْهِ أَنْ إِذَا نَزَلَتِ الْحَادِثَةُ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَنْتَظِرَ الْوَحْى اَوْلاً لِجَوابِهَا إِلى ثَلُثَةِ أَيَّامٍ أَوْ إِلَى أَنْ يَخَافَ تَوْتَ الْغَرَضَ ثُمَّ الْعَمَلُ بالرائِي بَعْدَ انْقِضَاعِ مُدَّةِ الاِنْتِظَارِ فَإِنْ كَانَ أَصَابَ فِي الرَائِي لَمْ يَنْزِلِ الْوَحْى عَلَيْهِ فِي تِلْكَ الحادثة وَإِنْ كَانَ أَخْطَاءَ فِي الرَّائِي يَنْزِلُ الْوَحْنُ لِتَنْبِيْهِ عَلَى الْخَطَّاءِ وَمَا تَقَرْرَ عَلَى الْخَطَاءِ قَطَ بِخَلافِ سَائِرِ الْمُجْتَدِينَ فَإِنَّهُمْ إِنْ أَخْطَاءُ وَيَبْقَى خَطَاؤُهُمْ إِلى يَوْمِ القَيمة .
And in explaining his method in manifesting the rulings of the Shariah through revelation, he said: Revelation is of two types: apparent and hidden. The apparent is of three types: First, what is established by the tongue of the angel, and he is Jibril, peace be upon him, with a decisive sign that negates doubt and uncertainty about him being Jibril or not. He is the one who sent down upon him the tongue of the Trustworthy Spirit, meaning the Quran, about which Allah said: 'Say, the Holy Spirit has brought it down from your Lord with truth.' Second, what he explained by his statement: 'Or it is established with him, peace be upon him, by the indication of the angel without verbal explanation,' as he said: 'Indeed the Holy Spirit breathed into my heart that no soul will die until it completes its provision.' But the author left out this entire detail and only mentioned what he preferred, so he said: 'The correct view with us is that we follow his actions according to the known legal category.' [Urdu commentary follows]. The third type is what he explained by his statement: 'Or it appears to his heart without doubt from Allah by showing him a light from Him.' This is called 'ilham' (inspiration), and the saints also share in it, although their inspiration may contain error and correctness, while his does not contain except correctness. He did not mention what comes through a 'hatif' (unseen voice) because it was not his way and no rulings of Shariah were established by it. Likewise, he did not mention what comes in dreams because it was at the beginning of prophethood and no rulings were established by it. The hidden type is what is attained through ijtihad by reflection on the prescribed rulings, by deriving an illah (ratio legis) from the prescribed ruling and analogizing to that which he does not know its ruling, as is the way of other mujtahids. Some denied that this is his [the Prophet's] lot, because Allah said: 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only revelation revealed.' So everything he says must be established by revelation, and ijtihad is not like that, so this is not his way. The answer is that what is meant by 'this revelation' is the Quran, not everything he spoke. And if it is conceded that it is general, it is not conceded that his ijtihad is not revelation; rather, it is hidden revelation in consideration of reflection and decision upon it. According to us, he is commanded to await revelation in what is not revealed to him, such that when an incident occurs before him, he must wait for revelation first for its answer up to three days or until he fears the purpose will be lost, then he acts on his opinion after the waiting period ends. If he was correct in his opinion, revelation does not come down to him concerning that incident, and if he was mistaken in his opinion, revelation comes down to alert him to the error, and he never settled on error, unlike other mujtahids, for if they err, their error remains until the Day of Judgment.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the types of revelation (wahi) received by the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the nature of his ijtihad. The author begins by stating that wahi is of two kinds: apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). The apparent is further divided into three: (1) direct verbal revelation through the angel Jibril, which includes the Quran; (2) revelation by angelic indication without words, such as the hadith about the Holy Spirit inspiring the heart; (3) ilham, which is direct inspiration into the heart without angelic mediation, like seeing a light from Allah. The author notes that the Prophet's ijtihad is considered a form of hidden revelation because it is guided by divine approval. An objection is raised: if the Prophet does not speak from desire, then his ijtihad must also be revelation. The response clarifies that the verse refers specifically to the Quran, not to all his statements. Moreover, the Prophet was commanded to wait for revelation before giving his opinion; if his opinion was correct, no revelation came, but if mistaken, revelation corrected him. Thus, his ijtihad never settled on error, unlike other mujtahids. This establishes that the Prophet's ijtihad is protected and is a form of hidden revelation.

Key Terms
الوحي الظاهر (al-wahy al-zahir): Apparent revelation that is perceived by the senses, such as through the angel Jibril.
الوحي الباطن (al-wahy al-batin): Hidden revelation attained through ijtihad and reflection, protected from error.
الإلهام (al-ilham): Inspiration into the heart, a type of hidden revelation that saints may also receive, but their ilham can err while the Prophet's does not.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Deriving rulings by reflection and analogy from prescribed texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, how is the Prophet's ijtihad regarded?
A) It is not a source of law because it is not revelation.
B) It is a form of hidden revelation that is protected from error.
C) It is allowed but may contain errors like other mujtahids.
D) It is only valid if confirmed by a separate revelation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds that the Prophet's ijtihad is a divinely guided form of hidden revelation, ensuring the authority of his practices beyond direct verbal revelation.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
12 min
Shara'i' Man Qablana: Laws of Predecessors
Usul dispute with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the binding nature of previous laws and apply the criterion of narration without rejection to distinguish binding from non-binding precedents.

Core Idea
Previous laws bind us only if Allah or His Messenger narrate them without condemnation.

After covering types of Sunna, the author addresses whether the laws of earlier prophets are binding on Muslims. Scholars disagree: some say absolutely binding, others never. The Hanafi middle path, presented here, holds that only those laws preserved in the Quran or Sunna without rejection are binding, while others are unreliable due to distortion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
Read the passage to find the two extreme positions on the binding nature of previous laws. Note that some scholars say they are absolutely binding, while others say they are never binding.
2
State the Hanafi mukhtar view
The preferred view is the middle path: laws are binding only when narrated by Allah or His Messenger without rejection (inkar). Understand that this view avoids both absolutism and outright rejection.
3
Understand the criterion
The key condition is that the law is narrated in the Quran or authentic Sunna without any condemnation. If there is inkar (rejection or condemnation) in the narration, the law is not binding and may be forbidden.
4
Examine the examples
The author provides three examples of binding laws (qisas, division of water, prohibition of sodomy) and one example of a rejected narration (the wrongdoing of Jews). For each, verify that it meets the criterion.
Examples are from Quran 5:45, 54:28, 7:81, and 4:160.
5
Recognize the epistemological basis
The reason for not relying on unconfirmed previous laws is the distortion (tahrif) of earlier scriptures. Without Quranic or prophetic confirmation, we cannot be certain of their divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم شرع في بحث شرائع من قبلنا ۔ شرائع سابقہ کا حکم سنت کے اقسام کے بیان سے فارغ ہو کر مصنف نے شرائع سابقہ کا بیان شروع کیا ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ سنت کے ساتھ ملحق ہیں (یعنی مصنف سنت کے بیان کے بعد شرائع سابقہ کا حکم بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں اس لئے کہ شرائع سابقہ کو سنت رسول کے ساتھ قریبی مناسبت ہے۔ اس میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے بعض علماء نے کہا کہ شرائع من قبلنا ہمارے اوپر مطلقاً واجب اور لازم ہیں اور بعض نے کہا ہم پر قطعا لازم نہیں ہیں۔ اور مختار اور پسندیدہ قول وہ ہے جس کو مصنف نے اپنے قول میں بیان کیا ہے کہ شرائع من قبلنا تلزمنا اذا نص الله ورسوله عن غیر انکار اور سابقہ شریعتوں کے احکام پر عمل کر یا اس وقت ہم ضروری ہے جبکہ اللہ تعالی اور اس کے رسول ان احکامات کو بغیر نکیر کے بطور حکایت بیان فرمائیں کیونکہ جب اللہ تعالی ہم کو نہ جائیں بلکہ وہ فقط تو رات یا انجیل میں پایا جائے تو ہمارے اوپر اس کا عمل کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کے ماننے والوں نے تورات وانجیل میں بہت زیادہ تحریف کر رکھی ہے اور اپنی نفسانی خواہشات کے مطابق بہت سے احکام اس میں داخل کر دیئے ہیں پس یہ یقینی نہیں رہا کہ حکم منزل من اللہ ہے۔ ایسے ہی جب کوئی واقعہ اللہ تعالی ہمارے لئے بیان فرمائیں پس اس واقعہ کو نقل کر کے اس کی ہمارے لئے صراحہ تکبیر فرمادیں کہ اس طرح تم لوگ مت کرنا یا اشارہ یہ چیز ظاہر ہو جائے کہ ان کے ظلم کی سزا کے طور پر ہوا تھا تو ہمارے لئے وہ عمل حرام ہو گا۔ وَهَذَا أَصل كَبِيرُ لأبِي حَنِيفَةَ يَتَفَرْعُ عَلَيْهِ أَكْثَرُ الْأَحْكَامِ الْفِقْسِيَةِ فَمِثَالُ مَالَمْ يُذْكَرَ عَلَيْنَا بَعْدَ نَقْل الْقِصَّةِ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى وَكَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهَا أَى عَلَى الْيَهُودِ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ أَنْ النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالْعَيْن بِالْعَيْنِ وَالْاَنْفَ بِالْآنَفِ وَاالأذن بالأذن والسن بالسن وَالْجُرُوحَ قِصَاصَ فَهَذَا كُلُّه بَاقٍ عَلَيْنَا وَهَكَذَا قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى ونَبْتُهُمْ أَنَّ الْمَاءَ قِسْمَةٌ بَيْنَهُمْ أَيْ بَيْنَ نَاقَةٍ صَالِحٍ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ وَقَوْمِهِ يُسْتَدَلُ به عَلَى آنَ الْقِسْمَةَ بِطَرِيقِ الْمَهَايَاهُ جَائَرَةٌ وَهَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى أَئِنَّكُمْ لَتَاتُونَ الرجال بشهْوَةٍ مِنْ دُونِ النِّسَاءِ فِي حَقٍّ قَوْمٍ لُوطٍ يَدلُ عَلَى حُرْمَةِ المُوَاطَةَ علَيْنَا وَمِثالُ مَا أَنْكَرَهُ عَلَيْنَا بَعْدَ الْقِصَّةِ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى بِظُلْمَ مِنَ الَّذِينَ هَادُوا
Then he began the discussion of the laws of those before us. The ruling of previous laws: after finishing the explanation of the types of Sunna, the author begins the statement of the previous laws in the sense that they are annexed to Sunna (i.e., the author wants to express the ruling of previous laws after the discussion of Sunna because previous laws have close connection to the Sunna of the Messenger). There is ikhtilaf among scholars: some say that the laws of those before us are absolutely binding upon us, and some say they are not at all binding. The chosen and preferred opinion is the one that the author stated in his statement: 'The laws of those before us are binding upon us if Allah and His Messenger narrate them without rejection.' Acting upon the rulings of previous laws is necessary for us only when Allah and His Messenger narrate those rulings as a story without rejection. Because when Allah does not narrate them to us, but they are only found in the Torah or Injil, then it is not obligatory upon us to act upon them, because their followers have greatly distorted the Torah and Injil and inserted many rulings according to their own desires, so it is no longer certain that the ruling is from Allah. Similarly, when Allah narrates a story to us, then after narrating it, He explicitly prohibits us from doing the like, or it is indicated that it happened as a punishment for their injustice, then that act becomes forbidden for us. And this is a great principle for Abu Hanifa upon which most of the fiqhi rulings are derived. For example, what is not mentioned to us after the narration of the story: His statement 'And We prescribed for them therein (i.e., for the Jews in the Torah) that the soul for the soul, the eye for the eye, the nose for the nose, the ear for the ear, the tooth for the tooth, and for wounds is qisas' – all this is remaining upon us. Similarly, His statement 'And tell them that the water is divided between them' (i.e., between the she-camel of Salih and his people) is used as evidence that division by way of alternate use (muhaya'ah) is permissible. Similarly, His statement 'Do you approach men with desire instead of women?' regarding the people of Lot indicates the prohibition of sodomy upon us. And an example of what He rejected after the story: His statement 'Because of the wrongdoings of those who were Jews.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the binding nature of the laws of predecessors (shara'i' man qablana). The author, after completing the types of Sunna, addresses whether previous divine laws (e.g., those in the Torah and Injil) are binding on the Muslim community. He presents the ikhtilaf: some scholars hold they are absolutely binding; others say they are never binding. The preferred (mukhtar) position is that they are binding only when Allah and His Messenger narrate them in the Quran or authentic Sunna without any rejection or condemnation. If they are only found in the original scriptures without Quranic corroboration, they are not binding because those scriptures have been distorted. Additionally, if the narration includes an explicit prohibition or indicates that the act was a punishment, then it is forbidden for us. This is a major principle of Imam Abu Hanifa, and many fiqhi rulings derive from it. Examples provided: the law of qisas (retaliation) prescribed in the Torah is confirmed in the Quran (5:45) and thus remains binding; the story of Prophet Salih's she-camel and the division of water is cited to prove the permissibility of muhaya'ah (alternate use of shared water); the story of Lot's people establishes the prohibition of sodomy. Conversely, where Allah condemns an action (e.g., the wrongdoing of Jews), it indicates the act is forbidden.

Key Terms
شرائع من قبلنا (shara'i' man qablana): The laws and rulings revealed to prophets before Prophet Muhammad, such as those in the Torah and Injil.
انكار (inkar): Rejection or condemnation by Allah or His Messenger in the narration of a previous law.
تحریف (tahrif): Distortion of the scriptures by previous communities, making them unreliable as a source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, when are the laws of predecessors binding upon Muslims?
A) Always, because all previous revelations are from Allah.
B) Never, because Islam abrogates all previous laws.
C) Only when narrated in the Quran or authentic Sunna without rejection or condemnation.
D) Only if they are found in the Torah and Injil exactly as revealed.

Key Takeaway
The binding nature of previous laws depends on their confirmation in the Quran or authentic Sunna without any rejection or condemnation.
